# GHJig-Claude вҖ” Design Specification

> Written to be self-contained: with this document alone, the shell can be built from an empty directory.

## Reading this document

This file is the SSOT and is large (2,502 lines / ~90K tokens for a full read). Subagents and the main assistant should consult the **Table of contents** below, then use a targeted `Read --offset <line> --limit <range>` against the specific section, rather than loading the whole document for routine lookups. Full reads are appropriate when authoring a cross-cutting change.

The TOC is auto-generated by `scripts/build_toc.sh` between machine-readable START/END markers below. After editing a heading (adding, renaming, moving), rerun `scripts/build_toc.sh` to refresh. CI / smoke `В§28` runs `scripts/build_toc.sh --check` and fails if the TOC is out of sync.

---

## 0. Intent and scope

### 0.1 What this is

An operating shell for Claude Code that runs on top of the standard GitHub workflow. Target repos are cloned into the shell's `workspace/` directory and worked on from there.

The shell covers two layers of the same workflow:

- **Engineering execution** вҖ” issue вҶ’ branch вҶ’ draft PR вҶ’ checklist commits вҶ’ ready PR вҶ’ merge. Per the GitHub-standard flow.
- **Setting direction** вҖ” `MISSION.md` вҶ’ Directive Issue вҶ’ Execution Issue, where a Directive is a medium-term directional context that scopes several issues вҖ” a feature with subsystems, a refactor, a migration alike вҖ” without being directly executable.

Both layers use the same generate вҶ’ review вҶ’ mode-based-approval вҶ’ audit pattern (В§1.5). See В§1.7 for the eng-mode / dir-mode split, В§2.1 for the Directive lifecycle, В§4.9 for the dir-mode reviewer.

The shell guarantees:

1. **Adherence to the GitHub-standard flow** вҖ” issue вҶ’ branch вҶ’ draft PR вҶ’ checklist commits вҶ’ ready PR вҶ’ merge.
2. **Doc вҶ’ Test вҶ’ Code work order** вҖ” every code change goes through docs first, then tests, then implementation.
3. **Active SSOT maintenance** вҖ” documents are updated alongside code. Code-only changes with stale docs are prevented.
4. **Aggressive use of subagents** вҖ” output quality doesn't rely on a single model and single context. Specialized per-phase agents are composed.
5. **Hook enforcement of engineering discipline** вҖ” direct commits to protected branches, force pushes, secret exposure, malformed commits, untested merges, etc. are actually blocked.
6. **Type-aware separation of dir-mode and eng-mode artifacts** вҖ” Directives and Execution Issues share storage but follow distinct workflows; hooks, commands, and listings discriminate by the `Item Type` custom field (В§1.7).

### 0.2 What this is not

- Not a general dotfiles framework. The shell is scoped to `workspace/`.
- Not an absolute enforcer. No policy is set in stone. A conscious escape hatch is always open, and every bypass is recorded in the audit log.
- Doesn't own the target repo's knowledge SSOT. Updates are made by people / Claude inside the target.

### 0.3 Assumptions

- GitHub-standard, but **upstream-only**. Not a fork workflow. All branches are created on upstream; PRs go branch вҶ’ main within the same repo.
- Hosted in a git repo, shareable across a team/org. Changes ship via PR.

### 0.4 Deferred capabilities

The following directional-layer capabilities are deferred вҖ” listed so current design choices preserve the option to add them later, not because they are scheduled work. Operating experience motivates each addition; see MISSION's "Success looks like" вҶ’ orchestrator criterion for the framing.

- Orchestrator / automatic switching between eng-mode and dir-mode workflows.
- `/derive-next-directive`, `/reassess` commands. (`/block-directive` and `/revise-directive` were promoted from this list under Directive #75 вҖ” see В§5.16 and В§5.17.)
- Auto-confidence calculation for Directives.
- Auto-detection of Directive completion based on success-signal evaluation.
- Auto-revision of Directives based on engineering outcomes.
- Directive dependency graph or visualization.
- Multi-MISSION support (multiple canonical-direction docs per shell instance).
- External Director-tool integration interface (e.g., webhook receivers).
- Stop conditions / kill switches / budget controls (deferred with the orchestrator).
- `roadmap-reviewer` subagent (deferred until operating experience surfaces real friction).
- Session-level cleanup: a `SessionEnd` hook (where supported) and/or a user-invoked `/wrap` for branch tidy + temp-file cleanup (referenced from В§6.3; not yet specified or built).

---

## 1. Core principles

These principles must be visible throughout the shell. CLAUDE.md, agents, commands, and hook messages should all point to the same principles.

### 1.1 GH-standard is the backbone

The flow comes before the principles. Each principle is an attribute attached to some stage of the flow.

### 1.2 Doc вҶ’ Test вҶ’ Code order

A code change has three phases:

**Phase A вҖ” Doc**: write the behavior / contract / decision into the doc first. Whichever of the target SSOTs applies (MISSION, SPEC, README, CLAUDE.md, ARCHITECTURE, ADR, API doc) вҖ” for a contract/behaviour change the **SPEC** is the primary surface (В§1.3).

**Phase B вҖ” Test**: translate the doc from A into a test. The test must fail at this stage. Confirm the failure message is the intended picture.

**Phase C вҖ” Code**: minimal implementation to make B pass. Run adjacent regression checks afterward.

Each phase should be a separate commit when possible. The PR's commit graph should show the doc вҶ’ test вҶ’ code arc.

Effect of this order:
- Intent is externalized before code, enabling self-consistency checking.
- Tests stay closer to spec than when written alongside code.
- Re-entering the work later, you immediately know "which phase am I in?"

**Discard-boundary = Execution** (Directive #477). The Code phase is where the most working churn accrues вҖ” file reads, abandoned approaches, lint/smoke iterations вҖ” none of which is durable. The **discard boundary sits at the Execution unit**: that within-Execution churn can be discarded once the Code commit lands, while *directive-level* memory (the cross-Execution context a Directive carries) is preserved. The `implementer` subagent (В§4.12) + `/implement` (В§5.28) are the action-form of this вҖ” they run Phase C in an ephemeral context and return only the structured result (commit + plan-deviations + discoveries), so the churn never re-enters the main assistant's context. This is the **default Code-phase route** (Directive #477 signal-4: the formal A/B measurement was descoped and the context-narrowing hypothesis adopted as operating policy on circumstantial evidence вҖ” the convergent mainstream pattern + the native subagent context-discard), with a **documented opt-out** for trivial / one-line / glue edits and the orchestrator's own glue (Non-goal 2) that stay in the main loop, and **fail-open reversibility** (a missing implementer path degrades to main-loop authoring) as the safety valve; В§3.7 records the same boundary against the flush вҶ’ clear вҶ’ reconstruct loop.

**Exception categories** вҖ” the following types relax the phase order. Note the reason in one line in the PR Plan.

| Type | Relaxation | Rationale |
|------|-----------|-----------|
| `fix` | failing test reproducing вҶ’ code вҶ’ (if needed) doc | Bug reproduction plays the spec role |
| `refactor` | when external behavior is unchanged, doc can be skipped; existing tests suffice | New doc/tests would be fake commits |
| `perf` | measure вҶ’ code вҶ’ doc (report results) | Hypothesis validation comes first |
| spike | free on a separate branch, restructured into a proper PR before merge | Protect exploration cost |
| one-line typo / obvious fix | single commit, keep the phase prefix | Splitting cost > benefit |

`feat`, `docs`, and changes to external contracts / API / schema apply the phase order strictly.

### 1.3 Active SSOT maintenance

Two SSOTs coexist:

| Layer | Location | Question it answers |
|-------|----------|---------------------|
| Process SSOT | GHJig-Claude git | **How** we work |
| Project SSOT | each target repo git | **What** / **why** we're building |

Target SSOT structure:
- `MISSION.md` вҖ” the project's ground truth. Why it exists, success criteria, explicit non-goals.
- `SPEC.md` вҖ” the project's **behavioural contract / design spec**: what the system does and the contracts it upholds. The primary Doc-phase surface for any contract/API/schema/behaviour change.
- `README.md` вҖ” for external readers.
- `CLAUDE.md` вҖ” directory index, run commands, domain vocabulary, conventions.
- `docs/ARCHITECTURE.md` вҖ” module boundaries, data flow.
- `docs/ADRs/NNNN-*.md` вҖ” record of irreversible decisions.

**MISSION + SPEC are the frequently-consulted pair** вҖ” the *why/what* (MISSION) and the *contract* (SPEC), the half of the durable memory the shell selectively injects from on nearly every task. README / CLAUDE.md / ARCHITECTURE / ADRs are reference memory, consulted on demand. This mirrors how the shell dogfoods itself (its own `MISSION.md` + `SPEC.md`), now imposed on targets too.

**Requiredness keys on code, not on an external surface.** `MISSION.md` is always required вҖ” every project has a direction. `SPEC.md` is **required for any project that carries code**: SPEC is the *behavioural* SSOT (*what the system does* and the contracts it upholds, per the definition above), and any codebase has behaviour worth specifying вҖ” so requiredness keys on the presence of code, **not** on whether an *external* contract (CLI, API, schema, protocol) exists. (This re-bases an earlier framing that gated SPEC on an external contract; that framing under-counted internal-only systems вҖ” like this shell itself вҖ” whose behaviour is exactly what a SPEC records.) A brand-new project with no code yet legitimately has none, but the shell treats SPEC as expected from the first code. The onboard tier decides how the slot is surfaced (В§5.1): the shell scaffolds the SPEC slot from a lightweight template, it never authors the target's contract content (the MISSION boundary вҖ” the shell owns the *how*, not the *what/why*).

**SPEC navigation is single-file + line-indexed ToC.** A SPEC is one file with a machine-generated Table of contents between `<!-- TOC START -->` / `<!-- TOC END -->` markers (`scripts/build_toc.sh`), so readers consult the ToC then `Read --offset` the targeted section instead of loading the whole file. Two norms make this robust: (a) **ToC line numbers are a hint, the heading text is the truth** вҖ” if an offset lands on the wrong section (the SPEC was edited), re-Grep the heading rather than trust the number; (b) **regenerate the ToC in the same commit that edits a SPEC heading** (not deferred to `/ship`), so the index is never stale across the rest of the task. Single-file is chosen for **no-divergence** (one place a contract lives cannot contradict itself), not for speed; splitting a SPEC into a per-subsystem directory is a **scale escape hatch** for when a single file grows too large to full-read вҖ” each split file then being a single-file SSOT for its domain.

A code change commits together with the SSOT items it invalidates or updates. If a doc is intentionally omitted, the commit body states `Docs: n/a вҖ” <short reason>`.

### 1.4 PR-as-living-doc

The PR body simultaneously serves three roles:
- **The work item's ground truth** вҖ” what this PR is for.
- **Cross-session memory** вҖ” Claude's context is volatile but the PR body is durable. The next session auto-loads it to restore context.
- **Execution progress display** вҖ” the checklist renders as a GitHub progress bar.

Principles:
- The PR body is **editorial, not append-only**. Curate right after each commit. Tidy stale items; if history is needed, keep one line per entry in a separate "Changelog" section.
- **commit вҶ’ PR sync** order. Fact (commit) first, then reflection (PR body). Reversing it creates false states.
- Before updating, refetch the remote body once. If it differs from what the shell last saw вҖ” checked against the persistent cache at `.claude/state/pr-cache/<owner>__<repo>__pr-<n>.json` via `helpers/pr_cache.sh` (В§5.4) вҖ” abort the automatic update and inform the user. Don't build a merge logic beyond that вҖ” conflicts are rare, and a human should be in the loop when they happen.
- **No stale unchecked items at merge.** A merged PR body must reflect truth at the moment of merge. Every `- [ ]` line is in one of three terminal states: ticked (`[x]`) because it was done, marked `[~] N/A вҖ” <reason>` because it intentionally won't be done, or removed from the body. "Pending, but oh well" is not acceptable вҖ” closed/merged PRs are loaded by SessionStart (В§6.5) into future context, so stale uncheckedness propagates as misinformation. The same rule applies to **issue bodies on auto-close**: every acceptance-criterion item is ticked, N/A'd with reason, or struck through with a closing comment that names the disposition.

### 1.5 Aggressive use of subagents

Quality benefits from not loading every burden onto a single context.

| Situation | Subagent |
|-----------|---------|
| Wide read-only exploration | `explorer` |
| 3+ file changes, API/schema/migration | `planner` |
| Doc writing / updating | `doc-writer` |
| Test writing (Phase B) | `test-writer` |
| Pre-commit / pre-PR review | `code-reviewer` |
| Auth / input / deps / crypto changes | `security-reviewer` |
| Rationale check on a proposed issue body | `issue-reviewer` |
| Approach / contest judgment on a planner output | `plan-reviewer` |
| Adversarial plan challenge (Г—2, distinct axes) on a planner output | `plan-challenger` (В§4.8.1) |
| Quality check on a proposed Directive or completion claim | `activation-reviewer` (В§4.9) |

Independent investigations that can run in parallel: call multiple agents at once.

You don't need to call all ten on a single PR. Use them per the table; the main assistant shouldn't re-run in `explorer` what it already explored. No call-count limits or tracking.

**Working-tree isolation** (#285): the read-only-by-intent subagents вҖ” `code-reviewer`, `security-reviewer`, `issue-reviewer`, `plan-reviewer`, `plan-challenger`, `activation-reviewer`, `explorer` вҖ” share the parent session's working tree unless invoked with worktree isolation, and they carry `Bash`, so a tree-mutating git command inside one (`git checkout <base> -- <path>`, `restore`, `stash`, `reset`, `add`, `commit`) silently reverts or stages the parent's uncommitted work вҖ” observed once in the v0.3 run. Two layers prevent it: (a) **canonical** вҖ” invoke these subagents with **worktree isolation** so their git cannot touch the parent tree; and (b) **belt-and-suspenders** вҖ” each such agent's prompt constrains it to **read-only git only** (`git diff`/`show`/`log`/`status`; compare a base via `git diff <base>...HEAD` or `git show <ref>:<path>`, never `git checkout <base> -- <path>`). The structural backstop is that merges build from the *pushed commit*, not the working tree, so a post-commit reversion cannot ship; still, run `git status` before each commit/merge to catch a pre-commit reversion. The **write-capable `implementer`** (В§4.12) is deliberately **not** in this isolation list вҖ” its Code commit must land on the PR branch, which a separate worktree cannot check out вҖ” so it substitutes a **path-scoped-add discipline** (stage only the manifest-named paths; never `git add -A`/`-u`) for isolation, and the caller surfaces a dirty tree before dispatch (В§5.28). The inversion is intentional: the one write-capable agent is the highest-stakes case, so its discipline is tightened in place rather than weakened by the absence of isolation.

**Isolation checks out the base, not the PR head** (#544): worktree isolation gives the reviewer the **harness-chosen base** (`origin/main`), not the pushed PR head вҖ” so a post-push reviewer that reads the ambient tree reviews a stale artifact and can still APPROVE (PR #543). A reviewer therefore **pins its artifact to the PR head by construction** per В§4.5 (resolve via `gh pr view --json headRefOid` / `gh pr diff` / `git show <HEAD_SHA>:<path>`, no checkout), and the invoking skill blind-compares the reviewer's independently-reported `reviewed-head` to the true head (В§5.7): a reviewed-artifact вү  PR-head вҖ” or an absent/unconfirmed head вҖ” is a **fail-closed invalid vote**, never an approve.

**Operating-mode coupling**: `code-reviewer`, `security-reviewer`, `issue-reviewer`, `plan-reviewer`, and `activation-reviewer` all substitute for human review at different points in the flow. In `attended` mode they surface findings to the user, who decides; in `unattended` mode their verdict gates the next step directly (`ship` вҶ’ proceed; `refine` вҶ’ re-produce with feedback; `block` вҶ’ stop with the reason and either ask the user, or вҖ” when no human is available вҖ” park the work). (`activation-reviewer` uses the equivalent `pass` / `revise` / `reject` vocabulary, В§4.9.1.) This pattern is what makes the `unattended` mode operationally complete: every human-confirm checkpoint has a subagent fallback.

**Filer-aware invariants** (added by Directive #92 вҖ” Issue #95): a layer of protections **above** the attended/unattended axis, keyed on the Issue's `authorAssociation` per GitHub's role taxonomy (`OWNER` / `MEMBER` / `MAINTAINER` / `COLLABORATOR` вҶ’ trusted; everything else вҶ’ untrusted). Independent of operating mode вҖ” both attended and unattended honor the same filer-aware rules. Two protections enforced by the `trusted-filer-mutate` hook matcher (В§6.1):

- **AI never auto-closes-as-not-planned on a trusted-filer Issue.** Closing a trusted-filer Issue with `--reason completed` is allowed (evidence-backed); closing as `not planned` or `duplicate` requires human confirm. Untrusted-filer Issues continue to follow the regular attended/unattended close rules.
- **Removing the `directive` label declassifies a Directive вҖ” human confirm required always, regardless of filer trust tier.** The `directive` label is the type-awareness key (В§1.7, В§6.1 `proposed-protect`); silently dropping it would bypass dir-mode review for an Issue still positioned as a Directive.

Both invariants escape via `SKIP_HOOKS=trusted-filer-mutate SKIP_REASON='<why>'` (В§7). Helper `is_trusted_filer <issue#>` lives at `.claude/hooks/helpers/issue_filer.sh`; caches per-session under `.claude/state/issue-filer-cache/`. Bot-filed Issues (Dependabot, GitHub Actions) carry `authorAssociation="NONE"` and are currently treated as untrusted вҖ” documented limitation per the helper's notes (Directive #92 brief В§11).

### 1.6 GitHub standard (upstream-only)

- No forks. The clone's origin is always upstream.
- All branches are created on upstream.
- PRs are branch вҶ’ **base** within the same repo. **Default base is `main`**; `/work-on --base <branch>` (В§5.3) opts into an alternate base for experimental work or long-lived feature branches. See В§10.5 "Topic-branch workflow."
- Every change starts from an issue. issue вҶ’ PR is 1:N (intermediate PRs use `Refs #N`, final uses `Closes #N`). For PRs whose base is non-`main`, `Refs` is the right default вҖ” the issue closes only when work reaches `main`.
- Branch naming: `<gh-username>/<type>/[<issue#>-]<slug>`. The required-issue-# group (В§6.1.1) always includes `<issue#>-`; the optional group (`chore`/`style`/`build`/`ci`/`test`/`revert`) may omit it. Examples: `ilgyu/feat/42-oidc-login`, `ilgyu/chore/typo-readme`.

### 1.7 Artifact tiers and the subagent shape they share

The shell operates over two **artifact tiers** above the commit/PR layer: a Directive Issue (medium-term directional context) and an Execution Issue (a concrete unit of work). Both tiers follow the same workflow pattern from В§1.5 (generate вҶ’ review вҶ’ approval вҶ’ audit); they differ in which subagents author and which review at each step. The terms `eng-mode` and `dir-mode` name the workflow each tier exercises, but the substrate, hooks, audit log, mode toggle (В§5.7.1), and state directory are shared.

**Shared code, per-project state** (the MISSION-tier principle В§3.2.2 builds on, and the reason "the substrate вҖҰ are shared" above holds across projects): there is exactly **one** canonical code/SPEC/norms source, and every bound project resolves it **live** вҖ” a project binds to the canonical root (В§3.2.1) rather than copying it, so a friction-fix propagates to *all* bound projects and none is pinned to a stale version (MISSION В§ "The mechanism" вҶ’ "Isolation model"). What isolates per project is only **ephemeral state**: the audit log, caches, and scope **registry** under each project's `ghjig-state/` (В§3.2.2), plus the session and Claude Code's native per-project memory. Shared substrate = the durable memory selective injection draws from; per-project state = the narrowed surface. Code/version isolation (per-project pinning) is an explicit non-goal вҖ” it would break propagation.

| Tier (workflow name) | Artifact type | Generate-subagent(s) | Review-subagent | Approval rule |
|---------------------|---------------|----------------------|------------------|---------------|
| **Execution Issue** (eng-mode) | Execution Issue, PR, Commit | `planner`, `doc-writer`, `test-writer`, `explorer` | `code-reviewer`, `security-reviewer`, `issue-reviewer`, `plan-reviewer` | attended: human / unattended: reviewer verdict (В§1.5) |
| **Directive Issue** (dir-mode) | Directive Issue | `planner`, `doc-writer`, `explorer` | `activation-reviewer` (В§4.9) | attended: human / unattended: `activation-reviewer` verdict |

**Hierarchy of artifacts** that the two modes act on:

```
MISSION.md                 вҶҗ human-defined long-term anchor (doc-as-code)
  в”Ӯ            вҶ“
  в”Ӯ       Initiative        вҶҗ planning-tier strategic commitment, consumed from
  в”Ӯ          в”Ӯ                upstream вҖ” never authored by the shell (live; the
  в”Ӯ          в”Ӯ                tier the shell consumes вҖ” see below)
  в””в”Җв”ҖвҶ’ Directive Issue вҶҗв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ  directing context (parent: a MISSION section OR an
       в”Ӯ                         Initiative), revisable, medium-term (dir-mode)
       вҶ“
     Execution Issue        вҶҗ concrete unit of work (eng-mode)
       вҶ“
     Pull Request           вҶҗ implementation evidence (eng-mode)
       вҶ“
     Reflection             вҶҗ engineering result summary
```

Dir-mode operates on the Directive layer; eng-mode operates on Execution Issue and below. The Initiative tier above the Directive is consumed from upstream, never authored by the shell вҖ” see "Initiatives вҖ” the planning tier the shell consumes" below.

**Workflow selection is manual.** Users invoke `/file-directive`, `/activate`, `/complete-directive`, `/list-directives`, `/link-directive`, `/revise-directive`, `/block-directive`, `/consume-initiative`, `/initiative-feedback` (В§5.10вҖ“В§5.22) for directing work and `/file-issue`, `/work-on`, `/ship` for engineering work. (`/activate-directive` and `/triage` are deprecated aliases of `/activate`, retained one release cycle вҖ” В§5.12/В§5.18.) No orchestrator decides between them; an automatic selector is a future addition that operating experience may motivate (see MISSION's "Success looks like" вҶ’ orchestrator criterion).

**Strategic judgment remains external.** AI may generate, draft, propose, and review at any level. Activation, completion, and revision decisions pass through either a human (attended) or `activation-reviewer` (unattended) вҖ” the shell never autonomously decides direction.

**Canonical direction.** The repo's `MISSION.md` is the canonical long-term anchor. Directives reference its sections in their `## MISSION fit` field; `activation-reviewer` checks alignment with MISSION rather than a separate Goal artifact. MISSION.md as doc-as-code beats an Issue-or-Project Goal artifact because the latter creates two representations of the same canonical direction вҖ” revising one without the other surfaces drift.

**Substrate.** All dir-mode state lives on GitHub Issues. The rationale for Issues-as-SSOT over Project-fields-as-SSOT: Project access is owner-scoped while repo access is broader (storing state on Project fields gates writes by access the contributor may not have); dual-recording across labels, fields, and body invites silent sync drift; and Issues are the OSS-standard proposal channel that external contributors expect.

- **`directive`** label вҖ” marks an Issue as a Directive. The single Type-awareness key.
- **`initiative`** label (#249) вҖ” marks an Issue as an Initiative (the planning tier above a Directive, consumed from upstream вҖ” see "Initiatives вҖ” the planning tier the shell consumes" below). The single Type-awareness key for that tier, symmetric to and mutually exclusive with `directive`; resolved by the `is_initiative_issue` predicate (`helpers/issue_type.sh`).
- **`status:proposed`** label вҖ” Status=Proposed (filed but not yet activated).
- **`status:blocked`** label вҖ” Status=Blocked (active but cannot proceed without external input).
- Open + `directive` + no `status:*` label вҶ’ Status=**Active**.
- Closed + `directive` + state-reason=completed вҶ’ Status=**Completed**.
- **`P0`/`P1`/`P2`/`P3`** label вҖ” Priority.
- **`execution`** label (#186) вҖ” positive type label for an Execution Issue (a unit of work parented under a Directive). Makes Execution a first-class queryable type rather than label-absence; the `Parent Directive: #N` marker is then purely the parent pointer. Distinct from `task` (standalone, not parented) and `bug`.
- **Issue body** вҖ” Objective, Success signals, Non-goals, Constraints, MISSION fit (Confidence is documented in body, not a field).
- **Body line 1 `Parent Directive: #N`** вҖ” Parent reference for Execution Issues; consumed by `/reflect`, the dir-mode-post-merge workflow, AND the issues-to-project-mirror workflow.

The GitHub Project named `<repo-name> roadmap` (override via `$GHJIG_PROJECT_NAME`) is a **derived view**, not the SSOT. Setup script `scripts/setup_project.sh` ensures the four mirrored fields exist: `Item Type / Status / Priority / Parent` (SINGLE_SELECT for the first three, TEXT for the last; the discriminator field is named `Item Type` rather than `Type` because GitHub reserves `Type` as a built-in Projects-v2 field name вҖ” #342). `Iteration` is owner-managed via the GH UI; the mirror workflow does NOT mirror it (Iteration is owner-level cadence, not repo-level deliverable grouping вҖ” those concerns split between Project Iteration and GitHub Milestone). Confidence and Success Signals live in the Issue body, not Project fields. The Project Item is populated by `.github/workflows/issues-to-project-mirror.yml` on every `issues.{opened,edited,labeled,unlabeled,closed,reopened,milestoned,demilestoned}` event. Dir-mode commands write to Issues only; they never write to the Project (the mirror handles the derivation). The two-layer idempotency contract on `setup_project.sh` (field existence + SINGLE_SELECT option-set correctness, from issue #76) carries forward to the 4-state Status schema: missing declared options are added via `updateProjectV2Field` GraphQL mutation; user-added options outside the declared set are preserved.

**Filer-aware invariants** (В§1.5, cluster C / issue #95): the `trusted-filer-mutate` hook matcher protects trusted-filer (OWNER / MEMBER / MAINTAINER / COLLABORATOR per `authorAssociation`) Issues from AI auto-close-as-not-planned and protects the `directive` label from declassification on any filer. Mode-independent вҖ” applies in both `attended` and `unattended`.

**Audit-line format guard** (issue #87): `audit_log` in `.claude/hooks/hookrt.sh` enforces strict format on `directive-file/created` lines pre-write вҖ” malformed calls are rejected and written as `decision=format-error` warn lines instead. Smoke В§50a remains as defense-in-depth + historical-line grandfathering.

**Initiatives вҖ” the planning tier the shell consumes** *(fully live as of milestone `v2 consuming initiatives`: the **recognition layer** (the `initiative` label, the `is_initiative_issue` predicate, `Parent Initiative: #N` marker reading вҖ” #249, M1.1), the **enforcement layer** (label mutual-exclusivity, the Directive parent-XOR, Initiative read-only-except-comments вҖ” #251, M1.2), the **reviewer layer** (`activation-reviewer` parent-kind branching + the contract-evaluability and extraction-faithfulness checks вҖ” #254, M2), the **consumption** flow (`/consume-initiative` extraction вҖ” #257, M3), the **feedback** flow (`/initiative-feedback` structured challenge + completion вҖ” #260, M4), and the **derived-view** integration (the issues-to-project-mirror workflow populates an Initiative-parented Directive's Project `Parent` field вҖ” #262) are all live.)* An **Initiative** is a planning-tier strategic commitment sitting one tier above a Directive. It arrives from **outside the shell** as a GitHub Issue bearing the `initiative` label вҖ” the single Type-awareness key for the tier, symmetric to `directive` and mutually exclusive with it. The shell **consumes** Initiatives and never authors them; an Initiative is **read-only to the shell except for appended comments** (the shell never edits its body, labels, or state). Consequently an Initiative is **outside the 4-state Directive lifecycle and the `status:*` taxonomy entirely** (В§2.1): the shell never applies `status:proposed`/`status:blocked`/`status:*` to it, it is never "Activated" or "Completed" or "Blocked," and `/activate` refuses it (В§5.12). Its real progress lives upstream and surfaces only through `/initiative-feedback` (В§5.22); the Project mirror may render an open Initiative as `Active` purely as a derived-view artifact of the shared Status field (В§2.1), not a lifecycle claim. The origin of an Initiative (a person, a planning tool) is immaterial вҖ” the shell relies only on the contract below, not on how the Initiative was produced.

- **Parent generalization.** A Directive has exactly one parent, of one of two mutually-exclusive kinds: a **MISSION section** (named in the Directive's `## MISSION fit` body field per В§2.1 вҖ” the default) or an **Initiative** (a `Parent Initiative: #N` marker on body line 1, the same line-1 `<kind>: #N` *shape* as `Parent Directive: #N` вҖ” but **not** consumed by the same workflow set; see "Derived-view integration" below). The two parent kinds have **different shapes** вҖ” a body *field* naming a section vs. a line-1 *marker* вҖ” so the parent-XOR check (below) tests "a MISSION-fit field and no Initiative marker" XOR "an Initiative marker and no MISSION-fit field," not two parallel markers. An Initiative is introduced only when a strategic commitment genuinely bundles several Directives and is worth reviewing and evolving in its own right; the default stays MISSION-parented, so the tier does not become ceremony. This **generalizes** the hierarchy above rather than replacing it вҖ” every existing MISSION-parented Directive remains valid unchanged.
- **Derived-view integration.** The line-1 `Parent Initiative: #N` marker is consumed by **exactly one** of the three `Parent Directive` consumers (В§5.2): the **issues-to-project-mirror** workflow, which derives a Directive's Project `Parent` field from its own line-1 marker and recognizes **both** `Parent Directive: #N` and `Parent Initiative: #N` (#262) вҖ” so an Initiative-parented Directive's Project `Parent` points to its Initiative (the `Parent` field is free-text `#N`, so the referent's type is immaterial). It is **not** read by `/reflect` or the dir-mode-post-merge workflow: those consume the **closing Execution Issue's** `Parent Directive` marker to reflect onto a Directive, and an Execution Issue is structurally always Directive-parented (the parent-XOR + `label-parent-consistency` restrict `Parent Initiative` to Directives, and a Directive never branches nor closes via a PR `Closes`, so it never becomes a `closingIssuesReference` вҖ” В§6.1, В§10.5). A Directive's `Parent Initiative` marker therefore never reaches the reflection path; **DirectiveвҶ’Initiative upward feedback flows through `/initiative-feedback` (В§5.22)**, deliberately a structured comment channel, not auto-reflection. This is why "symmetric" above is scoped to marker *shape*, not consumption.
  - **Create-path split.** The two parent kinds are born from **different commands**: `/file-directive` (В§5.10) authors a `## MISSION fit` field only, so it produces **MISSION-parented** Directives exclusively; `/consume-initiative` (В§5.21) is the **sole** producer of `Parent Initiative`-marked Directives. There is deliberately no `/file-directive` path to an Initiative parent вҖ” a hand-added `Parent Initiative` marker on a `/file-directive` body would carry a MISSION-fit field too and trip the parent-XOR. To parent a Directive under an Initiative, consume the Initiative; do not hand-author the marker.
- **The contract (load-bearing).** An Initiative must carry a **termination condition evaluable without knowledge of the code.** The shell extracts Directives by working backward from it. A *complete* Directive needs code knowledge вҖ” its Success signals and Constraints reference code reality, which is why the shell, not the upstream, extracts Directives вҖ” but the Initiative's termination condition sits above code and so can and must be stated without it. A condition that cannot be (one that smuggles in execution detail) marks the Initiative under-specified; the shell surfaces that upstream rather than guessing. This is the planning/execution boundary: above the point where a termination condition can be set without the code is the upstream's job; below it is the shell's.
- **Feedback is upward and non-deciding.** The shell sends findings to the Initiative as comments, a structured **challenge** when execution reality contradicts the Initiative, and a **completion** signal when the extracted Directives land вҖ” carrying code-derived information the planning layer structurally cannot have (real dependencies, measurability, implementation cost). It never rejects, retires, or asserts completion of an Initiative: discarding or closing a strategic commitment is a strategic judgment that stays upstream. This mirrors the reviewer pattern вҖ” a `block`/challenge escalates rather than auto-discards (В§4.9.1, В§5.7.1).
- **Location.** An Initiative is a GitHub Issue **in the same target repo**, located by the `initiative` label. The mechanism of its arrival is out of scope; **cross-repo Initiatives are out of scope** (they would reintroduce the cross-repo-trust surface of В§6.1's `trusted-filer-mutate` close arm).
- **Mechanisms.** **Live (M1.1, #249):** the `is_initiative_issue` predicate (symmetric to `is_directive_issue`, `helpers/issue_type.sh`; cached, fail-open per В§6.1) and `Parent Initiative: #N` marker reading (the `issue_has_initiative_parent_marker` tri-state resolver, distinct from the `Parent Directive` resolver that backs `label-parent-consistency`). **Live (M1.2, #251):** three enforcement matchers вҖ” the `initiative`/`directive` label mutual-exclusivity and the Directive parent-XOR (exactly one parent kind present: a `## MISSION fit` field **or** a line-1 `Parent Initiative:` marker, never both and never neither (different shapes вҖ” see Parent generalization), enforced via `issue_has_mission_fit_field`/`issue_has_initiative_parent_marker`), both folded into the `label-parent-consistency` matcher on the `--add-label` path; and `initiative-readonly` (mutating `gh issue edit`/`close`/`reopen` on an `initiative` Issue blocked, `gh issue comment` allowed). All fail-open per В§6.1. **Live (M2, #254):** reviewer branching вҖ” `activation-reviewer` (В§4.9, extended in place rather than via a new subagent, per the В§4.9.3 caveat) recognizes the `initiative` label, branches a Directive's alignment check on its parent kind (MISSION section vs. parent Initiative's termination condition), and gains a contract-evaluability check (Initiative intake) + an extraction-faithfulness check (post-extraction), both invoked by the M3 consume flow. **Live (M3, #257):** the `/consume-initiative <N>` command (В§5.21) вҖ” the consume flow: contract gate (I1) вҶ’ working-backward extraction вҶ’ faithfulness gate (I2) вҶ’ file the extracted Directives as `status:proposed` `Parent Initiative`-parented proposals (never activated; the only Initiative write is a plain under-specification comment). **Live (M4, #260):** the `/initiative-feedback <N>` command (В§5.22) вҖ” the upward-feedback flow: a `## Initiative challenge` comment (code-derived contradiction вҶ’ request re-evaluation, escalate-not-reject) and a `## Initiative completion` comment (merged-Directive evidence вҶ’ request termination assessment, never assert-done/close); comments only, never mutating the Initiative. **Live (#262):** the **derived-view** integration вҖ” the issues-to-project-mirror workflow recognizes a Directive's line-1 `Parent Initiative: #N` marker and populates its Project `Parent` field (the one `Parent Directive` consumer that legitimately reads a Directive's own marker; `/reflect` + dir-mode-post-merge read the Execution child's marker and are correctly unchanged вҖ” see Derived-view integration). **The milestone-`v2` model is now fully live** вҖ” recognition + enforcement + reviewer + consume + feedback + derived-view.

**Out of scope** (Initiative tier): authoring Initiatives; knowing their origin; tracking a challenge's outcome once escalated; rejecting/retiring an Initiative from within the shell; nested Initiative tiers (the tier is flat above the Directive); automatic orchestration between planning-mode and execution-mode work; cross-repo Initiatives.

#### Substrate-in-target contract (Issue #114; Directive #107)

Dir-mode's substrate is installed into target repos under `workspace/` via the `/onboard-dir-mode` skill. The boundary broadening вҖ” shell now mutates target `.github/` files + labels in addition to its `.claude/` symlinks вҖ” is acceptable only because each install step is detectable, individually revertable, and additive (never replaces target-owned artifacts). The reversibility contract below makes adoption low-risk: a target can fully unwind the shell via one PR plus a few `gh` commands, with no load-bearing dependency on installed files.

**Three-tier feature model.** Targets adopt the shell at one of three tiers; each is a strict superset of the previous and tier transitions are mechanical:

- **Tier 1: eng-mode** вҖ” no substrate required. `/file-issue`, `/work-on`, `/ship`, secret scan, AC closeout, conventional-commit enforcement.
- **Tier 2: dir-mode-with-labels** вҖ” tier 1 + the 12-label dir-mode set (`directive`, `initiative`, `status:proposed`, `status:blocked`, `awaiting-author`, `execution`, `task`, `discussion`, `P0`, `P1`, `P2`, `P3`), installed via `scripts/ensure_v3_labels.sh` + inline `directive` and `initiative` creates. (Count note: these 12 enumerate the dir-mode lifecycle/priority/type labels; the tier-2 *installer* reports **15 total** because `ensure_v3_labels.sh` creates 13 labels вҖ” the 11 lifecycle/priority labels (incl. the release-backbone `skip-changelog` #133) plus the two initiative-feedback projection labels `initiative:challenged` / `initiative:completion-requested` (#359) вҖ” but not the two tier type-keys, and `onboard_target.sh` then adds `directive` and `initiative` (#249) inline вҖ” i.e. 13 ensure + 2 inline = 15, traceable to `onboard_target.sh`'s count message and smoke В§63g.) Unlocks `/file-directive`, `/activate`, `/complete-directive` writing to Issues directly. No Project mirror, no Issue templates. (`awaiting-author` вҖ” #172 вҖ” marks the handoff state after a `revise` or trusted-filer `reject`; it is an action-signal label without a `status:` prefix, orthogonal to the lifecycle stage. The former raw-filing triage label was retired by #179 вҖ” raw filings now receive `status:proposed`+`task` directly.)
- **Tier 3: full substrate** вҖ” tier 2 + `.github/ISSUE_TEMPLATE/*.yml` + `.github/workflows/{auto-status-proposed,auto-clear-awaiting-author,issues-to-project-mirror,dir-mode-post-merge,check-changelog,check-toc,initiative-feedback-label}.yml` (7 workflows, matching the canonical source `target-substrate/workflows/` and smoke В§63a; `initiative-feedback-label.yml` #359 projects `/initiative-feedback`'s `## Initiative challenge` / `## Initiative completion` comment markers into the `initiative:challenged` / `initiative:completion-requested` labels вҖ” applied by the target-repo CI Action on `issue_comment`, never by eng's runtime, preserving the `initiative-readonly` boundary) вҖ” plus the sourced helpers the workflows read after `actions/checkout` (`resolve_parent_directive.sh` #335, `detect_bare_refs_directive.sh` #337; В§5.15, В§10.5) and the SPEC ToC-freshness checker `build_toc.sh` that `check-toc.yml` runs (#347, В§1.3 вҖ” byte-identical to the canonical `scripts/build_toc.sh`, smoke-guarded), which ship alongside the workflows into the target вҖ” + GitHub Project (`<repo> roadmap`) with the dir-mode field schema. Unlocks the template chooser for external contributors and the Project-as-derived-view. **Blank issues are disabled** (`blank_issues_enabled: false`, #186) вҖ” every UI filing must use a typed template (directive/execution/task/bug/discussion), so it is always classified and (for the four work-types) `status:proposed`-gated; the `discussion` template (В§5.19) is the sanctioned low-friction path, so blank issues are not needed. (`auto-status-proposed.yml` вҖ” repurposed by #179 вҖ” now serves as **defense-in-depth** for deliberate non-UI label-free creations (API / `gh issue create --no-label`): it stamps `status:proposed`+`task`. `/triage` is a deprecated alias for `/activate`, В§5.12/В§5.18.)

**Bootstrap path.** `/onboard-dir-mode` installs the tier-N artifacts via a **PR** to the target вҖ” never direct-push. Labels + Project install directly (not git-tracked); maintainer reverts via `gh label delete` / `gh project delete` per the reversibility contract below. **Stage-0 precedes all of this**: a brand-new target with no default branch (empty repo / unborn HEAD) is taken to a seedable default branch by `/bootstrap-repo` (В§5.0) *before* `/onboard` (В§5.1) can run вҖ” a PR-based substrate install presupposes a default branch to target, so stage-0 owns the no-default-branch starting state.

**Graceful-degradation principle.** Dir-mode commands check their substrate prerequisites before acting. **Hard-refusal only when the SPECIFIC dependency for the command is missing AND the command's contract cannot be met without it** вҖ” otherwise run in degraded mode with a one-line warning. Per-command judgment, not global. Test anchors: `/file-issue` works at tier 1; `/file-directive` hard-refuses at tier 1 (no `directive` label), degrades-with-warning at tier 2 (no Project mirror), works fully at tier 3; `/activate` (which `/triage` now aliases, В§5.12/В§5.18) requires tier 2 (the `status:proposed` label); `activation-reviewer` at tier 2 falls back to the existing bootstrap allowance for repos without MISSION.md.

**Reversibility contract.** Every install step is detectable + revertable: files via `git rm` in a normal PR; labels via `gh label delete`; Project via out-of-band `gh project delete` (owner-state, not scripted). The shell can be fully unwound from a target via one PR (file removals) + one-liner per label + an out-of-band Project decision. The per-command **substrate preflight** has landed (Directive #107, children #114/#118 merged): each dir-mode command (`/file-directive`, `/activate`, `/complete-directive`, `/list-directives`, `/link-directive`, `/consume-initiative`, `/initiative-feedback`, `/block-directive`) carries a step-0 preflight that aborts with `"target lacks dir-mode substrate; run /onboard-dir-mode --tier 2 first"` when `gh label list | grep -qx directive` (or `initiative`) finds nothing, fail-open on `gh` network errors.

### 1.8 In-session narrowing levers (clear-free)

A context **clear** is the bluntest narrowing tool (В§3.7) вҖ” it discards the whole working context and pays the cost of reconstructing from durable memory. The levers below keep the working context task-relevant **without** a clear, so a `/clear` is a rarer last resort rather than a routine necessity. This section inventories them as one named set with the contract each enforces and its current **enforcement face** (guidance vs. hook, in the В§6.0 sense). It is the complement of В§3.7: В§3.7 makes a clear *safe* (`active вҶ’ archived`), В§1.8 makes a clear *less necessary*.

| Lever | Contract it enforces | Current face |
|-------|----------------------|--------------|
| **Subagent isolation** (В§1.5) | Wide or context-dirtying work (broad search, multi-file review) runs in a separate agent window; only the narrowed result returns to the parent context. | **Guidance** вҖ” the CLAUDE.md subagent table + "don't re-run an exploration in `explorer`"; worktree-isolation is hook-adjacent (#285) but delegation itself is advised, not enforced. |
| **Doc вҶ’ Test вҶ’ Code phasing handoff** (В§1.2) | Each phase is its own commit; the next phase consumes the prior phase's *artifact*, not the accumulated conversation вҖ” context resets across the arc. | **Mixed** вҖ” guidance for the order; the PostToolUse commit reminder (В§6.2) and the `phase:`/`next:` status projection (В§6.4) partially mechanize it. |
| **Artifact-only reviewers** (В§1.5, В§4.5вҖ“В§4.9) | Reviewers judge from the diff / PR body / issue / MISSION, never from the main assistant's conversation вҖ” so review context stays task-scoped regardless of how long the authoring conversation grew. | **Mixed** вҖ” guidance + the worktree-isolation backstop (#285). |
| **Targeted SPEC / file reads** (В§1.3) | Consult the ToC (or a symbol search) then `Read --offset/--limit` the specific section, rather than loading a whole large file into context. | **Guidance only** вҖ” SPEC В§1.3 + CLAUDE.md prose; nothing observes a whole-file load. вҶҗ the lever reinforced below. |
| **Plan-as-manifest** (В§4.1, В§6.4) | The planner's Plan is the task-scoped manifest of what the work touches; the per-turn surface stays `status_compact`, not a re-read of everything. | **Mixed** вҖ” guidance + the UserPromptSubmit `status_compact` injection (В§6.4). |

**Advisory вҶ’ affordance migration (this section's reinforcement).** Per В§6.0 P3, a guidance-only lever is hardened into an affordance once the pattern proves out. The **targeted-reads** lever вҖ” guidance-only above вҖ” gains a positive **PostToolUse `Read` nudge** (В§6.2): when a `Read` loads a whole file (no `offset`/`limit`) above a line threshold, the hook emits a one-line, non-blocking suggestion to use a targeted `Read --offset/--limit` or delegate the search to `explorer`. The face is **positive, not a block**: a missed narrowing nudge is ignorable at no cost (В§6.0 P1 cost-asymmetry), so the lever guides rather than refuses. The other levers stay at their current faces; this section describes the present state, it does not reclassify them.

### 1.9 Harness-overlap classification

The shell runs on top of a Claude Code harness that **improves under use** and natively absorbs more of the generic agent-support machinery over time (context compaction, deferred/lazy tool loading, excerpt-reading search agents, native subagents, plan mode, task tracking, file-based memory). Treat the harness as a **rising floor** (MISSION "The mechanism"): a shell mechanism that merely re-does what the harness now does natively is redundant cost, while the shell's durable, non-redundant value concentrates in what the harness вҖ” which must stay general вҖ” does *not* encode. This section records, as standing doctrine, each mechanism's **posture** toward that floor. It is a classification, **not a removal mandate**: ceding is a forward-discipline signal (retire via a separate Issue, weighed against safety value), never an in-place deletion (#449).

**Posture vocabulary** (exactly one per mechanism):
- `cede-to-harness` вҖ” the harness now does this natively; the shell's version is redundant and is a candidate for retirement (forward discipline, not deleted here).
- `keep-as-policy` вҖ” opinionated GitHub-engineering policy the harness does not encode (and should not, staying general); the shell is the only source of it.
- `keep-as-safety-redundancy` вҖ” a deliberately redundant backstop for a high-cost-of-wrong (irreversible / shared-history-corrupting) action, kept even where the harness offers a partial native guard, per the В§6.0 cost-asymmetry principle.

Coverage is **parity-guarded** (smoke В§116): this section must classify every mechanism enumerated in В§1.8 (narrowing levers), В§4 (subagents), В§5 (slash commands), and В§6.1 (hook matchers) вҖ” a new mechanism in any of those families fails smoke until it gains a row here. The classification references each mechanism's home section by anchor; it adds no parallel contract content (В§9).

**Narrowing levers (В§1.8 вҖ” 5):**

| Lever | Posture | Rationale |
|-------|---------|-----------|
| Subagent isolation (В§1.8 / В§1.5) | `cede-to-harness` | The harness ships native subagents (Agent/Task, fork, worktree, parallel) and an excerpt-reading search agent; running wide work in a separate window is now a harness primitive. |
| Doc вҶ’ Test вҶ’ Code phasing handoff (В§1.8 / В§1.2) | `keep-as-policy` | The harness has no task-phase model; consuming the prior phase's artifact instead of the conversation is engineering policy the shell imposes. |
| Artifact-only reviewers (В§1.8 / В§4.5вҖ“В§4.9) | `keep-as-policy` | "Judge from the diff / PR / issue / MISSION, never the conversation" is a review discipline, not a harness capability. |
| Targeted SPEC / file reads (В§1.8 / В§1.3) | `cede-to-harness` | The harness now narrows input natively вҖ” deferred/lazy tool loading, excerpt-reading Explore, targeted reads вҖ” so the generic form of this lever is harness-absorbed. |
| Plan-as-manifest (В§1.8 / В§4.1) | `keep-as-policy` | The persistent, task-scoped manifest is the PR body / GitHub artifact (constraint-isomorphic durable memory), not the harness's ephemeral plan-mode buffer. |

**Subagents (В§4 вҖ” 11):**

| Subagent | Posture | Rationale |
|----------|---------|-----------|
| planner (В§4.1) | `keep-as-policy` | Produces the structured PR-body Plan (alternatives + target base) that rides the GitHub flow; overlaps plan mode only at the primitive level, not at the artifact. |
| explorer (В§4.2) | `cede-to-harness` | The native Explore agent already does read-only, excerpt-level wide search; explorer duplicates it. |
| doc-writer (В§4.3) | `keep-as-policy` | The Doc-phase role exists only because of the DocвҶ’TestвҶ’Code policy; no harness equivalent. |
| test-writer (В§4.4) | `keep-as-policy` | The failing-test-first Test-phase role is engineering policy, not a harness feature. |
| code-reviewer (В§4.5) | `keep-as-policy` | The native review skill is a tool; the shell's reviewer is a *gate* in the /ship flow judging from artifact + MISSION + issue. |
| security-reviewer (В§4.6) | `keep-as-policy` | Overlaps the native security-review skill at the tool level, but is wired as a conditional /ship gate вҖ” the gate integration is the policy. |
| issue-reviewer (В§4.7) | `keep-as-policy` | The rationale-triad gate on a proposed issue has no harness analogue. |
| plan-reviewer (В§4.8) | `keep-as-policy` | The contest-judge gate on a planner output has no harness analogue. |
| plan-challenger (В§4.8.1) | `keep-as-policy` | The adversarial rival-author on an assigned axis (Г—2, mutually blind); the generation-diversity mechanism is pure shell policy, no harness equivalent. |
| activation-reviewer (В§4.9) | `keep-as-policy` | The dir-mode substance gate (Directive / Execution / Initiative) is pure shell policy. |
| implementer (В§4.12) | `keep-as-policy` | The default Code-phase author вҖ” the action-form of task-boundary narrowing / Code-phase policy; it leans on the already-ceded native subagent-context-discard primitive but is itself the manifest-only authoring + discard-at-Execution policy, exactly like the other keep-as-policy subagents. |

**Slash commands (В§5 вҖ” 27):**

| Command | Posture | Rationale |
|---------|---------|-----------|
| /bootstrap-repo (В§5.0) | `keep-as-policy` | Stage-0 seeding of a GitHub-standard repo; not a harness concern. |
| /onboard (В§5.1) | `keep-as-policy` | GitHub-standard readiness check; shell-specific. |
| /file-issue (В§5.2) | `keep-as-policy` | Issue-as-durable-memory filing with a rationale gate; GitHub-flow policy. |
| /work-on (В§5.3) | `keep-as-policy` | issue вҶ’ branch вҶ’ draft PR вҶ’ planner orchestration; the core GH flow. |
| /sync-pr (В§5.4) | `keep-as-policy` | PR-as-living-doc curation; shell-specific. |
| /status (В§5.5) | `keep-as-policy` | Work-state summary over the GH-flow artifacts, not the harness's generic status. |
| /review (В§5.6) | `keep-as-policy` | Invokes the reviewer gates as a flow step; native review skills are tools, this is the gate. |
| /ship (В§5.7) | `keep-as-policy` | The ready вҶ’ CI вҶ’ merge-or-park gate; the heart of the flow, no harness equivalent. |
| /adr (В§5.8) | `keep-as-policy` | Architecture Decision Record authoring; GitHub-repo doctrine. |
| /audit (В§5.9) | `keep-as-policy` | Query over the shell's own audit log; shell-specific. |
| /file-directive (В§5.10) | `keep-as-policy` | Dir-mode planning tier; no harness analogue. |
| /list-directives (В§5.11) | `keep-as-policy` | Dir-mode listing; shell-specific. |
| /activate (В§5.12) | `keep-as-policy` | Proposed вҶ’ Active lifecycle gate; shell policy. |
| /complete-directive (В§5.13) | `keep-as-policy` | Directive closeout with an evidence gate; shell policy. |
| /link-directive (В§5.14) | `keep-as-policy` | Execution вҶ” Directive parenting; dir-mode policy. |
| /reflect (В§5.15) | `keep-as-policy` | Post-merge reflection on the parent Directive; shell-specific. |
| /revise-directive (В§5.16) | `keep-as-policy` | Directive body revision with archive; shell policy. |
| /block-directive (В§5.17) | `keep-as-policy` | Directive blocking lifecycle; shell policy. |
| /release (В§5.20) | `keep-as-policy` | Changelog consolidation + release PR; GitHub-flow policy. |
| /consume-initiative (В§5.21) | `keep-as-policy` | Initiative вҶ’ Directive extraction; dir-mode policy. |
| /initiative-feedback (В§5.22) | `keep-as-policy` | Upstream escalation comments; shell policy. |
| /changelog (В§5.23) | `keep-as-policy` | Per-PR changelog fragment authoring; release-backbone policy. |
| /flush (В§5.24) | `keep-as-policy` | The active вҶ’ archived distillation before a clear вҖ” the task-boundary handoff half of the narrowing differentiator; overlaps the harness's raw /clear only at the primitive level. |
| /recall (В§5.25) | `keep-as-policy` | Episodic retrieval over the project's GitHub decision record (issues / PRs / ADRs), a different substrate from the harness's private memory recall. |
| /replan-check (В§5.26) | `keep-as-policy` | Plan-vs-diff divergence check; shell policy. |
| /reconcile-spec (В§5.27) | `keep-as-policy` | Code-vs-SPEC drift classification + user-gated SPEC correction; SSOT-maintenance policy with no harness analogue. |
| /implement (В§5.28) | `keep-as-policy` | The default Phase-C author вҖ” manifest-assembly + structured-return absorption around the implementer subagent; the Code-phase discard-at-Execution policy, no harness analogue. |

**Hook matchers (В§6.1 вҖ” 17):**

| Matcher | Posture | Rationale |
|---------|---------|-----------|
| branch (В§6.1) | `keep-as-safety-redundancy` | A protected-branch commit/push corrupts shared history (irreversible); a backstop above any harness permission prompt. |
| force-push (В§6.1) | `keep-as-safety-redundancy` | Force-push to a protected/ambiguous ref is irreversible history loss; deliberate redundancy. |
| secret (В§6.1) | `keep-as-safety-redundancy` | A leaked secret is irreversible once pushed; staged-diff scanning backstops harness sandbox/permission guards. |
| destructive (В§6.1) | `keep-as-safety-redundancy` | `git reset --hard` / `git clean -f` discard work irrecoverably; redundancy above the harness's destructive-command prompts. |
| sensitive (В§6.1) | `keep-as-safety-redundancy` | Editing `.env` / `*.pem` / credentials risks irreversible leak; backstops the harness's partial sensitive-file handling. |
| amend (В§6.1) | `keep-as-safety-redundancy` | `--amend` after push rewrites published history; an irreversible-action backstop. |
| no-verify (В§6.1) | `keep-as-safety-redundancy` | `--no-verify` strips the very gates that catch irreversible mistakes; kept as a meta-backstop. |
| backmerge (В§6.1) | `keep-as-safety-redundancy` | A wrong-direction protectedвҶ’feature merge can corrupt shared history; a redundant guard. |
| ac-closeout (В§6.1) | `keep-as-policy` | "No merge with unchecked AC" is dir-mode completion policy; no harness analogue. |
| commit-format (В§6.1) | `keep-as-policy` | Conventional-commit subject enforcement is repo policy. |
| merge-strategy (В§6.1) | `keep-as-policy` | `--merge`-only to the default branch is a GitHub-flow policy choice. |
| push-parity (В§6.1) | `keep-as-policy` | Block `gh pr merge` while the local branch is strictly ahead of its pushed remote head (unpushed commits, #244) вҖ” a merge-integrity policy; no harness analogue. |
| merge-attestation (В§6.1) | `keep-as-policy` | Block `gh pr merge` whose review was skipped (no attestation, zero-network) or done at a stale head (#246/#543) вҖ” a review-integrity policy; the un-skippable pre-merge backstop on a CI-less target. |
| proposed-protect (В§6.1) | `keep-as-policy` | Block branching a Proposed / Directive Issue вҖ” lifecycle policy. |
| label-parent-consistency (В§6.1) | `keep-as-policy` | Issue type вҶ” parent-marker consistency is dir-mode schema policy. |
| initiative-readonly (В§6.1) | `keep-as-policy` | Initiatives are read-only to the shell вҖ” boundary policy (MISSION "Explicitly NOT goals"). |
| directive-close (В§6.1) | `keep-as-policy` | Block a close keyword auto-closing a Directive вҖ” dir-mode lifecycle policy (Directives close only via /complete-directive, В§5.13); Execution auto-close stays correct. |
| trusted-filer-mutate (В§6.1) | `keep-as-policy` | Filer-trust mutation rules are dir-mode governance policy. |
| out-of-scope (В§6.1) | `keep-as-policy` | The registry-scope boundary (edit/destructive outside registered paths) is a shell-specific containment policy. |
| format (В§6.1) | `keep-as-policy` | Staged-diff format enforcement is repo policy. |

**Reading of the result.** The classification is lopsided by design, and that lopsidedness *is* the doctrine: the narrowing-*primitive* levers (subagent isolation, targeted reads) and the generic search subagent (explorer) cede to the harness, while every GitHub-engineering policy вҖ” the flow commands, the dir-mode lifecycle, the enforcement matchers вҖ” and the constraint-isomorphic durable-memory levers (Plan-as-manifest, /flush, /recall) stay. The shell's non-redundant value lives where the harness, staying general, structurally cannot reach: opinionated engineering policy, high-asymmetry safety redundancy, and GitHub-artifact-as-durable-memory.

---

## 2. Engineering flow

```
[Project start / joining]
  ./scripts/clone-into.sh <upstream-repo-url>
  cd workspace/<repo>
  ghjig
  /onboard                   вҶҗ check target SSOT, .github/, permissions, branch protection
       в”Ӯ
       в–ј
[Start a work item]
  /file-issue <short description>   вҶҗ if needed, create the issue with goal + acceptance criteria
       в”Ӯ
       в–ј
  /work-on <issue#>           вҶҗ pull upstream, create branch, call planner, create draft PR
       в”Ӯ
       в–ј
[planner agent] plan + checklist. User approval required.
       в”Ӯ
       в–ј
[Phase A: Doc]
       в”Ӯ   doc-writer agent if useful. Separate commit for SSOT updates.
       в”Ӯ   commit: `docs(#N): ...`
       в”Ӯ   Tick the PR body checklist with the sha.
       в–ј
[Phase B: Test]
       в”Ӯ   test-writer agent for the failing test.
       в”Ӯ   Confirm the intended failure.
       в”Ӯ   commit: `test(#N): ...`
       в”Ӯ   Update the PR body.
       в–ј
[Phase C: Code]
       в”Ӯ   Implementation, committed in small increments.
       в”Ӯ   Each commit: hooks check format / secrets / tests.
       в”Ӯ   commit: `feat(#N): ...` / `fix(#N): ...`
       в”Ӯ   Update the PR body.
       в–ј
[Mid-checkpoint]   /status, /review as needed
       в”Ӯ
       в–ј
[/ship]
       в”Ӯ   0. resolve mode (flag > env > .claude/state/mode > default `attended`) вҖ” В§5.7.1
       в”Ӯ   1. invoke code-reviewer (blocker вҶ’ stop)
       в”Ӯ   2. (conditional) security-reviewer
       в”Ӯ   3. doc-writer final sync check
       в”Ӯ   4. run the full test suite
       в”Ӯ   5. curate the PR body (tidy stale items, ship-gate ticks)
       в”Ӯ   6. verify `Closes #N`
       в”Ӯ   7. check CI status (`gh pr checks`)
       в”Ӯ   7.5вҖ“7.7. pre-ready gates: checklist audit / AC closeout / changelog вҖ” see В§5.7
       в”Ӯ   8. `gh pr ready`
       в–ј
   в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
   в”Ӯ mode = attended (default)             в”Ӯ   mode = unattended
   в”Ӯ stop at "ready"; human picks up       в”Ӯ   continue: classify blocker
   в–ј                                       в–ј
[Human review + merge]              в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
  On merge, issue auto-closes       в”Ӯ clean вҶ’ `gh pr merge --auto     в”Ӯ
  and branch auto-deletes.          в”Ӯ           --merge --delete-     в”Ӯ
                                    в”Ӯ           branch` (#43)         в”Ӯ
                                    в”Ӯ soft  вҶ’ one self-fix-and-push,  в”Ӯ
                                    в”Ӯ         then wait               в”Ӯ
                                    в”Ӯ hard  вҶ’ comment + label         в”Ӯ
                                    в”Ӯ         `unattended-parked`,    в”Ӯ
                                    в”Ӯ         log, stop               в”Ӯ
                                    в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ
```

If a session is cut off mid-flight, the next session's SessionStart hook (В§6.5) injects the current branch's PR body, the referenced issue body, MISSION/CLAUDE, etc. as a single context block. Then before each user message, the UserPromptSubmit hook (В§6.4) only refreshes a short status summary when something has changed. The user can just say "continue" without re-explanation.

### 2.1 Directive lifecycle

A Directive moves through **four states** (Proposed / Active / Blocked / Completed). All transitions are entered via explicit dir-mode commands (В§5.10вҖ“В§5.22). Status is encoded as **labels on the Issue**; the Project Item's Status field is mirrored by `.github/workflows/issues-to-project-mirror.yml`. A transient revision state was considered and dropped вҖ” the audit-log entry + the archived prior-body comment are the durable evidence of revision (see `/revise-directive`, В§5.16).

**Scope of the 4-state machine.** The four states + the `Blocked`/`Completed` transitions are **Directive-specific**. Execution Issues (`execution`/`task`/`bug`) share only the `Proposed вҶ’ Active` gate (the full-symmetry lifecycle below), not `Blocked`/`Completed`. **`discussion`** Issues (В§5.19) and **`initiative`** Issues (В§1.7) are **outside this lifecycle entirely** вҖ” a discussion closes via `/resolve-discussion`, and an Initiative is read-only/consumed (the shell never sets its `status:*`). Because the mirror derives the Project `Status` field from the open/no-`status:*` label shape, an open `discussion`/`initiative` Issue surfaces in the Project as `Active` by default; that is a derived-view artifact of the shared field, **not** a claim that they run the Directive 4-state machine вҖ” read their real state from their own path (resolve/consume), not the mirrored `Status`.

```
   /file-directive
        в”Ӯ  (creates Issue with [directive, status:proposed])
        в–ј
   в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ        /activate        в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
   в”ӮProposedв”Ӯ в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв–¶ в”Ӯ Active в”Ӯ
   в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ   (reviewer-gated;      в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ
                removes status:           в”Ӯ
                proposed label)           в”Ӯ  /complete-directive
                                          в”Ӯ  (reviewer-gated; closes
                                          в”Ӯ   Issue --reason completed)
                                          в–ј
                                     в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
                                     в”ӮCompleted в”Ӯ
                                     в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

       /block-directive (В§5.17)
   Active в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв–¶ Blocked
                          (adds status:blocked label;
                           Issue stays open;
                           unblock via /activate)

   /revise-directive (В§5.16) вҖ” body replace + audit log only;
   no Status change (the audit-log entry + the archived prior-body
   comment ARE the durable evidence of revision).
```

**State semantics** (label-encoded on the Issue; mirrored to the Project Item by `issues-to-project-mirror.yml`):

| State | Encoding on Issue | Entry transition | Reviewer-gated? |
|-------|-------------------|------------------|-----------------|
| `Proposed` | open + `directive` label + `status:proposed` label | `/file-directive` (creates with both labels) | Yes вҖ” `activation-reviewer` on filing body |
| `Active` | open + `directive` label + no `status:*` label | `/activate` (removes `status:proposed`; `/activate-directive` is a deprecated alias, В§5.12) | Yes вҖ” re-reviews body in case it was edited since filing |
| `Blocked` | open + `directive` label + `status:blocked` label | `/block-directive` (adds `status:blocked` + `## Blocked: <reason>` comment) | No on block (annotation-only); unblock via `/activate` (treats `status:blocked` as a re-activatable precondition; on `pass` removes the label, В§5.12) |
| `Completed` | closed + `directive` label + close-reason=completed | `/complete-directive` (posts closing-comment evidence + closes `--reason completed`) | Yes вҖ” `activation-reviewer` evaluates evidence sufficiency |

**Lifecycle symmetry for Execution Issues** (#172, Directive #167). Under **full symmetry**, the `Proposed вҶ’ Active` gate applies to **all** Issues, not just Directives: `/file-issue` stamps `status:proposed` on every new Execution Issue, and `/activate <N>` (В§5.12) removes it after an `activation-reviewer` pass вҖ” the same generate вҶ’ review вҶ’ gate shape the Directive path uses. `status:proposed` Execution Issues are Issue-ops-only and cannot enter the PR/branch flow (the `proposed-protect` hook, В§6.1, blocks branch creation). `issue-reviewer` (author-side, at `/file-issue`) and `activation-reviewer` (observer-side, at `/activate`) are complementary, mirroring how `/file-directive` and `/activate` both gate the Directive path. The `awaiting-author` label (В§1.7) marks the handoff state when the reviewer returned `revise` or a trusted-filer `reject` and the author's action is pending.

**Reviewer-gating contract** (per В§1.5 operating-mode coupling):

- `attended` mode: human reviews `activation-reviewer`'s output and decides.
- `unattended` mode: `activation-reviewer`'s VERDICT line (`pass` / `revise` / `reject`) gates directly. `reject` on activation applies the filer-aware handling (В§5.12: trusted вҶ’ keep open + `awaiting-author`; untrusted + draft вҶ’ close + auto-discussion; untrusted no-draft вҶ’ close); `reject`/insufficient-evidence on completion leaves the Directive `Active`; `reject` on revision aborts the body replacement (no Status change, no audit `reconciled` line). `revise` retains `status:proposed` + `awaiting-author`, escalating to `reject` after N=3 rounds.

**Escape hatch.** `SKIP_HOOKS=directive-review SKIP_REASON='<why>' /complete-directive <id>` (and the equivalent on `/file-directive`, `/activate`, `/revise-directive`) bypasses the reviewer; the bypass is audit-logged per В§7. Use is reserved for cases where the reviewer's verdict is wrong and a human accepts the recorded responsibility вҖ” not a normalized routing. `/block-directive` is not reviewer-gated (annotation-only вҖ” no body change) and therefore has no review-skip variant.

**Audit categories** for dir-mode events: `directive-file`, `directive-activate`, `activation` (the `/activate` category, generalized from `directive-activate`; the log retains historical `directive-activate` entries), `directive-complete`, `directive-revise`, `directive-block`, `directive-link`, `directive-reflect` (`/reflect` posts/skips), `directive-exec-count` (`/ship`'s post-merge directive-aware audit, В§5.7), `directive-review`, `proposed-protect` (generalized from `directive-protect` by #171; the append-only log retains historical `directive-protect` entries), `triage` (decisions: `decided` with action=accept|reject, `refiled`, `rejected-skip`), `trusted-filer-mutate` (decisions: `deny`, `allow`), `label-parent-consistency` (decisions: `block`, `allow`; enforces labelвҶ”parent-marker consistency on `gh issue edit --add-label` вҖ” the `Parent Directive` marker for execution/task/bug (#199), plus the `initiative`/`directive` tier-key mutual-exclusivity and the Directive parent-XOR (#251), В§6.1), `initiative-readonly` (decisions: `block`, `allow`; blocks mutating `gh issue edit`/`close`/`reopen` on an `initiative` Issue вҖ” the shell consumes Initiatives, never mutates them; #251, В§6.1), `directive-close` (decisions: `block`, `allow`; blocks a close keyword + Directive `#N` in a PR body or commit message вҖ” auto-close would bypass `/complete-directive`; #490, В§6.1), `initiative-consume` (decisions: `extracted` with count=N, `under-specified`, `revise`; emitted by `/consume-initiative` В§5.21, #257), `initiative-feedback` (decisions: `challenge`, `completion`; emitted by `/initiative-feedback` В§5.22, #260), `mirror-stale-warn` (reserved for `issues-to-project-mirror.yml` failures; currently emits nothing). All append to `.claude/audit/audit.jsonl` per В§6/В§7.

---

## 3. SSOT distribution and injection

### 3.1 Location summary

```
GHJig-Claude/                      вҶҗ Process SSOT (single git)
в”ңв”Җв”Җ .claude/
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ settings.json                  вҶҗ hook / permission definitions
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ CLAUDE.md                      вҶҗ shell norms (natively loaded whole each session by Claude Code; thin-pointer + size budget В§9)
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ agents/                        вҶҗ subagent definitions (11)
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ commands/                      вҶҗ slash command definitions
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ hooks/                         вҶҗ hook scripts
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ templates/                     вҶҗ mission, issue, pr_body, adr, etc.
в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ audit/                         вҶҗ runtime audit log (.gitignored)
в”ңв”Җв”Җ bin/ghjig                     вҶҗ wrapper (env setup + exec claude)
в”ңв”Җв”Җ scripts/
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ bootstrap.sh
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ clone-into.sh
в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ ac_closeout.sh              вҶҗ posts '## AC closeout' on PR-linked issues (idempotent; satisfies В§6.1 gate)
в”ңв”Җв”Җ workspace/                         вҶҗ actual work (.gitignored)
в””в”Җв”Җ docs/, README.md, SPEC.md

workspace/<target-repo>/               вҶҗ Project SSOT (its own git)
в”ңв”Җв”Җ MISSION.md
в”ңв”Җв”Җ README.md
в”ңв”Җв”Җ CLAUDE.md
в”ңв”Җв”Җ docs/ARCHITECTURE.md, docs/ADRs/
в””в”Җв”Җ .claude/                           вҶҗ bundle of symlinks injected by the shell
    в”ңв”Җв”Җ ghjig-root      -> <canonical shell root>            (untracked binding; lets hooks resolve the shell via $CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR вҖ” no global env)
    в”ңв”Җв”Җ settings.local.json -> shell/.claude/settings.injected.json
    в”ңв”Җв”Җ agents/<name>.md    -> shell/.claude/agents/<name>.md     (skip injection if target has same name)
    в”ңв”Җв”Җ commands/<name>.md  -> shell/.claude/commands/<name>.md   (skip injection if target has same name)
    в””в”Җв”Җ (target's own .claude/CLAUDE.md, if present, is left alone)
```

> Conflict handling details in В§3.2.

### 3.2 Injection mechanism

`scripts/clone-into.sh` runs the following right after `git clone`. **The target's existing `.claude/` content is never overwritten.** If a same-named asset already exists, that asset is not injected вҖ” only a warning is printed. The target's choice wins.

```bash
mkdir -p "$TARGET/.claude" "$TARGET/.claude/agents" "$TARGET/.claude/commands"

# Per-project binding symlink (no global env): hooks resolve the canonical
# shell root via $CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR/.claude/ghjig-root (see В§3.2.1).
ln -sfn "$SHELL_ROOT" "$TARGET/.claude/ghjig-root"

# settings.local.json: symlink to the shell's settings.injected.json (the
# target-facing settings whose hook commands resolve via the binding symlink;
# the shell's own settings.json resolves hooks via $CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR for
# dogfood вҖ” project dir == shell root, so no env var is on the hook hot path).
if [ -e "$TARGET/.claude/settings.local.json" ] && [ ! -L "$TARGET/.claude/settings.local.json" ]; then
  echo "WARN: $TARGET/.claude/settings.local.json already exists. Shell settings not injected; user merge needed." >&2
else
  ln -sfn "$SHELL_ROOT/.claude/settings.injected.json" "$TARGET/.claude/settings.local.json"
fi

# agents/commands: skip and warn if a same-named asset exists.
for kind in agents commands; do
  for src in "$SHELL_ROOT/.claude/$kind"/*.md; do
    [ -e "$src" ] || continue
    dest="$TARGET/.claude/$kind/$(basename "$src")"
    if [ -e "$dest" ] && [ ! -L "$dest" ]; then
      echo "WARN: $dest already exists. Shell asset injection skipped." >&2
    else
      ln -sfn "$src" "$dest"
    fi
  done
done

# Add the shell injections (symlinks) to the target's .git/info/exclude so target git doesn't see them.
for entry in .claude/settings.local.json .claude/ghjig-root; do
  grep -qxF "$entry" "$TARGET/.git/info/exclude" 2>/dev/null \
    || printf '%s\n' "$entry" >> "$TARGET/.git/info/exclude"
done
```

Rules:
- If the target has a same-named asset, the shell's version is not injected (conflict avoidance). If you want to use both, rename or move your own asset.
- Post-hoc registration of a directory the user already cloned: `scripts/register.sh <path>` runs the same inject logic.
- The target's `CLAUDE.md`, `MISSION.md`, `docs/` are **not touched**. The shell's CLAUDE.md (process norms) is loaded whole by Claude Code as project instructions each session вҖ” not hook-injected; UserPromptSubmit injects only `status_compact` (В§6.4). As an always-on surface CLAUDE.md is held to the В§9 thin-pointer + size budget.

#### 3.2.1 Hook command path resolution

There are **two** consumers of hook settings, and they resolve the shell root differently (#312, Directive #311):

1. **The shell repo itself (dogfood)** reads its own tracked `.claude/settings.json`, whose `command` entries use **`${CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR}/.claude/hooks/<e>.sh`**. For the shell's own repo `$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR` (guaranteed by Claude Code for hook commands) *is* the shell root, so the hook hot path resolves **without any env var**. This is what keeps enforcement armed through an in-place rename of the shell-root var itself (then `$GHJIG_SHELL_ROOT`, now `$GHJIG_ROOT` вҖ” #533, #537): the running session never needs the renamed var to find its hooks, so a rename can never leave the current session's hot path expanding an empty prefix. `$GHJIG_ROOT` is still exported by the `bin/ghjig` wrapper (**convenience output, not load-bearing** as of #539 вҖ” deliberately-invoked scripts self-locate rather than trust the inherited value, see Self-location below), but it is no longer on the settings.json hook-command path вҖ” and it is **not an input** to the hook entry points, which never consult the ambient environment (see Hook self-location below, #537). (The `${CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR}` form mirrors the injected-target pattern in (2). As of #539 the dogfood repo also carries the binding symlink вҖ” a **committed relative self-symlink** `.claude/ghjig-root -> ..` вҖ” so *every* registered project, targets and dogfood alike, has `.claude/ghjig-root` (В§3.6); the dogfood hook hot path itself stays `${CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR}`-direct as above.)

2. **Injected targets** symlink `settings.local.json вҶ’ shell/.claude/settings.injected.json`, whose `command` entries use **`${CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR}/.claude/ghjig-root/.claude/hooks/<e>.sh`**. Claude Code guarantees `$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR` (the project root) for hook commands; `.claude/ghjig-root` is the per-project **binding symlink** (created at inject time, В§3.2) pointing at the canonical shell root. So the target resolves the shell **without any global env var** вҖ” a plain `claude` launched in the target works. This **supersedes** the prior rule (which required `$GHJIG_SHELL_ROOT` and noted that bare `$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR` "would resolve to an empty location and fail") вҖ” the binding symlink is exactly what makes `$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR`-relative resolution succeed.

```json
// shell/.claude/settings.injected.json (target-facing)
{ "hooks": { "PreToolUse": [{ "matcher": "Bash",
  "hooks": [{ "type": "command",
    "command": "${CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR}/.claude/ghjig-root/.claude/hooks/pre_tool_use.sh" }] }] } }
```

**Self-location вҖ” one idiom (#539).** Independent of which consumer invoked them, every shell-side entry point вҖ” the hook entry scripts, the CLI scripts, and the lib consult sites вҖ” derives its root with the **single** idiom `root="${GHJIG_ROOT_OVERRIDE:-$(cd "$(dirname "${BASH_SOURCE[0]}")/../.." && pwd -P)}"` (path depth adjusted per file location; hook entries name it `SHELL_ROOT`, then `export GHJIG_ROOT="$SHELL_ROOT"`) вҖ” the script self-locates from `${BASH_SOURCE[0]}`, and `pwd -P` resolves the `ghjig-root` symlink through to the real canonical root so helpers/`hookrt.sh`/audit still resolve. This is what lets the target path in (2) find the shell's code. `GHJIG_ROOT_OVERRIDE` is a **test-only seam** (precedent: `GHJIG_STATE_DIR_OVERRIDE`, В§3.2.2); on the production hook path the **ambient environment is never consulted** (#537) вҖ” an inherited `$GHJIG_ROOT` (or a legacy `$GHJIG_SHELL_ROOT`) cannot redirect which shell tree the hooks load, which kills the cross-clone contamination vector where a stale global export made clone B's hooks source clone A's helpers. The #537 demotion is a **clean cut, no deprecation shim**: a lingering legacy export is functionally ignored, and surfaced by a SessionStart banner arm (В§6.5(c)).

`$GHJIG_ROOT` is therefore an **internal, exported-only** variable, not an external input: the hook entry points and the CLI scripts export it after self-locating (above). The `bin/ghjig` wrapper's `export GHJIG_ROOT` on entry is **convenience output, not load-bearing** вҖ” every downstream consumer re-derives the root itself rather than trusting the inherited value:

```bash
#!/usr/bin/env bash
set -euo pipefail
export GHJIG_ROOT="$(cd "$(dirname "${BASH_SOURCE[0]}")/.." && pwd -P)"
exec claude "$@"
```
