Deliberately-invoked scripts no longer keep an env-first default: as of #539 the four CLI scripts (`dir_mode_project.sh`, `migrate_v3.sh`, `onboard_target.sh`, `setup_project.sh`) drop `: "${GHJIG_ROOT:=$SCRIPT_ROOT}"` and self-locate unconditionally with the idiom above, then `export GHJIG_ROOT` for their children вҖ” the ambient environment is retired as an input **everywhere**, not just on the hook path (`scripts/ghjig_skip.sh` already worked this way). The lib consult sites вҖ” four files, `audit_log_path.sh`, `dir_mode_project_resolve.sh` (Г—2), `inject.sh` (Г—2, including the former `${GHJIG_ROOT:?}` precondition), `self_register.sh` вҖ” adopt the same idiom in place of reading the environment; each self-locates *into* `GHJIG_ROOT` before any bare `$GHJIG_ROOT` use (libs run under `set -u`), which converts the prior convention "every entry must export first" into a **local structural guarantee** at the consumer. This also fixes a live unset-reachable bug where `narrowing_candidates.sh`/`promotion_candidates.sh` reached `audit_log_path.sh` with `GHJIG_ROOT` never exported (the fallback resolved to a filesystem-root-anchored `/.claude/audit/вҖҰ`).

**Agent-side command resolution (#539).** `.claude/commands` flows can rely on none of the above: each command step runs as a separate Bash call with no shared state, agent shells carry no `$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR`, and ambient `$GHJIG_ROOT` is retired as an input. Every `$GHJIG_ROOT/вҖҰ` reference in a command file is recast **structurally**, through the binding symlink every registered project carries вҖ” by one of two forms, keyed to whether the reference sits **inside a fenced multi-line `bash` block** (which can bind a local `$GR` variable) or is a **bare/inline reference**:

- **Fenced `bash` block** references (a multi-line block that `source`s, `bash`-invokes, or appends to a shell-root path вҖ” e.g. `. "$GR/.claude/hooks/вҖҰ"`, `bash "$GR/scripts/вҖҰ"`) bind `$GR` once via the CWD-robust prelude below and reuse it. `git rev-parse --show-toplevel` does not assume the block runs from the project root, and the guard **fails loud** rather than expanding empty (or, inside a nested/vendored repo, silently resolving to the wrong root):

  ```bash
  GR="$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel 2>/dev/null)/.claude/ghjig-root"
  [ -e "$GR/.claude" ] || { echo "GHJig: not inside a registered project (cd to the project root, or run scripts/register.sh)"; exit 1; }
  ```

- **Bare/inline** references вҖ” both a passive template the agent merely *reads*/copies **and** a single-line `Source вҖҰ`/invocation the agent runs as one Bash call вҖ” use the project-root-relative path `.claude/ghjig-root/вҖҰ` directly, with no shell variable (a `$GR/` token here would be a dangling reference, since `$GR` lives only inside a fenced block). These resolve against the **command-execution CWD, which is the project root** вҖ” the documented invariant for every command flow (`/onboard`, `/reconcile-spec`, etc. explicitly run from the target repo's cwd). If that invariant is violated the inline source **fails loud** (undefined helper вҶ’ command error), never silently loading the wrong tree; the extra CWD-robustness of the fenced-block prelude is reserved for the multi-line blocks that already carry it, so the common inline case stays a single clean token.

Because the dogfood repo commits its own self-symlink (#539, В§3.6), both forms behave identically in targets and in the shell repo.

Inside hook scripts, shell-side **code** (helpers, hooks) is accessed via `$GHJIG_ROOT`, while target files and **per-project ephemeral state** are accessed via `$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR` вҖ” keep code (shared) and state (per-project) cleanly separated (В§3.2.2).

#### 3.2.2 Per-project ephemeral state (`ghjig-state/`)

Ephemeral runtime assets вҖ” the **audit log**, the `.claude/state` **caches** (issue-type, issue-filer, status, pr; the park log), and the scope-guard **registry** вҖ” resolve per project under `ghjig-state/` (#314 + #316, Directive #311). The audit log and caches resolve via `ghjig_state_dir()`; the registry resolves via `ghjig_registry_file [project_dir]`; both live in `hookrt.sh`.

`ghjig_state_dir()` resolution order (`set -u`-safe, no external calls): `GHJIG_STATE_DIR_OVERRIDE` (test seam) вҶ’ `${CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR}/.claude/ghjig-state` when `CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR` is set (Claude Code guarantees it for hook commands) вҶ’ otherwise **empty**, in which case callers fall back to the legacy shared `$GHJIG_ROOT/.claude/{audit,state}`.

`ghjig_registry_file [project_dir]` serves two execution contexts with a single definition (#316):
- **Argless** (hook context вҖ” `cwd_guard.in_scope`/`path_in_scope`): defers to `ghjig_state_dir()` вҶ’ `${esd}/registry.txt`, else the legacy shared `${GHJIG_ROOT:-}/.claude/state/registry.txt`.
- **With an explicit project-dir argument** (launcher / CLI context вҖ” `bin/ghjig`, `register.sh`/`inject`, `self_register`, `dr_check_registry_guard` вҖ” where `CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR` is unset because the call *precedes* the Claude session): `${1}/.claude/ghjig-state/registry.txt`.

The caller passes the project root it already holds (the `<dir>` argument or `pwd -P`), so registry discovery becomes "does `<dir>` carry its own `ghjig-state/registry.txt`?" вҖ” a **self-describing per-project registry**, not a lookup in a shared cross-project index. Under Directive #311's model there is no longer a central authority listing every project.

**Back-compat read-floor.** Every *reader* вҖ” `cwd_guard.in_scope`/`path_in_scope` (hook context) and `dr_check_registry_guard`/`bin/ghjig` (CLI context) вҖ” when the per-project registry file is **absent**, falls back to *reading* the legacy shared `$GHJIG_ROOT/.claude/state/registry.txt`. This keeps a target registered before #316 (legacy entry only, no `ghjig-state/registry.txt` yet) enforcing on its next session, honoring the #311 "existing setups keep working" constraint. The fallback is **read-only** and triggers **only when the per-project file is absent** вҖ” once a target is registered the new way (per-project file present), the shared registry is never consulted for it, so a migrated target gets strict isolation. Writers (`inject`, `self_register`) always write per-project, so write-isolation (success signal 2) is unaffected; and because `in_scope` only ever matches the *current* path against the registry, reading the shared registry as a floor cannot leak another project's scope into the current session.

Consequence: in hook context two projects bound to the same canonical code source have **mutually-invisible** audit/caches **and registries** (writing audit/registry/state in project A leaves project B's `ghjig-state/` unchanged); in plain-Bash context (env unset, no arg) behavior is unchanged (back-compat вҖ” the legacy shared paths remain the floor). This realizes the В§1.7 / MISSION principle that the **codebase is shared** while **ephemeral state isolates per project**. `ghjig-state/` is added to the target's `.git/info/exclude` (the shell repo excludes its own `ghjig-state/` via its tracked `.gitignore`).

**Fail posture (security).** The registry gates the `out-of-scope` enforcement matcher (В§6.1). A missing/empty registry yields `in_scope=false` вҶ’ hooks pass through transparently (**fail-open**), unchanged from the pre-#316 shared-registry behavior вҖ” the move changes only *which path* is read, never the `[ -f "$registry" ] || return 1` posture or the #218 trailing-slash normalization. Because the resolver is `set -u`-safe, an unset `GHJIG_ROOT` (a plain-Bash context that never passed through the wrapper or a hook export, В§3.2.1) cannot abort the guard. Dogfood coherence: `self_register` writes through `ghjig_registry_file "$SHELL_ROOT"`, so the shell's registration write-target equals the path `cwd_guard` reads under `CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR=$SHELL_ROOT` вҖ” a mismatch would silently disable enforcement inside the shell repo (В§3.6).

### 3.3 Scope guard вҖ” cwd-based

All hook scripts prelude:

```bash
# Match physical PWD against registered (physical) paths in the registry.
# The registry is written by register.sh / clone-into.sh; clones inside workspace/ are recorded the same way.
# It resolves per-project via ghjig_registry_file (hookrt.sh, #316): argless = hook
# context (CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR), set -u-safe, legacy shared path as the floor.
REGISTRY=$(ghjig_registry_file)
PWD_REAL=$(cd "$PWD" 2>/dev/null && pwd -P) || exit 0
[ -f "$REGISTRY" ] || exit 0
in_scope=0
while IFS= read -r entry; do
  [ -z "$entry" ] && continue
  case "$PWD_REAL/" in "$entry"/*) in_scope=1; break ;; esac
  [ "$PWD_REAL" = "$entry" ] && { in_scope=1; break; }
done < "$REGISTRY"
[ "$in_scope" = "1" ] || exit 0
```

вҶ’ If `ghjig` is invoked from an unregistered directory, hooks pass through transparently. Works regardless of logical vs physical `$PWD` (we use PWD_REAL). External path registration is covered by the same mechanism.

**Fail-open contract.** All three guard exits вҖ” an unresolvable `PWD_REAL` (`cd вҖҰ || exit 0`), an absent or empty registry (`[ -f "$REGISTRY" ] || exit 0`), and an out-of-scope cwd (`[ "$in_scope" = 1 ] || exit 0`) вҖ” fail **open**: a missing/empty/unreadable registry or an unregistered cwd means enforcement is **off**, never on. This is the guardrail-not-sandbox framing (В§6.1): the shell narrows what a careful engineer would not do *inside a registered project*, and is silent everywhere else; a registry that cannot be resolved can only under-enforce (pass through), never lock the user out. (The escape hatch, В§7, and the helper fail-policy table, В§6.1, follow the same fail-open posture.)

The registry (per-project `.claude/ghjig-state/registry.txt`, or the legacy shared `.claude/state/registry.txt` outside hook context) format: one physical path (`pwd -P` output) per line. Comments and blank lines are ignored.

### 3.4 User-global isolation

The shell's installation and operation leave no changes in the user-global environment. The only way to "disable" the shell is to stop invoking `ghjig`. No deactivation procedure or cleanup script is needed.

**Surfaces never touched**:
- `~/.claude` (user-global Claude settings)
- shell rc/login files (`~/.zshrc`, `~/.bashrc`, `~/.bash_profile`, `~/.profile`, `~/.config/zsh/*`, `~/.config/fish/*`, etc.)
- global git config (`~/.gitconfig`, `~/.config/git/*`)
- PATH auto-registration вҖ” the user adds `<shell-root>/bin` to PATH or uses absolute path / alias themselves. The shell never injects an export line into rc files.
- LaunchAgents, systemd user units, login items, or any auto-start registration

`bootstrap.sh` boundary:
- Allowed: check dependencies (`gh`, `git`, `python3`, `jq`), run `gh auth status`, create `.claude/audit/` and `.claude/state/` inside the shell repo.
- Forbidden: any modification of the surfaces above, package manager invocations, sudo.

Target repos are the shell's work вҖ” they fall outside this isolation rule (the injection in В§3.2 is intended behavior).

### 3.5 Entry point

`scripts/setup.sh <local-path | repo-url>` is the single host-side orchestrator: it runs `scripts/bootstrap.sh` (deps check) вҶ’ `scripts/register.sh` or `scripts/clone-into.sh` (the register/clone arg contract below) вҶ’ `scripts/lib/onboard_checks.sh` (onboard pre-flight) вҶ’ an optional dir-mode gate (`scripts/onboard_target.sh`, default N), then prints the next command (or, with `--enter`, execs `claude` directly). Reachable by relative path, so the `ghjig` PATH export is optional вҖ” only needed to invoke `ghjig` from an arbitrary directory.

`ghjig` is meant to start at the root of `workspace/<repo>/`. Subdirectories work too (walk-up), but starting at the root avoids edge cases in monorepos where subprojects may carry their own `.claude/`.

**External path support**: a target repo can live outside the shell's `workspace/` (e.g. `~/code/<repo>`). `scripts/register.sh <abs-path>` (1) creates a `workspace/<basename>` symlink, (2) records the target's physical path (`pwd -P`) in the target's per-project `.claude/ghjig-state/registry.txt` via `ghjig_registry_file "$target"` (#316), (3) runs the inject logic of В§3.2. The shell's `.gitignore` whitelists `workspace/*` so the shell git tree doesn't pick up target trees even in the external-path case. Direct clones into `workspace/` are also recorded in the registry вҖ” the guard is always registry-based.

**Auto-register prompt**: when `ghjig <path>` is called with an unregistered external path, prompt once before entering the session:
```
$ ghjig ~/code/foo
? '/Users/.../code/foo' is not registered. Register as workspace/foo and enter? [Y/n]
```
yes вҶ’ run `scripts/register.sh` вҶ’ inject logic (В§3.2) вҶ’ start session. no вҶ’ exit.

**Monorepo subprojects**: clone-into injects **only at the repo root**. Subprojects with their own `.claude/` are not recursively injected. When the user starts `ghjig` in a subproject, the walk-up finds the root's shell injection. The subproject's `.claude/CLAUDE.md` is merged via Claude Code's default walk-up behavior.

**Discovery surface** (Issue #318, Directive #311): `ghjig list` prints the registered target projects, one resolved physical path per line, then exits 0. Like `--version` it short-circuits **before** the cwd registry guard (В§3.3), so it works from any cwd including unregistered ones, and has no side effects (no audit, no registry mutation, no cwd change). Enumeration is **advisory, not authoritative** вҖ” post-#316 the registry is self-describing per-project (В§3.2.2), so there is no single global index. `list` unions two sources and dedups by resolved absolute path: (1) the `workspace/*` symlinks (`register.sh` creates one per registration вҖ” the most complete set), resolving each and **skipping dangling** links; (2) the legacy shared `$GHJIG_ROOT/.claude/state/registry.txt` (catches pre-#316 + dogfood entries). A target injected without a `workspace/` symlink, or whose symlink was removed, is **invisible to `list` by design** вҖ” this incompleteness is inherent to the shared-code/per-project-state model, not a bug.

**Binding-health surface** (Issue #334, Directive #311): when `ghjig <dir>` enters an injected target (`<dir>/.claude/settings.local.json` is a symlink) whose binding `<dir>/.claude/ghjig-root` is **missing or dangling**, it emits one non-blocking stderr warning naming the repair (`scripts/register.sh <dir>`) before `cd`-ing in and `exec claude`. This is the launch-time detector for the broken-binding silent-no-op that the #318-removed SessionStart banner structurally could not surface (the SessionStart hook is itself invoked *through* the binding вҖ” В§6.5(c)); `ghjig` runs *before* the session and resolves the dir directly, so it is the one place that can warn. Healthy bindings and non-injected dirs stay silent; the check has no side effects beyond the warning.

**Version surface** (Issue #123, Directive #122): `ghjig --version` reads the top-level `VERSION` file (single line, semver 0.x format вҖ” `MAJOR.MINOR.PATCH` with `MAJOR=0` per Directive #122 constraint #1) and exits 0 with that string on stdout. If `VERSION` is missing or empty, the handler falls back to `git -C "$SHELL_ROOT" describe --tags --always`; if both fail, a one-line diagnostic is printed to stderr and the process exits 1. The `--version` short-circuit runs immediately after `SHELL_ROOT` resolution and before the cwd-based registry guard (В§3.3), so it works from any cwd including unregistered paths. The flag has no side effects: no audit log, no registry mutation, no cwd change. Tags follow `v` + semver (e.g., `v0.2.0`) and are pushed manually post-merge вҖ” `gh pr merge` does not push tags, and the merge gate does not assert tag-state freshness (explicit Directive #122 non-goal).

### 3.6 Shell self-registration

The shell repo itself must appear in its own registry so that `cwd_guard.in_scope` (В§3.3) returns true when `ghjig` is invoked from the shell root. Without it, the shell's own hooks short-circuit on `in_scope || exit 0` and the dogfooding promise of В§17 is empty вҖ” the shell can't enforce its own discipline on itself. Self-registration writes through `ghjig_registry_file "$SHELL_ROOT"` вҶ’ `$SHELL_ROOT/.claude/ghjig-state/registry.txt` (#316), which is exactly the path `cwd_guard` reads in a dogfood session (`CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR=$SHELL_ROOT` вҶ’ argless `ghjig_registry_file` вҶ’ the same file). Write-target == read-target; a divergence would silently fail-open the shell's own scope guard.

`scripts/bootstrap.sh` (and `scripts/register.sh "$SHELL_ROOT"`) ensure `$SHELL_ROOT` is present in the registry (idempotent вҖ” repeated runs do not duplicate). Self-registration performs no `workspace/<basename>` symlink and no `inject_into` against the shell, because the shell IS the injection source and a `workspace/` symlink would loop into `workspace/` contained within `$SHELL_ROOT`. It **does**, as of #539, create the per-project **binding symlink** `.claude/ghjig-root` вҖ” for the dogfood repo a **committed relative self-symlink** `.claude/ghjig-root -> ..` (from `$SHELL_ROOT/.claude/ghjig-root`, `..` resolves to `$SHELL_ROOT`, so `.claude/ghjig-root/.claude/hooks/<e>.sh` == `$SHELL_ROOT/.claude/hooks/<e>.sh`). This makes the binding symlink **uniform**: *every* registered project вҖ” injected targets (symlink created at inject time, В§3.2) and the dogfood repo alike вҖ” carries `.claude/ghjig-root`, so the structural `.claude/ghjig-root`-relative resolution used by hook settings (В§3.2.1 consumer (2)) and the agent-side command prelude (В§3.2.1) works identically in both. The self-symlink is relative (not absolute) so it survives a re-clone of the shell repo to any path; it is committed so a fresh clone carries it without a bootstrap run. The dogfood hook hot path still resolves via `${CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR}`-direct (В§3.2.1 consumer (1)) вҖ” the self-symlink is what the *deliberately-invoked* and *agent-side* structural paths use, not a change to the hook hot path.

`scripts/register.sh "$SHELL_ROOT"` (or any path that physical-resolves to the shell root) recognizes this case and:
- skips the `workspace/<basename>` symlink (would otherwise create a directory loop);
- skips `inject_into` (the source files are the destinations);
- ensures the registry entry exists;
- ensures the committed `.claude/ghjig-root -> ..` self-symlink exists (idempotent; #539).

For target repos this is unchanged: В§3.2 inject + registry entry, both performed by `clone-into.sh` / `register.sh` as before.

### 3.7 Context lifecycle: flush вҶ’ clear вҶ’ reconstruct

The injection mechanism (В§3.2) and its runtime surfaces (В§6.4 per-turn status, В§6.5(b) session restore) are the *inbound* half of the MISSION dual вҖ” selective injection pulls durable memory into the working context. This section names the full loop they presuppose: **flush вҶ’ clear вҶ’ reconstruct**, the operational form of MISSION's `active вҶ’ archived, not active вҶ’ deleted` invariant.

A context **clear** is the bluntest narrowing tool: it discards the entire working context. Done naively it is `active вҶ’ delete` вҖ” task-scoped state that lived only in the conversation (decisions taken, the current phase, what the next step was) is lost. The MISSION invariant requires it instead be `active вҶ’ archived`: the active surface contracts, but the artifact persists in durable memory for later selective re-injection. Three steps make that hold:

1. **Flush** (the gap this section closes) вҖ” *before* a clear, distill task-scoped session state into durable memory. The flush is **explicit / skill-invoked** (`/flush`, В§5.24), not automatic. What it distills is the small, reconstructable core: the current branch, issue, PR, phase, and the next intended step вҖ” the same field set `status_compact` (`helpers/status.sh`) projects. Where it writes (durable-memory targets, in priority order):
   - the **PR body** вҖ” curated per the PR-as-living-doc rule (В§1.4), the richest task-scoped artifact when a PR exists;
   - a record under **`.claude/state/`** вҖ” the always-available target (a branch may have no PR yet), carrying the `status_compact` field set;
   - **GitHub artifacts** generally (issue/PR comments) for anything narrative that belongs on the durable record.

   The flush writes *at least one* durable artifact, so that after the clear the state is recoverable rather than gone.

2. **Clear** вҖ” the working context is discarded. The shell does **not** and **cannot** intercept Claude Code's native `/clear` (it is outside the shell boundary, В§3.4); `/flush` therefore *precedes* a clear and makes it safe, rather than replacing or wrapping it. The clear-trigger contract is **explicit only** in this revision: the operator (or a skill) decides when to clear. **Threshold-based / automatic triggering is deferred** (В§0.4) вҖ” both because the shell cannot hook the native clear, and because a wrong automatic clear has a high cost-asymmetry (В§6.0): a clear is irreversible within the session.

3. **Reconstruct** вҖ” on the next session, **SessionStart session restore (В§6.5(b))** re-injects the durable memory: the current branch's full PR body, the referenced issue body, the MISSION summary, and one `/status` snapshot (CLAUDE.md is natively loaded whole, not re-injected here); В§6.4 then keeps the per-turn surface narrow. This is the *already-built* inbound half вҖ” this section adds no new reconstruct path, deliberately, to avoid a parallel injection surface that could drift from В§6.5(b).

**Known gap (noted, not closed here):** В§6.5(b) restore re-injects the PR body, the issue body, and a `/status` snapshot вҖ” it does **not** currently read the `.claude/state/` flush record written in step 1. So when a PR exists, reconstruct is complete; on a branch with no PR yet, the `.claude/state/` record is written (the archive exists) but is not auto-re-injected at SessionStart. Closing that gap вҖ” teaching В§6.5(b) restore to read the flush record вҖ” is a follow-up, kept out of this revision to hold the change to one section + one affordance.

**Discard-boundary = Execution** (Directive #477). The flush вҶ’ clear вҶ’ reconstruct loop is the *session-level* application of the MISSION `active вҶ’ archived` invariant; the **discard boundary at the Execution unit** (В§1.2) is the *within-task* application. The within-Execution authoring churn (the Code phase's file reads, abandoned approaches, lint/smoke iterations) is `active вҶ’ delete`-able once the Code commit lands вҖ” it was never durable вҖ” while **directive-level memory is preserved** (`active вҶ’ archived`, the cross-Execution context a Directive carries). The `implementer` subagent (В§4.12) + `/implement` (В§5.28) enforce the boundary structurally: Phase C runs in the subagent's ephemeral context and only the structured result (commit + plan-deviations + discoveries) crosses back, so the churn is discarded at the Execution edge rather than flushed. This is the **default Code-phase route** (Directive #477 signal-4: the formal A/B measurement was descoped, the narrowing hypothesis adopted as operating policy on circumstantial evidence), with a **documented opt-out** for trivial / glue edits that stay in the main loop and **fail-open reversibility** as the safety valve; preserving directive-level memory across Executions is the EI-2 coding-memory loop (signal 3, closed).

---

## 4. Subagent specifications

Each agent is defined in `.claude/agents/<name>.md` as YAML frontmatter + body.

### 4.1 planner

**When**: before any code edit. Required for 3+ file changes, migrations, schema changes, API changes, or external contract changes.

**Input**: user request, linked issue body, MISSION.md, target CLAUDE.md.

**When MISSION is absent**: planner proceeds with `issue body + README + CLAUDE.md` alone. The "How this serves the mission" section is labeled `(MISSION.md absent вҖ” review /onboard stub suggestion)`. Don't synthesize a MISSION via inference.

**Output** (markdown that drops straight into the PR body):

```
## How this serves the mission
<Which MISSION.md item this contributes to>

## Plan
<Why this approach, trade-offs, decision rationale>

## Target base
<branch name; default `main`. For non-`main`, name the topic-branch / feature-branch the PR will merge into. See SPEC В§10.5.>

## Alternatives considered
- <Alternative 1>: <one-line why-not>
- <Alternative 2>: <one-line why-not>
(If the choice is forced вҖ” single viable approach вҖ” say so explicitly with a one-line justification rather than fabricating alternatives.)

## Key context
<related file:line>

## Checklist
- [ ] **Doc**: <doc update item 1>
- [ ] **Doc**: <doc update item 2>
- [ ] **Test**: <failing test item>
- [ ] **Code**: <implementation item>
- [ ] **Code**: <implementation item>

## Out of scope
<What this PR will NOT do>

## Risks
<Compatibility, performance, data, security>

## Open questions
<To be decided before proceeding>
```

Checklist order: **Doc first, Test next, Code last**. Granularity: one item вүҲ one commit вүҲ 30 min to 2 hours.

**Alternatives section is mandatory** вҖ” even when the choice feels obvious. A "no alternatives вҖ” forced choice" entry with a one-line justification is acceptable; an empty section is not. The section exists so reviewers see what was rejected and why, and so future-you can revisit the trade-off without re-running the analysis.

### 4.2 explorer

**When**: locating code, symbol lookups, "where is X defined", "who calls Y" вҖ” read-only wide search. Protects the main context.

**Constraints**: no code edits. No dumping large files. Always summarize.

**Output**:
- Definition location (`path:line`)
- Up to 5 main references (`path:line` + one-line context)
- Related modules
- If nothing found: say "not found" and suggest next searches.

### 4.3 doc-writer

**When**: Phase A. Any change that alters external surface.

**Responsibilities**:
- Identify affected SSOT docs (MISSION, README, CLAUDE.md, ARCHITECTURE, ADR, API doc).
- Patch each doc preserving its existing format and tone.
- For absent docs, propose a minimal stub only after user confirmation.
- When an irreversible decision is detected, recommend writing an ADR (`docs/ADRs/NNNN-title.md`).

**Forbidden**: inventing target SSOT content (humans must review and sign off). Only stub proposals when absent.

### 4.4 test-writer

**When**: Phase B, right after doc.

**Responsibilities**:
- Take Phase A docs / spec as input; write a failing test.
- Reuse existing test patterns, tools, fixtures.
- Cover intended behavior + at least one boundary / exception / error path.
- Run it and confirm it **fails** (intentionally). If it passes, either Phase A is wrong or the test is too weak.

**Principles**:
- Suspect over-mocking.
- One test = one assertion.
- If tooling is absent (e.g. pytest not installed), report and stop. Don't guess.

### 4.5 code-reviewer

**When**: before commit / PR. Auto-invoked by `/review`, `/ship`.

**Premise**: assume no knowledge of the main assistant's discussion or reasoning. Input is:
- The full PR diff. Prefer `gh pr diff <num>` (or `--web` equivalent) over a literal `git diff main...HEAD` вҖ” the PR's `baseRefName` may be non-`main` for topic-branch / experimental work (В§10.5), and `gh pr diff` honors that automatically. The principle is "review what the PR actually changes against its declared base," not "everything since main."
- Read-only adjacent context for changed files (for call-graph tracing, as needed) вҖ” read via `git show <HEAD_SHA>:<path>` at the resolved PR-head SHA (below), **not** from the ambient working tree
- Target `MISSION.md`, referenced issue body (for MISSION fit + acceptance criteria evaluation)
- Full PR body (for declared plan + checklist verification)

Nothing outside this input.

**Artifact resolution (canonical; #544).** A worktree-isolated reviewer (В§1.5) is checked out at the **harness-chosen base** (`origin/main`), **not** the PR head вҖ” so an ambient `git diff`/full-file read reviews the *wrong artifact* and can still emit APPROVE (observed live in PR #543: three ship reviewers ran at the base SHA while the PR head had advanced; one approved a diff it never saw). The reviewer therefore **resolves its artifact from the pushed PR head by construction**, never from the ambient worktree:
- **Head SHA**: `gh pr view <n> --json headRefOid --jq .headRefOid`.
- **Diff**: `gh pr diff <n>` (equivalently `git fetch origin refs/pull/<n>/head && git diff <base>...<HEAD_SHA>`).
- **Changed-file context**: `git show <HEAD_SHA>:<path>` вҖ” read-only git, **no checkout**. This closes the residual hole where an adjacent full-file context read would otherwise hit the stale base worktree even when the diff itself was fetched correctly.
- **`reviewed-head:` line**: the verdict's **first line** is `reviewed-head: <sha>`, the SHA the reviewer **independently derived** from the artifact it actually resolved (not one handed to it вҖ” see В§5.7 caller-side blind compare). If the reviewer cannot confirm its resolved copy equals the current PR head (a `gh`/`fetch`/resolve failure of its own), it **says so explicitly and its verdict is invalid** вҖ” an unconfirmed head is never an approve.

**Known residual (deferred, #544 follow-up вҖ” not built here).** The `reviewed-head:` line binds the *artifact the reviewer resolved*, not the *cognitive act of review* вҖ” a reviewer could resolve the head correctly yet reason over stale context. A **content-challenge** (the reviewer quotes a specific diff line the caller privately knows, binding the review act to the artifact) is the intended tightening; it is deferred to a follow-up issue, tracked here as a known limitation.

**Check**:
- Consistency (coherent changes, missing adjacent callers)
- Tests (alignment with Phase B, regression risk)
- Error handling (at boundaries only, no defensive code creep)
- Security surface
- Obvious performance traps
- Readability, naming
- Scope (extraneous changes?)
- **Doc sync (Phase A reflected?)**
- **MISSION fit (contributing to or violating which item?)**
- **Issue acceptance criteria met?**
- **Enforcement-style (В§6.0)** вҖ” *only for diffs that add/change a hook, gate, matcher, or standing guidance*: a new block must name its positive alternative and the negative/positive face must match the cost-asymmetry (В§6.0 P1 + P4); a bare block or gateless guidance is a one-sided regression. (n/a for diffs touching no enforcement surface.)

**Output**: ship / ship after fix / block. Each finding cites `path:line`.

### 4.6 security-reviewer

**When**: PRs touching auth / authz / sessions / external input / new deps / crypto / hashing / randomness / new IO boundaries.

**Input / artifact resolution**: same artifact-resolution contract as В§4.5 вҖ” resolve the diff and changed-file context from the **pushed PR head** (`gh pr view <n> --json headRefOid`, `gh pr diff <n>`, `git show <HEAD_SHA>:<path>`), never the ambient (possibly base-pinned) worktree, and emit `reviewed-head: <sha>` as the verdict's first line. An unconfirmed head вҶ’ invalid verdict. This is the reviewer whose base-pinned APPROVE in the high-asymmetry tier (В§4.11) is highest-cost, so the pin is load-bearing here.

**Check areas**: authentication / authorization, injection (SQL / shell / HTML / path), sensitive data exposure, weak crypto, CSRF / CORS / headers, dependency risk.

**Output**: High / Medium / Low / Info. Each finding: risk + exploit scenario + remediation.

### 4.7 issue-reviewer

**When**: invoked by `/file-issue` before `gh issue create`. Validates the rationale triad of SPEC В§5.2 вҖ” every issue passes through this gate.

**Input**:
- Proposed issue body (title + body + label).
- Target `MISSION.md` (if absent, label as `(MISSION.md absent вҖ” review /onboard stub suggestion)`).
- Open-issues list (`gh issue list --state open`).

**Check**:
- **MISSION fit**: does the body cite a specific MISSION item? "It's general improvement" or "tidy" answers fail.
- **Why now**: does the body explain what changes if this waits? Vague "would be nice" fails.
- **Existing-coverage**: scan open-issues / open-PRs; does another issue cover this, or would a comment on an open PR suffice? If yes вҶ’ suggest the cheaper path.
- **Acceptance criteria**: explicit, testable, вүҘ1 item.
- **Enforcement-style fit (В§6.0)** вҖ” *only when the proposed issue adds/changes a hook, gate, matcher, or standing guidance* (else n/a): the negative/positive face must match the cost of being wrong (В§6.0 P1) and a proposed block must name its alternative / proposed guidance must have a gate behind it (В§6.0 P4); a mismatch or one-sided proposal вҶ’ `refine`.

**Output**: one of three verdicts on stdout's last line, each with a one-line reason:
- `ship` вҖ” file as-is.
- `refine: <one-line why>` вҖ” return for body revision before filing.
- `block: <one-line why>` вҖ” don't file at all (existing-coverage hit, scope problem, or non-MISSION work).

Inside `attended` mode the verdict surfaces to the user; inside `unattended` mode it gates the next step directly. Hook into `attended` is non-skippable вҖ” Auto mode does not suppress this gate (SPEC В§5.2).

### 4.8 plan-reviewer (adversarial-pairing plan review, #530)

**When**: invoked by `/work-on` after the planner and the two challengers (below), to **judge the contest** and gate the plan-approval step.

**The omission bias this fixes.** Historically the `planner` authored both the Plan *and* its own `## Alternatives considered`, and `plan-reviewer` only *graded that self-curated list*. The interested party controlled the choice set, so the structural failure mode was **omission** вҖ” a genuinely superior approach the planner never surfaced could not enter the contest, and its absence was invisible from inside the loop (a "not strawmen" check catches crude weakness but not a plausible list that silently excludes the real winner). This matters most under `unattended` mode, where a clean `plan-reviewer` verdict *substitutes for human plan approval* (В§1.5, В§5.3): a reviewer grading a rigged set is a weak substitute for the human it replaces, who would have brought their own rival approach.

**Adversarial pairing (the default whenever the planner is invoked).** The planner produces **one base Plan A** and **no longer authors alternatives**. `/work-on` then runs an **upstream axis selector** and dispatches **two independent, mutually-blind `plan-challenger` agents** (В§4.8.1) on **two distinct axes**, **parallel + worktree-isolated**. Each returns exactly one of three outcomes on its axis: a plan that **dominates A**, a **genuine non-dominating alternative** (a real trade-off), or an **explicit reasoned concession** (names the axis it tried + why A held). `plan-reviewer` then **judges the three candidates {A, B1, B2}**.

**Axis selection.** The selector (homed **upstream in `/work-on`**, between the planner and the challenger dispatch вҖ” *not* inside a challenger or the reviewer, since blind challengers cannot self-coordinate distinctness and an interested agent choosing its own axis re-introduces bias) picks the **2 highest-leverage axes for this specific change** from a fixed menu: **{correctness, simplicity/maintainability, performance, security, cost/effort, robustness/risk, extensibility, UX}**, and assigns one to each challenger. **No hardcoded axis pair** вҖ” a fixed pair (e.g. simplicity+robustness) would itself be an omission mechanism, systematically excluding performance/security from ever being challenged, relocating the very bias this fixes rather than removing it.

**Why this is a DEFAULT, not gated (the В§4.11 relationship вҖ” both legs required, do not state only one):**
1. **Generation diversity вү  vote redundancy.** В§4.11's "N-way independent voting is blast-radius-gated, *never* a default" governs **vote redundancy** вҖ” N copies of *one* reviewer casting approve-verdicts that tally to a majority gate, where correlated votes de-risk nothing. #530 is **generation diversity** вҖ” *distinct authors* producing *distinct artifacts* for *one* judge, with no vote tally. В§4.11's correlated-vote caution does not reach it.
2. **Isolation protects the acting context, not the token budget.** MISSION narrowing protects the **acting/working context** (what the parent loop holds), not total token spend. `plan-challenger`s are **worktree-isolated subagents**: they spend tokens in *their own* contexts and return only **distilled verdicts** to the parent вҖ” so two challengers do **not** grow the acting context. The honest residual is higher *total tokens* + ~1 parallel planner-latency; that is a favorable trade for the **plan artifact, whose blast radius governs all downstream code** вҖ” the highest-leverage artifact in the flow.

**Guards (both challenger outcomes can degenerate; the judge rejects both):**
- **Lazy concession** вҖ” a concession is valid **only if** it names the axis tried + why A held; an empty "A is fine" is rejected (rubber-stamp regression).
- **Fake-diff** вҖ” a "different-but-worse" plan that does not actually dominate resolves to **A stands** (the inverse strawman).

**Shared-blindspot check** вҖ” the reviewer reads the code/issue directly. Scoped to same-model prior correlation (A/B1/B2 on one model can share a blindspot вҖ” adversarial structure breaks *framing* bias, not *shared-prior* blindness) **and** the N>2 residual (a change with 3+ live axes that 2 challengers cannot cover). It is **not** a substitute for a systematically-omitted axis вҖ” the upstream selector, not this backstop, is what prevents systematic omission.

**Input**: the base Plan A (markdown); the two challenger outputs {B1, B2} with their assigned axes; the issue body; target `MISSION.md`.

**Check**:
- **Judge the contest {A, B1, B2}**: pick the winner; or declare **A forced / high-confidence** when both challengers fail to beat it (both concede or fake-diff); or **surface a genuine trade-off** (attended: to the user; unattended: resolve per mode) when no candidate dominates. Verify challenger **genuineness** (reject lazy-concession; fake-diff вҶ’ A-stands).
- **Scope hygiene**: items in `Checklist` map to `Acceptance criteria`; anything orphaned belongs in `Out of scope` or a follow-up issue.
- **Phase-order sanity**: Doc вҶ’ Test вҶ’ Code per В§1.2; relaxation reasons noted if applicable.
- **Target base fit**: the `Target base` field (В§4.1) names a branch; a `main`-default plan proposing experimental-base work (or vice versa) fails.
- **Enforcement-style fit (В§6.0)** вҖ” *only when the plan introduces/changes a hook, gate, matcher, or standing guidance* (else n/a): face must match the cost of being wrong (P1), a planned block names its alternative / guidance has a gate (P4).

**Output**: the same three verdicts as `issue-reviewer` вҖ” **the `^VERDICT: (ship|refine|block)` grammar is unchanged** (the 3-way adjudication collapses to these three tokens: a winning challenger or a surfaced trade-off вҶ’ `refine` carrying the winner/trade-off forward; A-stands вҶ’ `ship`). `refine` causes `/work-on` to re-run the contest with the feedback; `block` stops with a comment on the issue.

**Non-adopted / subsumed (recorded so a future edit cannot silently reintroduce them):**
- **naive parallel-independence** (N identical-prompt planners) вҖ” **non-adopted**: identical prompts on one model converge (correlated draws), buying redundancy without diversity. The diversity mechanism is *distinct-axis mutual-blindness*, not repetition.
- **reviewer-steelman-only** (the judge authors its own single rival) вҖ” **subsumed**: two *independent* challengers steelman better than a judge authoring the rival it then adjudicates (which re-introduces a milder interested-party bias). The reviewer's code-read survives only as the shared-blindspot *backstop*, not as the primary rival source.
- **N>2 challengers / more axes** вҖ” a **deferred future В§4.11-style high-asymmetry escalation** (for a change with 3+ live axes); no gate is built now, and the shared-blindspot check backstops the N>2 residual in the interim.

#### 4.8.1 plan-challenger

**When**: dispatched by `/work-on` (Г—2, parallel + worktree-isolated) after the planner and axis selection, before `plan-reviewer`.

**Mandate**: **beat Plan A** on the single **axis passed by the caller**. Mutually blind (no visibility into the other challenger). Return one of: **dominates-A** (a superior plan on the axis) / **genuine non-dominating alternative** (a real trade-off) / **reasoned concession** (names the axis tried + why A held вҖ” a bare "A is fine" is rejected downstream). Never manufacture a different-but-worse plan to avoid conceding (the fake-diff the judge resolves to A-stands).

**Working-tree discipline**: read-only-by-intent, invoked with worktree-isolation and constrained to read-only git вҖ” same posture as the other read-only reviewers (В§1.5, #285). Tools: `Read, Grep, Glob, Bash`.

**Session-restart caveat (В§4.9.3)**: `plan-challenger` is a new `subagent_type`; until the next session restart `/work-on` routes it through `general-purpose`. Its prompt is **self-describing** (it instructs `general-purpose` to behave as `plan-challenger`) so the fallback is functionally complete; restart is canonical.

### 4.9 Director subagents

The dir-mode workflow (В§1.7) uses one reviewer subagent (`activation-reviewer`, В§4.9.1). A second (`roadmap-reviewer`, В§4.9.2) is documented for future activation.

#### 4.9.1 activation-reviewer

**When**: invoked by `/file-directive` (proposed Directive body, В§5.10), `/activate` (re-check on the possibly-edited body before ProposedвҶ’Active, and on unblock, В§5.12), `/revise-directive` (the new body before replacement, В§5.16), and `/complete-directive` (completion claim + linked-Execution-Issue evidence, В§5.13); and вҖ” via the Initiative rulebook вҖ” by `/consume-initiative` (contract-evaluability at Initiative intake, extraction-faithfulness on the proposed Directive set, В§5.21). Mirrors the structure of `issue-reviewer` (В§4.7) and `plan-reviewer` (В§4.8) вҖ” review only, never authors content.

**Type-label dispatch**: `activation-reviewer` is **type-neutral** вҖ” it resolves the reviewed Issue's type label and applies the matching rulebook. The `directive` label present вҶ’ the Directive checks below. The `initiative` label present (#254, M2) вҶ’ the **Initiative rulebook** (contract-evaluability вҖ” the termination condition must be evaluable without code knowledge; and extraction-faithfulness вҖ” extracted Directives decompose the termination condition without smuggling strategy); the reviewer never activates or mutates an Initiative (the shell consumes them), it judges the Initiative/extraction as input for the M3 consume flow. Absent (an Execution Issue, `task`/`bug`) вҶ’ an Execution rulebook (schema completeness, acceptance-criteria verifiability, scope clarity, MISSION fit, duplicate coverage; **parent-fit is gated by label** вҖ” applied only to the `execution` type, while `task`/`bug` are standalone per the В§1.7 `execution`/`task`/`bug` type-label definitions and skip the parent checks and the Parent-mismatch matrix). For a Directive, the **alignment check branches on parent kind** (#254): a `## MISSION fit` MISSION-section parent is judged against MISSION; a line-1 `Parent Initiative: #N` parent is judged against that Initiative's termination condition (the parent-XOR guarantees exactly one). The **reviewer verdict vocabulary** (#172, canonical here): `activation-reviewer` вҶ’ `pass` / `revise` / `reject`, while `issue-reviewer` (В§4.7) and `plan-reviewer` (В§4.8) retain `ship` / `refine` / `block` 1:1 (out of #172's scope) вҖ” uniform across both `activation-reviewer` rulebooks; only the *checks* differ by type. The structured refile fields and the type-mismatch / parent-mismatch matrices apply on `reject`.

**Input**:

- **For proposal review:** the proposed Directive body (objective, success signals, non-goals, constraints, and the parent вҖ” a `## MISSION fit` field **or** a line-1 `Parent Initiative: #N` marker, В§1.7), plus the list of currently `Status=Active` Directives (via `gh issue list --label directive --label '-status:proposed' --state open` вҖ” Issues are the SSOT; the Project is a lagging derived view and is NOT consulted, В§1.7/В§5.11).
- **For completion review:** the Directive's body (success signals as written at activation), the list of linked Execution Issues (Issues with `Parent` = this Directive), and their close states / AC ticks.

**Checks**:

- **Schema completeness** вҖ” does the body cover objective / success signals / non-goals / constraints / MISSION fit (or, for an Initiative-parented Directive, a `Parent Initiative: #N` marker)? Missing any вҶ’ `revise`.
- **Parent-kind alignment** (#254) вҖ” a Directive has exactly one parent kind; judge alignment against it: a `## MISSION fit` parent against the named MISSION section, a line-1 `Parent Initiative: #N` parent against that Initiative's termination condition. Both-or-neither parent kind вҶ’ `revise` (the parent-XOR, В§1.7). The full per-check detail is in the contract SSOT `.claude/agents/activation-reviewer.md` (check 1.5).
- **Success-signal verifiability** вҖ” are signals objectively testable, or vague aspiration? "Engineering reviews go faster" without a metric вҶ’ `revise`.
- **Scope clarity** вҖ” is the objective bounded? "Improve the codebase" вҶ’ `reject`.
- **Non-goal clarity** вҖ” are exclusions explicit or implied? Vague exclusions invite scope creep.
- **Active-Directive conflict** вҖ” does the proposed Directive overlap with an existing `Status=Active` Directive? If yes вҶ’ `revise` or `reject` with a pointer.
- **Evidence sufficiency (completion only)** вҖ” do the linked Execution Issues collectively satisfy each success signal? A signal with no linked Execution Issue вҶ’ `revise` ("need engineering evidence"). A signal whose Execution Issues are open or stalled вҶ’ `revise`.

**Output** вҖ” three verdicts: `pass` / `revise` / `reject` (the **reviewer verdict vocabulary** above). On `reject` the verdict additionally carries the structured refile fields (`verdict` / `reason` / `refile-target-type` / `refile-target-parent` / `refile-body-draft`) and follows the type-mismatch / parent-mismatch matrices. The full output contract вҖ” verdict meanings, the `revise`-vs-`reject` boundary rule, the structured fields, both matrices, the `<!-- activation-verdict: <verdict> -->` marker, and the N=3 `revise`вҶ’`reject` escalation вҖ” is specified in `.claude/agents/activation-reviewer.md` (the contract SSOT). Callers apply the post-verdict handling per В§2.1 (Directive lifecycle) and В§5.12 (`/activate`).

**Rules**: do not author body content for a `revise` (matches В§4.7 rule; the one exception is the `reject` `refile-body-draft` field вҖ” drafting there IS the preserve signal). Verdict is content-only; filer identity affects only the caller's post-verdict handling. Judge from the inputs above only. Auto-approving without scanning active-Directive conflicts is a regression against the В§1.5 reviewer-pattern integrity.

#### 4.9.2 roadmap-reviewer (deferred)

Cross-Directive coherence check вҖ” MISSION alignment, Directive sequencing, drift detection. Deferred until operating experience surfaces the friction; see MISSION's "Success looks like" вҶ’ orchestrator criterion.

#### 4.9.3 Session-restart caveat for new reviewer subagents

Claude Code enumerates available `subagent_type` values **at session start** by scanning `.claude/agents/*.md`. A reviewer added mid-session is **not routable** as a first-class subagent until the next session start: `Agent({subagent_type: "<new-name>"})` falls back to `general-purpose`, which loses the Type-aware specialized prompt.

This caveat is the parallel of В§6.1's "Session-restart caveat for hook-spec changes" вҖ” Claude Code binds its routing surfaces (hook configuration AND subagent enumeration) at session start. Both bindings are stable for the session's duration; both are picked up automatically at the next session.

Empirical confirmation (Directive #62 / PR #67-followup): in the dogfood session, `.claude/agents/directive-reviewer.md` landed via PR #50 mid-session (this reviewer was later renamed to `activation-reviewer` by Issue #170 under Directive #167; the historical filename is retained here because it records the actual PR #50 event). Every subsequent `Agent({subagent_type: "directive-reviewer"})` invocation routed through `general-purpose` because the harness's `subagent_type` enumeration had been frozen against the pre-#50 state. A session restart resolves this automatically вҖ” no `.claude/settings.json` registration needed, no harness-config change. The same mechanism applies to the Issue #170 rename itself: until a session restart, `subagent_type: "activation-reviewer"` falls back to `general-purpose`.

**Mitigation for the in-session window**: the falling-back-to-`general-purpose` path is functionally complete вҖ” the agent's prompt instructs `general-purpose` to behave as the new reviewer. The cost is the loss of Type-aware specialization (the harness's per-subagent prompt + tool restriction). Acceptable for one session; restart at session end is canonical.

**Hook-side note**: the smoke `В§42` structural assertions (PR #50) lock the agent file's shape, so the routing-layer regression is the only failure mode this caveat names. The behavioral surface that catches the routing regression is **smoke В§42e** (issue #69, under Directive #62; extended for the type-neutral reviewer by #170): three assertions gated behind `GHJIG_BEHAVIORAL_SMOKE=1` invoke `activation-reviewer` with a synthetic minimal-but-valid Directive body (asserting `^VERDICT: pass`), a synthetic Directive body missing the `## Success signals` section (asserting `^VERDICT: (revise|reject)`), and a synthetic minimal-but-valid Execution Issue body exercising the Execution-rulebook dispatch (asserting `^VERDICT: pass`). Env-var unset вҶ’ В§42e is a no-op so default smoke stays deterministic and offline; env-var set вҶ’ the block exercises the live `subagent_type: "activation-reviewer"` route end-to-end. A regression in either the agent file or the routing surface flips at least one of the three verdicts.

> **В§4.10 triage classifier вҖ” retired (#173, Directive #167).** The former triage classifier agent was deleted: its `status:proposed` substantive gate is now `activation-reviewer` (В§4.9), and its template-shape classification is absorbed by `/activate`'s type-mismatch matrix. `/triage` survives only as a one-cycle deprecation alias (see В§5.12). The `triage` audit category is retained in В§2.1 as append-only history. (The В§4.10 number is retired and not reused; the high-asymmetry reviewer tier below is **В§4.11**.)

### 4.11 High-asymmetry reviewer tier (Issue #428)

A cross-cutting reviewer **tier**, not a subagent: where a wrong *approve* is irreversible or corrupts shared history, a single reviewer's verdict is replaced by an **N-way independent vote**. This is the reviewer-side counterpart of В§6.0 P1 вҖ” the same cost-asymmetry that makes the protected-branch / secret matchers hard negative gates makes these *approvals* warrant redundancy. It is **blast-radius-gated, never a default**: N-way everywhere would bloat the acting context (the narrowing principle, MISSION) and correlate votes, so the common path stays single-reviewer. It extends the existing conditional dispatch (`/ship` step 2 already spawns `security-reviewer` only when the diff touches a security surface).

**Enumerated high-asymmetry decision set** (closed вҖ” `is_high_asymmetry <kind>` in `helpers/blast_radius.sh` returns rc 0 for exactly these, rc 1 otherwise):
- `merge-security-surface` вҖ” `gh pr merge` to the default branch of a PR whose diff touches a security surface (the В§4.6 trigger), at `/ship`.
- `force-push` вҖ” a force-push / history-rewrite judgment surfaced *inside the `/ship` motion* (the В§13 rebase-pull tail or a named-branch escape). This is the **reviewer judgment** when a force-push is legitimately part of shipping вҖ” distinct from the autopilot force-push **negative gate** (В§6.1), which still blocks unreviewed force-pushes independently.
- `directive-completion` вҖ” the `/complete-directive` evidence evaluation (В§5.13).
- `irreversible-adr` вҖ” merging a PR carrying an ADR (`docs/ADRs/`) to the default branch, at `/ship`. ADR *authoring* via `/adr` is a reversible doc-write (the file is editable until merged); the irreversible point is the merge, so the tier fires there, not in `/adr`.

**Mechanism вҖ” N=3, majority=2, independent.** For a high-asymmetry decision the invoking skill spawns the relevant reviewer type (`security-reviewer` for `merge-security-surface`/`force-push`, `activation-reviewer` for `directive-completion`, `code-reviewer` for `irreversible-adr`) **three times as independent fresh subagent invocations** вҖ” worktree-isolated, artifact-only (the В§4.5 "no knowledge of the main assistant's discussion" premise), with **no shared context** between the three. **Independence is load-bearing**: redundancy de-risks only if the votes don't correlate through a shared prime вҖ” a serial debate where each reviewer sees the others' verdicts is explicitly *not* this (it is the rejected design).

**Fixed-denominator tally (#544).** The denominator is **fixed at 3**; majority = **2 valid approve-verdicts of 3**. A vote is *valid* only if the reviewer's independently-reported `reviewed-head` (В§4.5) matches the caller's privately-held expected head (В§5.7 blind compare); a mismatch, absent, or unconfirmed head is a **non-approve invalid vote вҖ” fail-closed, never counted as APPROVE**. An invalid vote is **not an abstention that lowers the bar**: it still consumes one of the three slots, so two invalid votes make majority unreachable (max 1 valid approve) вҮ’ non-majority вҮ’ `hard` blocker вҮ’ park. The bar is always 2-of-3, never 2-of-(valid votes).

This **parallel** N=3 is distinct from В§4.9.1's **serial** N=3 (the `revise`вҶ’`reject` escalation, which counts *consecutive revise verdicts on one reviewer across rounds*). Here the three are simultaneous, independent, and tally to one gate decision; there one reviewer is re-consulted over time.

**Mode coupling** (В§5.7.1): in `unattended`, the majority tally gates directly (it substitutes for the human exactly as a single reviewer's verdict does). A non-majority on a high-asymmetry decision is a **`hard` blocker** вҖ” unfixable without a product decision вҖ” so `/ship` parks (В§5.7.1 hard-blocker path) for human adjudication; the park is the named next action (В§6.0 P4), not a bare refusal.

**Fail-open** (В§4.9.3 / В§6.1 session-restart caveat): `is_high_asymmetry` is sourced via `safe_source`; on a miss (the helper absent in a pre-#428 session) the gated decision **degrades to a single reviewer** with an `audit_log warn reviewer-tier` record вҖ” never a lockout. A wrong *degrade* costs the redundancy on one decision (recoverable); a lockout would block all shipping (not) вҖ” the asymmetry that picks fail-open.

### 4.12 implementer (Issue #486; Directive #477)

**When**: Phase C (Code), **by default** вҖ” `/work-on` routes the Code phase here via `/implement` (В§5.28). The **opt-out** is for trivial / one-line / glue edits and the orchestrator's own glue (Directive #477 Non-goal 2), which the main assistant authors directly in its own loop. The default-flip is Directive #477 **signal-4**: the formal A/B measurement was descoped and the context-narrowing hypothesis (В§1.2 / В§3.7) adopted as operating policy on circumstantial evidence, hedged by fail-open reversibility (a missing implementer path degrades to main-loop authoring) rather than a measured result.

**Premise**: the write-capable counterpart of the artifact-only reviewers (В§4.5). It implements strictly from a supplied **manifest** and has **no knowledge of the main assistant's conversation** вҖ” the same "judge/act from the artifact, not the discussion" discipline, applied to authoring rather than review.

**Input = manifest** (the caller assembles it, В§5.28): the **Plan** (PR-body / planner output), the **failing Phase-B test** + how to run it, the **named relevant file paths**, and the **directive-level learnings** вҖ” the distilled `### Learnings for the next Execution` blocks `/work-on` (В§5.3 step 4.5) reads back from the parent Directive's `/reflect` comments (В§5.15) and injects as **advisory context** (closes Directive #477 signal 3). If the Plan or the failing test is missing, the manifest is incomplete вҖ” the subagent reports and stops rather than inferring the intent; the directive-level learnings field is **optional** (advisory; its absence does not make the manifest incomplete).

**Output = structured return** (and nothing else): exactly (a) the commit / diff ref(s) authored, (b) plan-deviations (where/why it diverged from the Plan), and (c) discoveries (signal worth surfacing). The file reads, abandoned approaches, and lint/smoke iterations stay in the subagent's **ephemeral context** and are not returned вҖ” that churn-discard is the point (the within-Execution authoring churn never re-enters the parent context).

**Norms**: follows Doc вҶ’ Test вҶ’ Code (it is the Code phase вҖ” Doc/Test already exist, do not re-author them), commit-format (В§10.2), and authors its commit in the **work language** (В§5.7.2). Working-tree discipline (#285): write-capable, but git is constrained to its own `add`/`commit` вҖ” stage **only the manifest-named paths** (`git add <those paths>`); **never** `git add -A`/`-u` (a blanket stage sweeps in the parent's uncommitted work), and never a tree-mutating git command (`checkout`/`restore`/`stash`/`reset`/`clean`) that touches it. Because the implementer is **not** worktree-isolated (its commit must land on the PR branch, В§1.5), this path-scoped-add discipline is the substitute for isolation; the caller also surfaces a dirty tree before dispatch (В§5.28).

**В§4.9.3 caveat**: a freshly-added `subagent_type: implementer` falls back to `general-purpose` until the next session restart; `implementer.md`'s self-describing prompt makes that fallback functionally complete (the Type-aware tool restriction is the only loss), restart is canonical.

---

## 5. Slash commands

### 5.0 `/bootstrap-repo`

**When**: once, on a brand-new target that has **no default branch** вҖ” an empty GitHub repo (zero commits) or a greenfield local directory freshly `git init`'d (unborn HEAD). This is **stage-0**: it precedes `/onboard` (В§5.1). The adoption lifecycle (`clone-into.sh` вҶ’ `register.sh` вҶ’ `/onboard` вҶ’ `/onboard-dir-mode`, В§2) presupposes a default branch with at least one commit already exists; `/bootstrap-repo` is the step that produces it, so there is an owner for the no-default-branch starting state rather than ad-hoc manual git.

**Precondition**: the target has no commits / no default branch. If a default branch already exists (`git rev-parse --verify HEAD` succeeds), `/bootstrap-repo` **refuses** вҖ” the repo is already past stage-0 and `/onboard` is the right entry point.

**Outputs**: a default branch (`main`) carrying a single seed commit вҖ” `MISSION.md` from `.claude/templates/mission.md` and `README.md` from `.claude/templates/readme_for_target.md` вҖ” pushed to the remote so the repo is ready for `/onboard`. Stage-0 seeds only these two SSOT files; `.github/` templates, labels, and substrate remain `/onboard` / `/onboard-dir-mode` concerns (В§5.1, В§1.7).

**The bootstrap exception (target repos).** The protected-branch gate is name-based (`PROTECTED_BRANCH_PATTERN`, В§6.1): on an unborn HEAD, `git symbolic-ref --short HEAD` returns `main` (rc=0) while `git rev-parse --verify HEAD` fails, so `is_protected_branch()` matches by name and the seed commit (and the Edit/Write that authors `MISSION.md`/`README.md` on that branch) is blocked вҖ” correct, desirable behavior for the general case. `/bootstrap-repo` owns the **narrowly-scoped** exception for *this one seed commit only* вҖ” it does **not** weaken the gate. **In-agent escape (В§7):** the two in-command forms are stripped before the hook in the live Bash tool, so they cannot disarm the seed commit. `/bootstrap-repo` instead writes a `branch`-category **file-based skip token** immediately before the seed commit вҖ” `scripts/ghjig_skip.sh branch '<seed-commit-subject>' '<reason>'` вҖ” and the seed commit then succeeds **in-agent** (the hook reads the token at fire time, audits it, and consumes it). The seed-commit subject is the high-entropy fingerprint:

```
scripts/ghjig_skip.sh branch 'chore: seed first commit (MISSION + README)' 'stage-0-bootstrap-seed-on-unborn-HEAD'
git commit -m "chore: seed first commit (MISSION + README)"
```

Running the seed commit in a **real terminal** (no hook in the path, the commit succeeds directly) remains the fallback. Either way the bypass routes through `should_skip branch` and is recorded in `audit.jsonl`. This generalizes the **shell's own-repo** first-commit exception (В§16 item 15) to *target* repos: both are the same chicken-and-egg case (the first commit cannot ride a flow that presupposes a prior commit).

**Steps**:

1. **Preflight** вҖ” refuse if `git rev-parse --verify HEAD` succeeds (already has commits) with `"target already has a default branch вҖ” run /onboard, not /bootstrap-repo"`. Refuse if not inside a git work tree.
2. **Seed SSOT** вҖ” copy `MISSION.md` from `.claude/templates/mission.md` (a draft for the user to complete) and `README.md` from `.claude/templates/readme_for_target.md`, **via a Bash file copy** (`cp`), not the Edit/Write tool. The Edit/Write protected-branch arm (В§6.1) blocks writes on the unborn-HEAD `main` and cannot be disarmed by a trailing sentinel (there is no command string to carry it); a `cp` into the registered target path carries no protected-branch check and is in-scope, so it is the correct seeding path.
3. **Seed commit** вҖ” `git add MISSION.md README.md`, write the `branch`-category file token (`scripts/ghjig_skip.sh branch '<seed-commit-subject>' '<reason>'`, В§7), then run the seed commit above **in-agent** (the hook reads, audits, and consumes the token at fire time). Running it in a **real terminal** is the fallback. The seed commit message is a `chore` (no issue # required вҖ” there is no issue tracker state yet).
4. **Publish** вҖ” `git push -u origin main` (GitHub adopts the first pushed branch as the repo default).
5. **Handoff** вҖ” print `Next: /onboard` so the operator continues into the read-only onboarding check.

**Forbidden**:
- Running on a repo that already has a default branch (preflight refuses).
- Bypassing the protected-branch gate for anything other than the single seed commit вҖ” the exception is scoped to stage-0, not a general escape.
- Mutating `/onboard`'s responsibilities (`.github/`, labels, substrate) вҖ” stage-0 seeds only `MISSION.md` + `README.md`.

### 5.1 `/onboard`

**When**: once, right after a target repo is first cloned. **Precedes**: stage-0 `/bootstrap-repo` (В§5.0) must already have produced a default branch вҖ” `/onboard` is a read-only check and assumes a seedable, cloned, registered repo; a brand-new target with no default branch goes through В§5.0 first.

**Steps**:

1. **Upstream check** вҖ” `gh repo view --json isFork,parent`. Fork вҶ’ block.
2. **Permission check** вҖ” push permission required. Missing вҶ’ advise and block.
3. **Target SSOT check**:
   - `MISSION.md` present? Absent вҶ’ strong warning + draft proposal from `.claude/templates/mission.md` (no auto-create).
   - `SPEC.md` present? `SPEC.md` is **required for any project that carries code** (В§1.3) вҖ” it is the behavioural SSOT, so requiredness keys on the presence of code, not on whether an external contract (CLI, API, schema, protocol) exists. Absent on a code-carrying project вҶ’ scaffold the slot from `.claude/templates/spec.md` (no auto-authoring of contract content вҖ” the MISSION boundary).
   - Report `README.md`, `CLAUDE.md`, `docs/ARCHITECTURE.md` presence.
4. **`.github/` check**:
   - `ISSUE_TEMPLATE/` absent вҶ’ suggest shell template.
   - `PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE.md` absent вҶ’ suggest shell template.
   - `CODEOWNERS` absent вҶ’ recommend.
5. **Branch protection check** вҖ” `gh api repos/{owner}/{repo}/branches/main/protection`. Report missing items (PR required, review required, status checks required, force push blocked). Setup requires admin, so just print commands.
6. **CI presence** вҖ” check `.github/workflows/`. Absent вҶ’ recommend appropriate workflows.

No automatic changes. All recommendations require human review and execution.

### 5.2 `/file-issue [--quick] <description>`

**Steps**:
- Confirm title, body, label with the user.
- Force MISSION reference and acceptance criteria in the body.
- **Rationale check** (before `gh issue create`): surface (a) which MISSION item this serves, (b) why now vs later, (c) whether an existing issue or an open-PR follow-up note would suffice. If any of (a)вҖ“(c) is weak, refine the issue or drop the request instead of filing. The check is mandatory вҖ” Auto / unattended mode does not skip it; a poorly-justified issue propagates downstream into planner output and merged code, where the cost of redirection is highest.
- **Reviewer gate**: invoke `issue-reviewer` (В§4.7) on the proposed body before `gh issue create`. In `attended` mode the verdict surfaces to the user (who may override); in `unattended` mode the verdict gates the next step (`ship` вҶ’ proceed; `refine` вҶ’ re-author the body with the feedback and re-invoke; `block` вҶ’ stop and surface the reason). The reviewer fills the human-confirm slot when no human is present. On a **non-pass** verdict the invoking flow emits a categorized reject-audit record (`issue-review`/`plan-review`/`activation` category + a reason-class token; the contract lives in В§6.1, #361) вҖ” this applies to every reviewer gate in the command family (issue-reviewer here, plan-reviewer В§5.3, activation-reviewer В§5.12/В§5.13), feeding the `scripts/promotion_candidates.sh` consumer.
- `--quick`: one-line issue (label `bug`) for fast creation. Rationale check + reviewer gate still required, in compressed form (one-line "serves X mission item, blocks Y" suffices). The `bug` label matches the `bug-report.yml` Issue Form template.
- **Directive parenting** (added by tracking #41 child #6, issue #47): when the new Issue is parented to a `Status=Active` Directive (via `--parent <directive-id>` or interactive prompt listing active Directives, В§1.7), prepend the `Parent Directive: #N` body marker (line 1); the Project `Parent` field is **derived** from that marker by `issues-to-project-mirror.yml` вҖ” `/file-issue` writes the Issue only, never the Project directly (В§1.7 Issues-as-SSOT). `--no-parent` opts out. Rationale check + `issue-reviewer` gate apply unchanged вҖ” parenting is metadata, not part of the rationale triad.
- **Full-symmetry stamp** (#172): `gh issue create` applies the `status:proposed` label so every new Execution Issue enters the lifecycle as Proposed and requires `/activate <N>` (В§5.12) before it is actionable. This is why `issue-reviewer` (author-side, here) and `activation-reviewer` (observer-side, at `/activate`) are complementary, not redundant (В§2.1). The output `Next:` line points at `/activate <N>`. `/work-on` against a `status:proposed` Issue is blocked by `proposed-protect` (В§6.1) until activation.
- **Priority** (#291; parity with `/file-directive`, В§5.10): `/file-issue` captures a `P0`/`P1`/`P2`/`P3` priority and applies it as a label at create time, so an Issue never lands priority-less (a priority-less backlog can't be triaged). Source order: an explicit `--priority P<N>` flag вҶ’ else **ask the user** in `attended` mode вҶ’ else **default `P2`** in `unattended` mode (the same default `/file-directive` uses). The `P<N>` label is **graceful-degradation guarded** вҖ” applied only if present on the target (tier вүҘ 2), else a warn and file-without-it вҖ” and the priority is also recorded in the `issue-file` audit line so it survives a degraded label. An Execution Issue carries its own priority (it does not silently inherit the parent Directive's).
- Call `gh issue create`, return the number.

### 5.3 `/work-on <issue#> [--base <branch>]`

**Steps**:

1. `gh issue view <#> --json title,body,labels,comments` вҖ” read the issue.
2. Validate body вҖ” if acceptance criteria are missing or vague, ask the user to fix it. **Don't start work with an ambiguous goal.**
3. Resolve the **target base** (default `main`; override via `--base <branch>`). `git fetch origin && git checkout <base> && git pull --ff-only`. If `<base>` is not `main` and is not reachable locally or remotely, fail with a clear message вҖ” `/work-on` does NOT auto-create alternate bases (see В§10.5).
4. Create branch:
   ```
   USER=$(gh api user --jq .login)
   TYPE=<detected type>
   SLUG=<kebab of issue title>
   git checkout -b "${USER}/${TYPE}/${ISSUE}-${SLUG}"
   ```
   If the branch already exists on remote: `git pull --ff-only origin <branch>`.
4.5. **Read back directive-level learnings** (closes Directive #477 signal 3 вҖ” the directive-level coding-memory loop). When the Issue body carries a `Parent Directive: #N` marker (line 1, В§5.2), read the accumulated `### Learnings for the next Execution` blocks from #N's enriched `/reflect` comments (В§5.15) and inject them as **advisory context** into (a) the planner input (step 5) and (b) the `directive-level learnings` field of the `/implement` manifest (В§4.12). Advisory only вҖ” context the next Execution starts from, never a gate; absent/empty learnings (no parent Directive, or no enriched reflections yet) is a normal no-op. This is the *read* half of the loop `/reflect`'s Learnings section (В§5.15) writes.
5. Invoke `planner` agent (with issue body + MISSION + target CLAUDE.md context + the resolved `<base>` + the step-4.5 directive-level learnings when present). The planner produces **one base Plan A** and **no longer authors `## Alternatives considered`** вҖ” the interested party no longer controls the choice set (В§4.8). Its output must include the mandatory `## Target base` section (В§4.1); the `Target base` value must equal the `<base>` passed in.
5.5. **Axis selection.** Run the lightweight **upstream axis selector** (homed here, between the planner and the challenger dispatch вҖ” *not* inside a challenger or the reviewer, since mutually-blind challengers cannot self-coordinate distinctness): pick the **2 highest-leverage axes for this specific change** from the fixed menu **{correctness, simplicity/maintainability, performance, security, cost/effort, robustness/risk, extensibility, UX}**, and assign one to each challenger. **No hardcoded axis pair** (a fixed pair would relocate the omission bias by systematically excluding performance/security вҖ” В§4.8).
5.6. **Challenger dispatch.** Dispatch **two independent, mutually-blind `plan-challenger` agents** (В§4.8.1), **parallel + worktree-isolated**, one assigned axis each. Each attempts to **beat Plan A** and returns one of: **dominates-A**, a **genuine non-dominating alternative**, or a **reasoned concession** (names the axis tried + why A held). This step **rides the existing planner gate** вҖ” it fires exactly when the planner is invoked (non-trivial changes), never on trivial/glue edits; there is **no new tier gate and no `blast_radius` involvement**.
6. **Reviewer gate**: invoke `plan-reviewer` (В§4.8) to **judge the contest {A, B1, B2}** вҖ” the base Plan A plus the two challenger outputs with their assigned axes. Parse the verdict line (`^VERDICT: (ship|refine|block)`). In `attended` mode the verdict surfaces to the user; in `unattended` mode it gates the next step (`ship` вҶ’ step 7; `refine` вҶ’ re-run the contest with the feedback, then re-review; `block` вҶ’ stop with a comment on the issue naming the structural problem). On any non-pass verdict the flow emits the categorized reviewer-reject-audit record (В§6.1). The reviewer substitutes for the human reviewer when no human is present.
7. **Wait for user approval of the plan.** Approval requires an **approach check**: confirm with the user that the winning candidate from the contest record (A / B1 / B2 / verdict) is the right one, not just that a plan exists. In `unattended` mode, a clean `plan-reviewer` verdict from step 6 counts as approval.
8. **Write and commit Phase A (Doc)** вҖ” the first commit on the branch is real Doc work, never an empty seed. The branch graph begins with content the PR Plan describes, not a placeholder.
   ```
   # вҖҰedit the SSOTs identified by the plan (MISSION, README, CLAUDE.md, ARCHITECTURE, ADR)вҖҰ
   git add <changed SSOTs>
   git commit -m "<type>(#<#>): <subject>

   {Closes|Refs} #<#>"
   git push -u origin HEAD
   gh pr create --draft --base "<base>" --title "<type>(#<#>): <subject>" --body "<template>"
   ```
   First-line trailer: use `Closes #<#>` when `<base>` is the repo's **default branch** (resolved via `gh repo view --json defaultBranchRef`, not a hardcoded `main` вҖ” #504); otherwise use `Refs #<#>` (per В§10.4 вҖ” the issue closes only when work reaches the default branch, which is `main` on most repos but `master`/other elsewhere).

   If the planner's Phase A isn't ready to commit (e.g. blocked on clarification), defer the PR вҖ” keep the issue + plan in conversation. **Never fall back to an empty seed commit just to open the draft PR.**
9. Insert plan + checklist + ship gate sections in the PR body.
10. Sync internal TaskList with the checklist.
11. Continue with the next phase (Test).

### 5.4 `/sync-pr`

Explicit entry point for updating the PR body. The main assistant does this automatically; this command lets the user trigger it on demand. After a successful sync, `/sync-pr` references `/replan-check` (В§5.26) as a post-sync advisory step вҖ” the body was just curated, the natural cadence to compare it against the actual diff for structural divergence.

Refetch the remote body once before updating. The shell stores the SHA-256 of the last body it saw at `.claude/state/pr-cache/<owner>%2F<repo>__pr-<n>.json` (the `/` between owner and repo is URL-encoded as `%2F` so `<owner>/<repo>` slug boundaries survive the filename); the file holds at least `last_seen_body_sha256`, `last_synced_head`, and `last_synced_at`. If the remote body's SHA differs from `last_seen_body_sha256`, an external edit happened (reviewer, parallel session, GitHub UI) вҖ” the automatic update aborts with a stderr message naming the conflict, and merging is the human's call. After a successful sync the cache is rewritten. A corrupt cache file (unparseable / missing key) also aborts the sync rather than silently treating as "first sync."

The cache lives under `.claude/state/`, which is gitignored вҖ” it's per-clone state, not part of the repo's history. The helper `.claude/hooks/helpers/pr_cache.sh` exports `pr_cache_read`, `pr_cache_write`, and `pr_cache_check`. The repo slug is derived from `gh repo view` of the cwd, overridable via `$PR_CACHE_REPO` (used by the smoke test suite). `/ship` reuses the cache transitively by routing its body curation through `/sync-pr` (В§5.7 step 5). `/work-on` doesn't update the body after PR creation, so it doesn't touch the cache directly; later edits go through `/sync-pr`.

### 5.5 `/status`

`/status` and the `UserPromptSubmit` hook both delegate to the canonical helper at `.claude/hooks/helpers/status.sh`. Two output modes:

- `status_compact` вҖ” multi-line plaintext block, the standard turn-context surface.
- `status_json` вҖ” same fields as stable JSON for diff-comparison or piping.

Fields (both modes):
- Branch + dirty status
- Linked issue (#, title) вҖ” extracted from `Closes #N` / `Refs #N` in the PR body
- PR (#, draft/ready, checklist progress `[x/y]`, CI status) вҖ” `gh pr view`, `gh pr checks`
- Next unchecked checklist item
- Current phase (Doc / Test / Code / Review / Ship), inferred from the next unchecked item's section heading
- Active mode (attended / unattended) per В§5.7.1
- **Bound canonical root** (#318) вҖ” the shared shell root this project resolves to, surfacing the В§1.7 shared-code model. Source: `$GHJIG_ROOT` (exported by the hooks after self-location, В§3.2.1) or `readlink $CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR/.claude/ghjig-root`.
- **Ephemeral-state locality** (#318) вҖ” `project-local` when `ghjig_state_dir()` resolves to `$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR/.claude/ghjig-state` (the normal hook-context case, В§3.2.2), else `legacy-shared`. Surfaces that audit/caches/registry isolate per project.
- **Active work language** (#325) вҖ” the language of durable repository artifacts, resolved via `resolve_work_lang` (В§5.7.2). Compact `work-lang:`, JSON `work_lang`.

`UserPromptSubmit` (В§6.4) emits `status_compact` instead of a hand-rolled branch summary. Keeping the source single ensures `/status` and per-turn injection never drift.

The UserPromptSubmit hook reuses this output for the short per-turn summary.

**Cache**: status results are cached at `.claude/state/status-cache/<branch>.json` with a TTL of `STATUS_CACHE_TTL` seconds (default 5; env-overridable). The cache key is the branch name, so a `git checkout` to a different branch transparently loads a different cache file. Hits skip every `gh` round-trip (today: `gh pr view`, `gh issue view`, `gh pr checks` вҖ” 3 calls per uncached invocation). The 5-second TTL is short enough that real PR/issue/CI changes surface within one user turn (turns typically exceed 5 s) and long enough to dedupe a flurry of prompts. Cache files live under `.claude/state/` (gitignored).

### 5.6 `/review [--staged | <base>]`

Invokes `code-reviewer`. If the diff touches a security surface, also invokes `security-reviewer`. No auto-fix unless explicitly asked.

**Reviewer-head pin (#544)**: when reviewing a pushed PR, `/review` applies the same caller-side blind compare as `/ship` (В§5.7) вҖ” compute the expected head privately (`gh pr view <n> --json headRefOid`, never revealed to the reviewer), compare each reviewer's independently-reported `reviewed-head` (В§4.5), and treat a mismatch/absent head as a fail-closed invalid vote. The reviewer resolves its artifact from the PR head per В§4.5.

### 5.7 `/ship`

Runs the ship sequence from В§2 (steps 0вҖ“8), plus the pre-ready sub-step gates 7.5вҖ“7.7 detailed below. `/ship` runs the full test suite (step 4) before transitioning to ready (step 8). Tests are `/ship`'s responsibility; the hook does not add a separate test gate on ready transition (В§6.1).

**High-asymmetry reviewer tier** (В§4.11): when a ship decision is high-asymmetry вҖ” a `merge-security-surface` merge to the default branch, a `force-push` judgment inside the ship motion, or an `irreversible-adr` merge (a PR carrying `docs/ADRs/`) вҖ” `/ship` classifies it via `is_high_asymmetry` and replaces the single-reviewer verdict with an N=3 independent majority vote. A non-majority is a `hard` blocker вҶ’ park (В§5.7.1). The common path (no high-asymmetry kind) stays single-reviewer.

**Reviewer-head pin вҖ” caller-side blind compare (#544).** Because a worktree-isolated reviewer is checked out at the base, not the PR head (В§1.5), the reviewer pins its artifact to the PR head and reports `reviewed-head:` (В§4.5); `/ship` closes the loop from the caller side:
- **Compute expected head once, privately.** Before dispatch, `/ship` resolves the true head via `gh pr view <n> --json headRefOid` and **holds it privately вҖ” it is NEVER passed to or revealed to any reviewer.** Passing it would let a reviewer echo it back (a tautological pass); the reviewer must derive its `reviewed-head` *independently* for the compare to mean anything.
