- **Blind compare each verdict.** `/ship` compares every reviewer's independently-reported `reviewed-head` against the private expected head. A verdict whose `reviewed-head` вү  current PR head, or is absent/unconfirmed, is a **non-approve: an invalid vote, fail-closed вҖ” never counted as APPROVE** (feeds the В§4.11 fixed-denominator tally: invalid вү  abstention).
- **`gh`-resolve failure at dispatch вҶ’ park (hard).** If `/ship` cannot resolve the expected head at all, no reviewer output can be trusted вҶ’ `hard` blocker вҶ’ park (В§5.7.1). A reviewer's *own* fetch/resolve failure instead makes only *its* vote invalid. No path proceeds unchecked.
- **Merge-time re-pin (TOCTOU).** Before the merge step, `/ship` re-reads the PR head; if it has advanced past the reviewed SHA since the votes were cast, the prior review is **stale вҶ’ re-review**. Never merge an unreviewed head.

**Live immediately for #544's own ship.** The caller-side leg (compute-expected-head + blind compare + non-approve) lives in `ship.md`/`review.md` command text, read at invocation time вҖ” so it is **in force immediately for this fix's own ship**, independent of the В§4.9.3 session-restart caveat. That caveat gates only the *agent-prompt* changes (the reviewer-side `reviewed-head` emission in `code-reviewer.md`/`security-reviewer.md`), which route through `general-purpose` until the next session restart; the caller-side gate does not wait on a restart.

**Merge-attestation write (#544).** Once вҖ” and **strictly after** вҖ” the review pass is determined, `/ship` writes the attestation for PR #N at the confirmed head so the В§6.1 `merge-attestation` gate will allow the subsequent `gh pr merge`. The pass condition is path-specific: on the **single-reviewer** path, the caller-side blind compare above must confirm the reviewer's `reviewed-head` equals the true head; on the **high-asymmetry** path, the В§4.11 fixed-denominator tally must resolve **2-of-3 valid approves**. The write goes through the inline `write_review_attestation` function (folded into `ac_closeout_gate.sh`, В§6.1 fail-policy table вҖ” no new `scripts/review_attest.sh`, no new helper file), recording the confirmed head SHA to `$(ghjig_state_dir)/attest/pr-<N>`. Because the write happens **only after** a determined pass, an **aborted or failed review writes no attestation** вҖ” leaving the `merge-attestation` presence check to block the merge (the never-ran-`/ship` fast-track, handol #246). Like the blind-compare leg, this write lives in `ship.md`/`review.md` command text and is **live immediately** for this fix's own ship (no В§4.9.3 restart wait). No TTL: a later re-push advances the head and auto-invalidates the file, so a stale-head merge is re-blocked until `/ship` re-attests.

CI monitoring: snapshot `gh pr checks --json state` right before ready transition вҖ” already failing вҶ’ block. Right after the transition, run `gh pr checks --watch` in background and return immediately. On failure, the PostToolUse hook notifies the user.

**Checklist audit (mandatory step 7.5, between CI snapshot and `gh pr ready`)**: scan the PR body for any `- [ ]` line. Each unchecked item must be resolved before transition вҖ” ticked if done, marked `[~] N/A вҖ” <reason>` if intentionally skipped, or removed if obsolete. The audit applies to every checklist in the body (Plan, Test plan, Docs touched, Ship gate). Per SPEC В§1.4, stale uncheckedness at merge propagates as misinformation into future context.

**Issue AC closeout (mandatory step 7.6, before `gh pr ready`)**: for every issue in the PR's `closingIssuesReferences`, run `scripts/ac_closeout.sh <pr-num>` to post the canonical `## AC closeout (resolved by PR #N)` comment with each acceptance-criterion item ticked or `[~] N/A`'d. The helper is idempotent, and its skip guard mirrors the gate **exactly** вҖ” it skips an issue only when a **trusted-filer** comment (author association вҲҲ OWNER/MEMBER/MAINTAINER/COLLABORATOR) already carries the strict canonical `^## AC closeout (resolved by PR #N)` marker; a loose `^## AC closeout` lookalike or an untrusted-author comment does **not** satisfy the skip (#556). Were the remedy's guard looser than the gate's, a drive-by lookalike would make the remedy skip while the gate kept blocking вҶ’ merge deadlock. The PreToolUse `ac-closeout` gate (В§6.1) blocks `gh pr merge` when an unchecked-AC closing issue lacks this marker, so running step 7.6 here satisfies the merge gate by construction. Steps 7.5 (PR-body side) and 7.6 (issue side) together are the symmetric halves of "PR-as-living-doc" (В§1.4) across the `Closes #N` linkage. Skipped (all-Directive closing set) when Directives close via `/complete-directive`, not AC checkboxes.

**Changelog gate (mandatory step 7.7, before `gh pr ready`)**: the PR must satisfy the В§18.1 fragment contract (CI-enforced per В§18.6) *before* ready, not after a red CI check вҖ” exactly one of {a fragment exists for the PR number or one of its `closingIssuesReferences`, the `skip-changelog` label is present} must hold. This is a **presence** check; fragment *shape* stays CI's job (В§18.5). When neither holds, `/ship` invokes `/changelog` (В§5.23) to author the fragment or apply the label вҖ” `attended` proposes for confirmation, `unattended` decides automatically (В§5.7.1) вҖ” so the flow self-heals instead of failing at CI. The skip decision follows В§18.7.

When mode is `unattended` (see В§5.7.1), `/ship` continues past step 8 into the CI-wait вҶ’ merge / park branch.

### 5.7.1 Operating modes (attended / unattended)

`/ship` has two terminal behaviors selected by **mode**:

- **`attended`** (default): `/ship` stops at "ready" and hands off to a human reviewer.
- **`unattended`**: after "ready", `/ship` waits on CI / required reviews and either merges or parks the PR for human attention.

**Resolution priority** (high вҶ’ low):

1. `--mode=<attended|unattended>` flag on `/ship`
2. `$GHJIG_SHELL_MODE` env var
3. `.claude/state/mode` per-target file (one of `attended` / `unattended`, no other content)
4. default `attended`

Unknown values fail closed to `attended` and emit a stderr warning naming the offending source. `settings.json` is intentionally **not** a layer вҖ” that file is symlinked across targets (В§3.2) and a mode key would leak between unrelated work.

**Blocker taxonomy** вҖ” `ship_classify_blocker` returns one of:

| State | Criterion |
|-------|-----------|
| `clean` | All required CI checks green; required reviewers (if any) satisfied; branch protection rules satisfied. Eligible for auto-merge. |
| `soft` | CI is `pending` / `in_progress` / `queued`, **or** there is a CI failure that is attributable to the agent's own last commit and is fixable without new product decisions. One self-fix attempt is permitted (see below). |
| `hard` | Required-review with no available reviewer, undiagnosable / non-attributable CI failure, branch-protection rule the agent cannot satisfy, or a `soft` state that has already consumed its one self-fix attempt. |

**Soft-blocker behavior**: at most **one** self-fix-and-push attempt per `/ship` invocation. The retry pushes a `fix(#N): ...` commit and returns to the CI-wait state. A second `soft` outcome immediately escalates to `hard` вҖ” no further fix attempts.

**Hard-blocker behavior** (parking) вҖ” all four actions, in order, and idempotent:

1. Post a `gh pr comment` with a deterministic state summary (blocker reason + current SHA + CI snapshot).
2. Apply label `unattended-parked` (create the label on demand if missing). If the label is already present from a previous park on the same PR, `ship_park_pr` writes a single `park-suppressed: <reason>` line to the log instead of reposting the comment, and emits no comment to stdout. The original park comment remains canonical; the label remains applied.
3. Append one line to `${SHIP_PARK_LOG_PATH:-$GHJIG_ROOT/.claude/state/unattended-park.log}` (shell-side, gitignored вҖ” not the target's MEMORY.md). The override exists for smoke-test isolation. On suppressed repeat, only the `park-suppressed: <reason>` line is appended. **Additionally, on a fresh park** (not the suppressed-repeat arm), `ship_park_pr` emits one `audit_log warn unattended-park parked "reason=<token>"` record (guarded by `command -v audit_log` вҖ” best-effort, so a standalone invocation without the runtime still writes the park-log unconditionally). This is **additive** (the human-readable park-log is unchanged, not a schema change): it bridges overnight park frequency вҖ” the highest-value unattended friction signal вҖ” into `audit.jsonl`, the aggregate the В§6.5(d) friction advisory reads, so parks stop being invisible to the friction-observability loop (#398, Directive #391). The `unattended-park` audit category records park-as-friction-signal; it is read **directly** by the В§6.5(d) advisory (neither `narrowing_candidates.sh` nor `promotion_candidates.sh` matches a `warn`/`parked` record).
4. Stop. Do not toggle draft or self-assign.

**Classifier robustness**: `ship_classify_blocker` fails closed to `hard` in two failure modes and emits a one-line stderr warning naming the cause:

- empty stdin вҶ’ `ship_classify_blocker: no input on stdin вҖ” defaulting to hard`
- missing `jq` dependency вҶ’ `ship_classify_blocker: jq not found вҖ” defaulting to hard`

The intent is to make overnight runs debuggable without changing the safe fail-closed default. Either condition resolves the classification to `hard` and the dispatch path proceeds to park.

**Merge mechanism**: `gh pr merge --auto --merge --delete-branch` (no-fast-forward merge commit; PR branch's commits are preserved on `main`). This requires repo-level auto-merge to be enabled at GitHub. If the API call fails because auto-merge is disabled, fall back to the park path (log + label + comment) with reason `auto-merge-disabled`.

**Why `--merge` rather than `--squash`**: SPEC В§1.2 makes the Doc вҶ’ Test вҶ’ Code commit graph load-bearing вҖ” the arc is the artifact that proves the discipline happened. Squash erases the arc on merge (the PR branch is deleted; only a single new commit lands on `main`). `--merge` keeps both: the individual phase commits stay on `main`, plus a merge commit anchors the PR-as-a-unit so `git log --first-parent main` gives a clean PR-level view. The visible cost is a busier `git log`; the audit-trail philosophy in В§6/В§7 trades that for the preserved arc.

**Composition with branch protection**: server-side rules in GitHub are always authoritative. `unattended` does not bypass them. A required-reviews rule with no available reviewer resolves to `hard` and parks вҖ” the shell never self-approves or auto-requests review against policy.

**Composition with Auto mode**: Auto mode (single-conversation clarification suppression) is orthogonal to operating mode. Any combination is valid: `attended + Auto`, `unattended + non-Auto`, etc. Mode controls the `/ship` terminal behavior; Auto controls in-turn prompting.

Note: В§6.1's "direct push to protected branch blocked" hook is **not** tripped by the merge step вҖ” `gh pr merge --auto` is a GitHub API call, not a `git push` to `main`.

**Directive-aware audit** (added by tracking #41 child #6, issue #47): when the merged PR's linked Issue carries a `Parent Directive: #N` marker (В§5.2), `/ship` appends one audit line `directive-exec-count directive=#N pr=#M issue=#K` to `audit.jsonl`. The audit reads `closingIssuesReferences` вҖ” so in topic-branch flow (В§10.5), sub-task PRs (which use `Refs #N`) emit no audit line, and the audit fires only on the **consolidator PR** that closes each parented Execution Issue at the moment work reaches `main`. Informational only вҖ” `/ship` does **not** auto-mark the Directive `Completed`. Completion is `/complete-directive`'s job, gated by `activation-reviewer` (В§4.9). This preserves the В§1.5 invariant: generation is open, decision is gated.

**Canonical hook-enforced path** (Directive #61): `.github/workflows/dir-mode-post-merge.yml` (installed from `.claude/templates/target-substrate/workflows/dir-mode-post-merge.yml`) fires on every `pull_request.closed && merged == true` event, regardless of who performed the merge (Claude-in-loop, human via UI, CI auto-merge). The Action emits an equivalent reflection comment on the parent Directive вҖ” the comment surface IS the audit surface for hook-enforced events, since the workflow runner cannot write to a per-clone `audit.jsonl`. The Markdown procedure above stays valid for Claude-in-loop runs (defense in depth); the workflow posts a marker-stamped **stub** and `/reflect` enriches it in place, the two paths deduping on the `reflect-stub`/`reflect-enriched` **content markers** rather than the shared PR URL (#329 вҖ” see В§5.15).

### 5.7.2 Communication language vs work language

The shell separates two independent language channels (#322):

- **Communication language** вҖ” the humanвҶ”agent conversation. Whatever language the user writes in; the agent's chat replies stay in it. The shell never detects, configures, or translates it.
- **Work language** вҖ” the single language of **durable repository artifacts**. Resolved by `resolve_work_lang` (`.claude/hooks/helpers/work_lang.sh`), defaulting to `en`.

**Per-surface classification** вҖ” every shell-authored artifact is one or the other:

| Work language (durable, in the repo) | Communication language (ephemeral, in the chat) |
|---|---|
| commit messages; PR titles/bodies; issue / directive / execution bodies; acceptance criteria; changelog fragments; shell-authored code comments; audit `reason` text | the agent's conversational replies to the user |

**Pre-work context-recast step.** After the human conversation concludes and **before authoring any durable artifact**, the agent re-organizes the task context into the work language вҖ” it does not transliterate the chat verbatim but re-expresses intent, decisions, and plan in the work language, then authors every work-language surface from that recast. This is the "narrowing/normalization" half of the MISSION mechanism applied to language: durable memory and the artifact-only review surface stay legible in one consistent language regardless of the conversation language.

**Resolution priority** (high вҶ’ low), mirroring В§5.7.1:

1. `$GHJIG_WORK_LANG` env var
2. `.claude/state/work-lang` per-target file (a single language code, cwd-relative вҖ” read exactly as `resolve_mode` reads `.claude/state/mode`)
3. default `en`

Any non-empty language code is accepted **verbatim** (BCP-47-style tokens such as `en`, `ko`, `fr`, `ja`, `pt-BR`) вҖ” there is no closed enum, so the capability generalizes to any (communication, work) pair and is never `ko`/`en`-hardcoded. An empty / whitespace-only value resolves to `en` (the surface is named in a stderr note). `resolve_work_lang` is `set -u`-safe and makes no external calls beyond `head`/`tr`.

**Config placement** вҖ” `.claude/state/work-lang`, **not** `ghjig-state/`. Work language is user-set, set-once **configuration** (the same tier as the `mode` toggle В§5.7.1 and the `coauthor` toggle В§10.2), not regenerable **ephemeral state** (`ghjig-state/` holds the audit log, caches, and registry вҖ” В§3.2.2). Directive #322's body says "ghjig-state" but cites "the mode toggle" as the analog; the mode toggle lives at `.claude/state/mode`, so `work-lang` follows that concrete precedent (config tier, cwd-relative) rather than the mislabeled category word. Like В§5.7.1, `settings.json` is intentionally **not** a layer вҖ” it is symlinked across targets (В§3.2) and a work-language key would leak between unrelated projects.

Back-compat: unset вҶ’ `en`, i.e. today's behavior; nothing changes for a target that never sets a work language. **Surfacing** is delivered (#325): `status_compact` emits a `work-lang:` line and `status_json` a `work_lang` key (resolved via `resolve_work_lang`), so `/status` and the per-turn statusline show the active work language alongside `mode`. **Skill integration** is delivered (#327): the artifact-authoring skills (`file-issue`, `file-directive`, `work-on`, `ship`, `complete-directive`) each carry a `## Work language` note instructing the agent to recast context and author their durable artifact in the work language вҖ” co-located with the authoring step (skills-as-environment) so the instruction survives context-narrowing. Enforcement is agent-followed prose, not a hook: the *language of free prose* is not mechanically checkable (#322 success signal 2 delegates it to review); smoke grep-locks only that each skill carries the note.

### 5.8 `/adr <title>`

**ADR vs PR body Decisions**:
- **ADR** вҖ” irreversible, system-level. Migrations (DB engine, schema change), external contracts (API spec, wire format), default technology choices (auth scheme, queueing model). High cost to reverse once merged.
- **PR body Decisions** вҖ” reversible, PR-scoped trade-offs. Default option choice, algorithm tuning parameters, equivalent-library preference, naming choices. Explainable within this PR and not affecting other PRs.

`/adr` creates `docs/ADRs/NNNN-title.md` (from `.claude/templates/adr.md`). A `вҶ’ ADR-NNNN` link is auto-added to the PR body's Decisions section. Authoring is a **reversible doc-write** (the file is editable until merged), so the high-asymmetry reviewer tier (В§4.11) does *not* fire here вҖ” it fires at the irreversible point, the PR merge carrying the ADR, in `/ship`.

### 5.9 `/audit [<filter>]`

Query `.claude/audit/audit.jsonl`. Recent blocks / escapes / warns. A frequently-escaped category is a signal to tune the hook.

### 5.10 `/file-directive`

Create a new Directive as a GitHub Issue with `directive` + `status:proposed` labels. AI-assisted authoring from `.claude/templates/directive.md` (Objective / Success signals / Non-goals / Constraints / MISSION fit вҖ” MISSION.md reference replaces a separate parent-goal artifact). Routes through `activation-reviewer` (В§4.9) before commit; verdict gates per В§5.7.1 mode rules (`reject` parks the proposal to `.claude/state/directive-block.log`). Audit category: `directive-file` (reason format: `directive: <Objective summary> issue=#<N> priority=P<P> confidence=<C>`). The Project Item is created and populated by `.github/workflows/issues-to-project-mirror.yml`; `/file-directive` does NOT write to the Project. **Priority encoding (#185):** the `P<P>` label (`P0`вҖ“`P3`, installed in the tier-2 set by `scripts/ensure_v3_labels.sh`, В§0.4) is the mirror-readable projection of priority and is applied with graceful degradation вҖ” present вҶ’ labeled; absent вҶ’ warn + file without it (never abort), per В§0.4. The body `## Priority` field + the `directive-file` audit line are the durable priority record; the label is the queryable/mirror projection. Full procedure lives in `.claude/commands/file-directive.md`.

### 5.11 `/list-directives [--status <state>]`

List Directive Issues filtered by Status label. Read-only вҖ” queries Issues directly; does NOT consult the Project (which is a derived view that may lag). `--status` accepts `Proposed | Active | Blocked | Completed | All`; default omits `Completed`. Tabular output: `# / Status / Priority / Title`. Status derivation per Issue: `status:proposed` label вҶ’ Proposed; `status:blocked` label вҶ’ Blocked; closed + reason=completed вҶ’ Completed; open + no `status:*` label вҶ’ Active. No audit emission. Full procedure lives in `.claude/commands/list-directives.md`.

### 5.12 `/activate [<issue-#>]`

Promote a `Proposed` Issue (Directive **or** Execution Issue вҖ” `/activate` is type-neutral) to `Active` by removing the `status:proposed` label after a fresh `activation-reviewer` (В§4.9) pass on the current body. This is the observer-side gate of the full-symmetry lifecycle (В§2.1): every Issue is filed `status:proposed` and becomes actionable only after `/activate` returns `pass`. `/activate` is also the **unblock** path for a Blocked Directive (В§5.17): a re-activatable Issue carries `status:proposed` (Proposed) **or** `status:blocked` (an Active-but-Blocked Directive); only when **neither** label is present is the Issue plain Active and `/activate` errors "already Active". On `pass` it removes whichever of `{status:proposed, status:blocked, awaiting-author}` are present (each removal presence-guarded вҖ” `gh issue edit --remove-label` errors on an absent label). Batch mode scans `--label status:proposed`, so it does **not** sweep Blocked Directives вҖ” unblock is single-mode `/activate <N>` only (auto-unblocking would silently reverse a deliberate maintainer block).

- **Single mode** `/activate <N>`: resolve `<N>`'s type label (tri-state, matching `activation-reviewer`'s В§4.9 dispatch вҖ” an `initiative`-labelled Issue is **refused**, not activated: Initiatives are consumed via `/consume-initiative` (В§5.21) and live outside the ProposedвҶ’Active lifecycle (В§2.1); a bare `directive`-else-Execution split would otherwise mis-type one as Execution. The guard normally never fires because an Initiative never carries `status:proposed`), invoke `activation-reviewer` with the type context, parse the verdict, and apply it:
  - `pass` вҶ’ remove the present activation labels (`status:proposed` and/or `status:blocked`, plus `awaiting-author` if present) вҶ’ Active.
  - `revise` вҶ’ post the findings as a comment carrying `<!-- activation-verdict: revise -->`, retain `status:proposed`, add `awaiting-author`. After **N=3** `revise` markers on the Issue, escalate to `reject`.
  - `reject` вҶ’ post the verdict + structured fields with `<!-- activation-verdict: reject -->`, then apply **filer-aware handling** (verdict is content-only; handling keys on `authorAssociation` via `is_trusted_filer`): **trusted** вҶ’ keep open + `awaiting-author`, never close (composes with `trusted-filer-mutate`, В§6.1); **untrusted + `refile-body-draft`** вҶ’ close (`--reason "not planned"`) + auto-create a `discussion`-tier Issue (В§5.19) preserving the draft + a lineage link; **untrusted, no draft** вҶ’ close + brief comment.
- **Batch mode** `/activate` (no arg): scan all open `status:proposed` Issues and process each. **Loop-safety:** skip an Issue whose latest `<!-- activation-verdict: <verdict> -->` comment marker post-dates its last body/label edit (verdict already delivered, awaiting the author) вҖ” independent of the `awaiting-author` label. In `attended` mode `reject` surfaces to the operator; in `unattended` it auto-applies the filer matrix.
- **Reviewer invocation** is robust to the В§4.9.3 session-restart caveat: the agent file is on disk and its prompt is self-describing, so a `general-purpose` fallback still behaves as the reviewer.

`/activate-directive <issue-#>` is retained as a **thin alias** delegating to `/activate <N>` for one release cycle (Directive-only ergonomics), then removed. Audit category: `activation`. The mirror workflow fires on `issues.unlabeled` and updates the Project Item's Status. Escape: see В§7. Full procedure lives in `.claude/commands/activate.md`.

### 5.13 `/complete-directive <issue-#>`

Close a Directive Issue with `--reason completed`. `activation-reviewer` (В§4.9) evaluates evidence вҖ” the linked Execution Issues' close states / AC ticks вҖ” against the success signals. **Directive completion is a high-asymmetry decision** (В§4.11, `directive-completion`): the evidence evaluation runs as an N=3 independent majority vote of `activation-reviewer`, not a single verdict (a wrong "complete" is irreversible вҖ” it closes the Directive). A non-majority leaves the Issue open. `reject` (insufficient evidence) leaves the Issue open. On `pass`, posts a closing comment listing each signal and its evidence, then closes the Issue. The `trusted-filer-mutate` hook matcher (SPEC В§1.5, В§6.1) allows `--reason completed` on trusted-filer Issues without further confirmation. Audit category: `directive-complete`. Escape: see В§7. The mirror workflow fires on `issues.closed` and updates the Project Item's Status. When the Directive's Execution Issues used the topic-branch flow (`/work-on --base <topic-branch>`, В§10.5), `/complete-directive` must run **after** the topic branch consolidates to `main` вҖ” the reviewer reads closed-Execution-Issue evidence, and still-open `Refs`'d Issues yield insufficient-evidence verdicts. Full procedure lives in `.claude/commands/complete-directive.md`.

### 5.14 `/link-directive <directive-#> <execution-#>`

Link an Execution Issue to its parent Directive by ensuring the `Parent Directive: #<directive-#>` line-1 body marker is set on the Execution Issue + posting cross-reference comments. Idempotent вҖ” re-running on an already-linked pair no-ops with an info-level audit line. The Project Item's `Parent` field is mirrored from the body marker by `.github/workflows/issues-to-project-mirror.yml`; `/link-directive` does NOT write to the Project directly. Audit category: `directive-link`. Full procedure lives in `.claude/commands/link-directive.md`.

### 5.15 `/reflect [<pr-#>]`

Post a structured reflection comment on a PR's parent Directive (when one exists) summarizing the PR's contribution toward that Directive's success signals. Run after merge; idempotent вҖ” classifies the Directive's existing comments by **content marker** (#329): a `<!-- reflect-enriched pr=#N -->` comment вҶ’ no-op; the hook-enforced floor's `<!-- reflect-stub pr=#N -->` вҶ’ **enrich in place** (edit that comment by REST comment id); neither вҶ’ post fresh. (Keying on the marker, not the shared PR URL, is what lets `/reflect` enrich the workflow's at-merge stub instead of no-op'ing against it.) Resolves the parent Directive from each closing Issue's body via the regex `^Parent Directive: #(\d+)$` (the marker `/file-issue --parent` writes on line 1, SPEC В§5.2) вҖ” **label-aware** (#335): it climbs the marker chain to the first `directive`-labelled ancestor (depth-cap 2, cycle guard, fail-soft) rather than stopping at the first marker, so a nested-umbrella Execution Issue reflects onto the grandparent Directive, not the intervening umbrella. Audit category: `directive-reflect` (decisions: `posted` / `skipped`). Read-only on the linked Execution Issues; writes only the reflection comment on the Directive Issue. The human-readable counterpart to `/ship` step 10.5's bare `directive-exec-count` audit (SPEC В§5.7). Full procedure lives in `.claude/commands/reflect.md` (added by tracking #41 child #6, issue #47).

**Hook-enforced floor** (Directive #61): `.github/workflows/dir-mode-post-merge.yml` posts a **stub** reflection automatically on every merged PR with a `Parent Directive:` marker (marked `<!-- reflect-stub pr=#N -->`), so the reflection trail is complete regardless of who merged. The workflow resolves the target Directive via a **sourced helper** `resolve_parent_directive.sh` (shipped alongside the workflow and read after `actions/checkout`) rather than inline run-block bash, so the resolution вҖ” the label-aware climb to the first `directive`-labelled ancestor (#335) вҖ” is CI-shellchecked and smoke-executed; a resolved-nothing run logs a visible no-op. The helper has three byte-identical copies (canonical `scripts/lib/`, this-repo runtime `.github/workflows/`, and the target-substrate copy installed into onboarded targets), kept in lock-step by a `cmp` smoke assertion (the same discipline that holds the three workflow YAML copies in sync). The same workflow also runs the **bare-`Refs`-to-default check** (`detect_bare_refs_directive.sh`, #337, В§10.5): when a merged PR's base is the live default branch, its closing set is empty, and its body carries a directive-scoped `Refs #N`, it posts a single idempotent warning comment on the PR вҖ” surfacing the В§10.5 leak that would otherwise silently deprive the Directive of a reflection. Warn-only, fail-soft, and (unlike a `gh pr merge` hook) it fires on human UI merges too. When Claude runs `/reflect`, it produces the richer per-signal block by **editing that stub in place** (PATCH by REST comment id), swapping the marker for `<!-- reflect-enriched pr=#N -->`. The two paths dedupe on the **content markers**, not the shared PR URL (#329): a URL-keyed check would make `/reflect` no-op against the workflow's at-merge stub and the enrichment would never happen. Classification: enriched-marker present вҶ’ no-op; stub-marker present вҶ’ enrich in place; neither вҶ’ post fresh.

**`### Learnings for the next Execution` section** (closes Directive #477 signal 3 вҖ” the directive-level coding-memory loop). The enriched reflection comment carries a fourth section alongside Contribution / Success signals advanced / Next: distilled **durable coding signal** from the merged PR's Code phase вҖ” codebase gotchas, conventions to follow, what to reuse vs avoid вҖ” and, when the `/implement` path (В§5.28) authored the PR, drawn additionally from the structured-return **discoveries**. **Distillation heuristic**: keep only learning that **outlives this PR** and would help a sibling Execution under the same Directive; the within-Execution **churn** (file reads, abandoned approaches, lint/smoke iterations) is the В§1.2 / В§3.7 discard boundary and is **not** transcribed. This is the *write* half of the loop `/work-on` step 4.5 (В§5.3) reads back. **Idempotency is unchanged**: the section rides **inside** the existing reflection comment under the same `reflect-stub` / `reflect-enriched` marker (a fourth body section, not a new comment), so the step-3 classification and the PATCH-by-REST-id enrich-in-place flow are untouched.

### 5.16 `/revise-directive <issue-#>`

Replace an `Active` Directive Issue's body with a new one when scope or success signals changed, archiving the prior body as a comment for history. Procedure: (1) read the current body; (2) compute its sha256; (3) invoke `activation-reviewer` (В§4.9) on the **new** body вҖ” the same proposal checks as `/file-directive` (schema / parent-kind alignment / success-signal verifiability / scope / non-goal / active-Directive conflict); (4) on `pass`, post a `## Pre-revision body вҖ” archived <ISO date>` comment with the verbatim prior body, then replace the Issue body via `gh issue edit --body-file`; (5) emit `audit_log info directive-revise reconciled "directive=#<issue-#> from-sha=<prior-sha> archive-comment=<url>"`. **No Status change** вҖ” the audit-log entry + the archive comment ARE the durable evidence of revision (no transient state needed вҖ” see В§2.1). On `revise` or `reject`, leave the body unchanged. Escape: see В§7. Full procedure lives in `.claude/commands/revise-directive.md`.

### 5.17 `/block-directive <issue-#> --reason <why>`

Mark an `Active` Directive as `Blocked` by adding the `status:blocked` label and a `## Blocked: <reason>` comment. Procedure: (1) require the `--reason <why>` flag вҖ” empty or missing reason aborts; (2) post a `## Blocked: <reason>` comment on the Issue (idempotent вҖ” skip if the same `## Blocked:` marker is the latest comment AND `status:blocked` label is already present); (3) add the `status:blocked` label via `gh issue edit --add-label`; (4) emit `audit_log info directive-block created "directive: #<issue-#> reason=<short> comment=<url>"`. The Issue stays **open** on GitHub вҖ” closing the Directive Issue continues to require `/complete-directive` (В§5.13). Unblock by running `/activate <issue-#>` (the `/activate-directive` alias delegates to it): it treats `status:blocked` as a re-activatable precondition, re-invokes `activation-reviewer` on the current body, and on `pass` removes the `status:blocked` label (В§5.12). Not reviewer-gated вҖ” blocking is an annotation, not a body change. Audit category: `directive-block`. The mirror workflow fires on `issues.labeled` and updates the Project Item's Status. Full procedure lives in `.claude/commands/block-directive.md`.

> **В§5.18 `/triage` вҖ” deprecated alias (#173, Directive #167).** `/triage`'s `status:proposed` substantive gate is now `/activate` (В§5.12), and its stale-discussion surfacing (open `discussion` Issues > 14 days, formerly В§5.19 step 2.5) moved into `/activate` batch mode. `/triage` survives one release cycle as a thin alias delegating to `/activate`; its notice names the Phase-2 gap honestly вҖ” `/activate` subsumes only the `status:proposed` half, while raw-filing classification is now handled by `auto-status-proposed.yml` (#179). Full alias body: `.claude/commands/triage.md`.

### 5.19 Discussion tier (Issue #112 substrate; Directive #109)

A distinct open-Issue tier alongside Directive / Execution / task / bug. **Purpose**: capture deliberately-ambiguous observations ("weird but not a bug", half-formed ideas, smells, RFC-style probes) without forcing premature classification. The tier exists because the other tiers each force a misclassification on such filings: `task` reads as actionable, `bug` claims a defect, and skipping filing loses the observation entirely. Discussion is the honest path. (Raw label-free filings are auto-stamped `status:proposed`+`task` by `auto-status-proposed.yml` (#179) and validated at `/activate`; deliberate ambiguity is filed `discussion` instead.)

**Labeling**: a single `discussion` label (color `#FEF2C0`, light yellow) installed by `scripts/ensure_v3_labels.sh` alongside the other dir-mode labels. Issue Form template at `.github/ISSUE_TEMPLATE/discussion.yml` requires only title + body вҖ” no acceptance criteria, no MISSION fit, no rationale-triad prompt; the reduced-required shape is the whole point.

**Lifecycle**: develop in comments. Discussion Issues are NOT parented to Directives (no AC; nothing to roll up). The Issue's comment thread IS the development surface.

**Close paths** вҖ” exactly two:

- **`promoted`** вҖ” a concrete Issue (bug / task / Directive) was filed; the discussion closes referencing it (`gh issue close <N> --reason completed` plus a `^promoted to #<M>$` comment). The new Issue cross-references back.
- **`no-action`** вҖ” the discussion concluded nothing needs doing (`gh issue close <N> --reason "not planned"` plus a one-line comment naming the reason). The `gh` CLI accepts only `{completed|not planned|duplicate}` вҖ” the **space** form; `not_planned` (underscore) is rejected by `gh`, so the space form is canonical everywhere the value reaches `gh`.

No third path. Stale discussions surface via `/activate` batch mode (В§5.12; relocated from `/triage` by #173); no auto-close timer.

**Tier-relationships table**:

| Tier | Label(s) | AC-bearing? | Parented under Directive? | Close paths |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Directive | `directive` + `status:*` | No (success signals instead) | No (root of the hierarchy) | `/complete-directive` (В§5.13) вҖ” Completed via reviewer ship |
| Execution | (none, or template-applied) | Yes | Optional (`--parent`) | `Closes #N` via PR merge |
| task | `task` | Yes | No | `Closes #N` via PR merge or close-as-not-planned |
| bug | `bug` | Yes | No | `Closes #N` via PR merge or close-as-not-planned |
| **discussion** | `discussion` | **No** | **No** | **`promoted` or `no-action` only** |

**Lifecycle implementation** (Issue #116; Directive #109 final slice):

- `/discuss <title>` вҖ” friction-free filing; bypasses the rationale triad + `issue-reviewer` gate. Full procedure in `.claude/commands/discuss.md`.
- `/resolve-discussion <N> [--promoted-to <M>] [--no-action <reason>]` вҖ” closes via exactly one of the two paths above. Idempotent. Full procedure in `.claude/commands/resolve-discussion.md`.
- Close-path enforcement вҖ” hook matcher arm under `trusted-filer-mutate` (В§6.1) blocks `gh issue close <N>` on a `discussion`-labeled Issue without `--reason completed` OR `--reason "not planned"`. The matcher tolerates both the gh-valid space form and the legacy underscore so it is never itself the blocker; the canonical emitted form is the space form. Discussion-tier classification is evaluated **first and independent of filer trust** (#236): once an Issue is recognized as `discussion`, the В§5.19 two-path rule governs вҖ” `--reason completed` OR `--reason "not planned"` is allowed regardless of the filer's `authorAssociation`, and a bare close or `--reason duplicate` is blocked. The trusted-filer block (below) applies only to **non-discussion** Issues. Stage 1 of the close-arm two-stage check (stage 2 = trusted-filer enforcement).
- `/activate` batch mode (В§5.12; relocated from `/triage` by #173) вҖ” surfaces open `discussion`-labeled Issues older than 14 days as a maintainer-decision queue (promote / dismiss / let-incubate). Mode-independent: AI does not autonomously promote/dismiss even in unattended.
- Smoke В§62 вҖ” 8 assertions covering skill files, hook close-path enforcement (block + allow paths, the gh-valid `"not planned"` space form + legacy-underscore tolerance + a `duplicate` negative, #216), and `/triage` extension.

**Lockstep with Directive #107**: the `discussion` label is in `/onboard-dir-mode`'s bootstrap-label set (the dir-mode label set вҖ” see the canonical count in В§1.7's Tier 2 note). #112 (label substrate) merged first; #116 (lifecycle) merged second; #107's `/onboard-dir-mode` consumes both.

### 5.20 `/release <X.Y.Z> [--base <branch>] [--dry-run]`

Cut a versioned release by consolidating per-PR changelog fragments into a new section of `CHANGELOG.md` and opening a `release/X.Y.Z` draft PR. Implements the fragment-contract consumer side of SPEC В§18.

Procedure (full body in `.claude/commands/release.md`):

1. **Parse args** вҖ” required `<X.Y.Z>` (semver 0.x; reject `MAJOR > 0` with explicit `SPEC В§3.5 / В§18.2 MAJOR=0 invariant` message), optional `--base <branch>` (default `main`; for maintenance-line cuts per В§18.3 / В§10.5), optional `--dry-run` (helper stages but does not commit/push/branch).
2. **Preflight** вҖ” assert clean working tree on the target base, `git fetch --tags origin`, refuse if `release/X.Y.Z` branch exists on origin OR `vX.Y.Z` tag already exists (exits 0 with `already released` message вҖ” idempotent retry).
3. **VERSION write-back** вҖ” strip any `-dev` suffix from the top-level `VERSION` and write `X.Y.Z`. Resolution-time queries fall back to `git describe --tags`; write-back is `VERSION`-only per В§18.2.
4. **CHANGELOG consolidate** вҖ” read every `changelog_unreleased/<category>/<N>.md`, validate (positive-integer filename stem; bullet contains `(#<N>)` matching stem), prepend a new `## [X.Y.Z] вҖ” YYYY-MM-DD` section (UTC date) to `CHANGELOG.md` with `### <Category>` subheadings (Keep-a-Changelog), append `[X.Y.Z]: https://github.com/<owner>/<repo>/releases/tag/vX.Y.Z` reference link at the file footer.
5. **Fragment cleanup** вҖ” `git rm` every consumed fragment file (leave the six `.gitkeep` placeholders intact).
6. **Branch + draft PR** вҖ” create `release/X.Y.Z` (short-lived; covered by the existing `release/*` arm of the protected-branch matcher per В§6.1). Commit the VERSION + CHANGELOG + fragment-removal as a single **scopeless** `chore: release X.Y.Z` commit under the documented `SKIP_HOOKS=branch SKIP_REASON='/release initial release-branch commit'` escape (audit-logged; structurally required since the protected-branch matcher blocks all direct commits on `release/X.Y.Z` and this is the one purposeful commit). The subject is scopeless вҖ” not `chore(release): вҖҰ` вҖ” because the `commit-format` matcher permits only a `(#N)` scope or no scope, and the `branch` escape does not cover `commit-format`. Push, open a draft PR titled `chore: release X.Y.Z`.
7. **Reviewer gate** вҖ” in `unattended` mode, re-run `code-reviewer` (В§4.5) against the release diff before `gh pr create` to catch malformed CHANGELOG concatenation / mismatched tag / VERSION drift. Per В§1.5 reviewer-substitution. Escape: `SKIP_HOOKS=release-review SKIP_REASON='<why>'`.
8. **On-merge tag + Release** (documented post-merge step; **maintainer-run, not automated** per В§18.5 non-goals вҖ” this is the one step that sits *past* the `unattended` autonomy ceiling, which terminates at `gh pr merge`/park (В§5.7.1); the `unattended` `/release` continuation stops at the merged release PR and does **not** cut the tag/Release): after the release PR merges to the target base, the maintainer runs:
    ```bash
    MERGE_SHA=$(git rev-parse HEAD)  # on target base, post-merge
    awk '/^## \[X\.Y\.Z\]/{f=1; next} /^## \[/{f=0} f' CHANGELOG.md > /tmp/release-notes-vX.Y.Z.md
    gh release create vX.Y.Z --title vX.Y.Z --target "$MERGE_SHA" --notes-file /tmp/release-notes-vX.Y.Z.md
    scripts/release_verify.sh X.Y.Z   # post-merge verify (below)
    ```
    Re-running on an already-released tag is a no-op with a clear message. **No `--verify-tag`** (#448): the flag aborts `gh release create` unless the tag already exists, but the tag is created *together with* the Release here (from `--target`), so it would always abort on a fresh release.

    **Post-merge verify** (#471, Directive #468): `scripts/release_verify.sh X.Y.Z` is a **read-only, fail-open** confirmation run *after* the create вҖ” it checks the `vX.Y.Z` tag exists and a GitHub Release with **non-empty notes** is present (one `gh release view --json tagName,body` query), printing a named advisory line on a missing tag / missing-or-empty-notes Release. It **never creates** anything and **exits 0 on every path** (gh error / offline вҶ’ one advisory line), so it observes the release result without blocking вҖ” the verification-only / never-false-block posture (В§6.0 cost-asymmetry). The `unattended` `/release` continuation runs it after its post-merge create.

`/release` factors deterministic work into `scripts/release_consolidate.sh` so smoke can exercise it against throwaway repos without booting a Claude Code session (same precedent as `scripts/ac_closeout.sh` вҶ” `/ship` step 7.6). Audit category: `release` (decisions: `created`, `idempotent`, `blocked`).

### 5.21 `/consume-initiative <N>` (Issue #257; Directive #256)

The consume flow (SPEC В§1.7 "Initiatives вҖ” the planning tier the shell consumes"): turn an upstream `initiative`-labelled Issue into Initiative-parented Directive proposals, working backward from its termination condition. A **prompt-driven skill** (`.claude/commands/consume-initiative.md`), script-less like `/file-directive` вҖ” the load-bearing work (judging the contract, decomposing the termination condition, authoring Directive bodies) is LLM reasoning, not mechanizable steps. Procedure:

1. **Type/substrate check** вҖ” resolve `#N`; require the `initiative` label (else error). Same-repo only (cross-repo Initiatives are out of scope, В§1.7).
2. **Contract gate** вҖ” invoke `activation-reviewer` (Initiative rulebook, contract-evaluability I1, В§4.9). If the termination condition is not evaluable without code knowledge вҶ’ the Initiative is under-specified: post a plain `gh issue comment <N>` surfacing it upstream and **STOP** (file no Directives). `gh issue comment` is the only Initiative write the flow performs вҖ” allowed by `initiative-readonly` (В§6.1), which blocks only `edit`/`close`/`reopen`.
3. **Extract (working backward)** вҖ” restate the termination condition, decompose it into the sub-outcomes that together satisfy it, and map each to one Directive proposal. The **necessary-and-sufficient** framing is the *faithfulness criterion* the I2 gate checks (necessary вҶ’ no Directive exceeds the condition; sufficient вҶ’ the set covers it), **not** a deterministic decomposition algorithm вҖ” the partition is judgment. Each proposal carries a line-1 `Parent Initiative: #N` marker and **no `## MISSION fit` field** (the parent-XOR is satisfied by the marker; the Initiative traces to MISSION upstream).
4. **Faithfulness gate** вҖ” invoke `activation-reviewer` (extraction-faithfulness I2, В§4.9) over the **whole proposal set** (coverage is a set property, not per-Directive); on `revise`, refine and re-invoke (two-round backstop as `/file-directive`).
5. **File** вҖ” `gh issue create --label directive --label status:proposed` for each proposal (body via `--body-file` so upstream-authored Initiative text is never interpolated into a `gh` argument position вҖ” this covers the injection surface; content-trust is handled by the I1/I2 gates + human activation, not by `--body-file`). The extracted Directives are **never activated** вҖ” activation stays human/reviewer-gated via `/activate` (generation-open / decision-gated, В§5.7). At create time `label-parent-consistency` is not matched (it is scoped to `--add-label`), so the **I2 gate is the effective parent-XOR check** for the create path (it sees the full proposal bodies before filing).

Audit category: `initiative-consume` (decisions: `extracted` with count=N, `under-specified` (contract gate stopped the flow), `revise`). The command never edits/closes/relabels the Initiative (M1.2 `initiative-readonly`); never activates the extracted Directives; never files a proposal without the `Parent Initiative: #N` marker. Escape (reviewer gate): see В§7.

### 5.22 `/initiative-feedback <N> {--challenge "<reason>" | --completion}` (Issue #260; Directive #259)

The **upward-feedback** flow (SPEC В§1.7 "Feedback is upward and non-deciding") вҖ” the execution layer surfaces findings to an Initiative as structured comments, never as strategic decisions. One command, two modes (mirrors `/resolve-discussion`'s two-path shape). Both modes require the `initiative` label on `#N` (else error), operate same-repo, and write **only** a `gh issue comment --body-file` (the sole Initiative write вҖ” allowed by `initiative-readonly`; `--body-file` for the injection surface). Each comment leads with a **scannable marker** (`## Initiative challenge` / `## Initiative completion`, modeled on `## AC closeout`) so an upstream consumer could parse it. These markers are projected into the `initiative:challenged` / `initiative:completion-requested` labels by the target-repo `initiative-feedback-label.yml` CI Action (#359, В§1.7) вҖ” applied by CI, never by eng's runtime, preserving `initiative-readonly`.

- **`--challenge "<reason>"`** вҖ” when execution reality contradicts the Initiative (a termination condition that looked measurable but isn't; a real dependency / measurability / implementation cost the planning layer structurally cannot have), post a `## Initiative challenge` comment carrying that **code-derived** information and **requesting re-evaluation**. It **escalates** вҖ” it does NOT reject, retire, or close the Initiative (mirrors a reviewer `block` escalating rather than auto-discarding, В§4.9.1). The decision stays upstream; the shell does not track what happens next.
- **`--completion`** вҖ” when the Directives extracted from the Initiative (`/consume-initiative`, В§5.21) have all landed, post a `## Initiative completion` comment carrying the **evidence** (the merged Directives / PRs) and **requesting termination assessment**. It reports the fact and requests assessment; it does NOT assert the termination condition is met and does NOT close the Initiative вҖ” asserting completion is a strategic judgment that stays upstream (the same logic that forbids rejection).

Audit category: `initiative-feedback` (decisions: `challenge`, `completion`). The command never edits, closes, reopens, relabels, or retires the Initiative (M1.2 `initiative-readonly` is the runtime backstop); the only write is the structured comment. With В§5.22 the milestone-v2 model is **fully live** вҖ” recognition (M1.1) + enforcement (M1.2) + reviewer (M2) + consume (M3) + feedback (M4) + derived-view (the mirror's Project `Parent` field for Initiative-parented Directives, #262).

### 5.23 `/changelog` (Issue #346)

The in-flow **authoring affordance** for the В§18.1 fragment contract вҖ” the local pre-image of the remote CI gate (В§18.6), closing the "gate enforced but no in-flow authoring surface" gap that produced repeated post-hoc `chore(#N): add changelog fragment` commits (#320, #323, #325, #327, #329, #334; root cause #300). A prompt-driven skill (`.claude/commands/changelog.md`), script-less вҖ” the load-bearing work (inferring the Keep-a-Changelog category from the diff, judging skip-eligibility per В§18.7) is LLM reasoning. For the current PR/branch it does exactly one of:

- **Write a fragment** вҖ” resolve the allow-set (the PR number вҲӘ its `closingIssuesReferences`, computed the same way as `check-changelog.yml` вҖ” referenced, never re-derived), infer the category, and write `changelog_unreleased/<category>/<N>.md` as a single-line bullet per В§18.1.
- **Apply `skip-changelog`** вҖ” when the change is skip-eligible per В§18.7, `gh pr edit --add-label skip-changelog`.

`/changelog` is an **authoring** surface, not a `/changelog-check` lint surface (the В§18.5 non-goal): it produces the artifact or the label and **delegates all validation to the CI gate (В§18.6)** вҖ” it never re-implements the fragment-shape rules. Mode coupling (В§5.7.1): `attended` proposes the fragment draft (or a skip) for human confirmation; `unattended` runs the decision automatically (reviewer-substitution model, В§1.5). Invoked standalone or by the `/ship` pre-ready arm (В§5.7, step 7.7) when the gate is unsatisfied.

### 5.24 `/flush` (Issue #387; Directive #385)

The **flush** affordance of the context lifecycle (В§3.7) вҖ” the pre-clear distillation that makes a context clear an `active вҶ’ archived` transition rather than `active вҶ’ delete`. A prompt-driven skill (`.claude/commands/flush.md`), script-less вҖ” the load-bearing work (judging what task-scoped state is worth archiving, curating the PR body) is LLM reasoning. Before the operator clears the working context, `/flush` distills the reconstructable core (branch / issue / PR / phase / next step вҖ” the `status_compact` field set) into **at least one durable-memory artifact**:

- **PR body** вҖ” curated per the PR-as-living-doc rule (В§1.4) when a PR exists (the richest target);
- a **`.claude/state/` flush record** вҖ” the always-available target (a branch may have no PR yet), carrying the `status_compact` fields.

`/flush` **does not and cannot invoke** Claude Code's native `/clear` (outside the shell boundary, В§3.4) вҖ” it *precedes* a clear and makes it safe by guaranteeing the archive exists first; the reconstruct half is SessionStart restore (В§6.5(b)). Trigger is **explicit only** (operator- or skill-invoked); threshold automation is deferred (В§0.4, В§3.7). Mode coupling (В§5.7.1): `attended` proposes the flush targets for confirmation; `unattended` writes them automatically. Additive вҖ” no change to native `/clear`.

### 5.25 `/recall <topic>` (Issue #422)

The **selective-injection** affordance of the context dual (MISSION "The mechanism") вҖ” an on-demand query into durable memory's `active вҶ’ archived` half. SessionStart restore (В§6.5(b)) re-injects only the *current* task's artifacts; `/recall` retrieves *prior, unrelated* decisions from the decision record on demand, answering "have we addressed this shape before?" A thin command file (`.claude/commands/recall.md`) delegating to `helpers/recall.sh::recall_pointers`, mirroring the `/status` вҶ’ `status.sh` precedent (В§5.5).

`recall_pointers <topic>` fans out across the decision record's substrates and merges into one **pointers-only** list:
- closed issues вҖ” `gh search issues --state closed`;
- merged PRs вҖ” `gh search prs --state closed`;
- ADRs вҖ” title/H1 match over `docs/ADRs/*.md`.

**Pointers-only is the load-bearing narrowing safeguard** (MISSION; the same fixed-size-pointer discipline В§6.5(d) applies to the friction advisory): each result is one line вҖ” a tag (`#` / `PR#` / `ADR-NNNN`) + number + the one-line title вҖ” **never a body**. The guarantee is *structural*, not advisory: the `gh` arms project `--json number,title`, so a body is never fetched into reach (a later edit adding `body` to the projection is the one regression path вҖ” smoke pins against it). The count is **bounded**: a per-substrate cap `RECALL_LIMIT` (default 5, env-overridable; 15-line worst case) so no substrate starves the others and the worst-case context cost is fixed and documented. **Fail-open**: any `gh`/grep error (offline, rate-limited, unauthenticated) yields a single `recall: decision record unavailable` line вҖ” never a block, never a partial body dump.

**Two-tier design** (Issue #524). The paragraph above specifies the **light tier**; a **deep tier** extends it for the high-conviction case. The tiers share every safeguard (pointers-only, `RECALL_LIMIT`-bounded, fail-open); they differ only in *what corpus they reach* and *who may trigger them*.

- **Light tier** (today's behavior, UNCHANGED). Best-effort, pointers-only, fail-open, **assistant-auto-triggerable** at recall-shaped moments (before planning / a non-trivial decision). The `gh search` fan-out over closed issues / merged PRs / ADR titles described above. This is the reflex hot path.
- **Deep tier** (new). A **bounded comment-body search**, invoked **ONLY on explicit user intent** вҖ” natural-language conviction ("search the comments", "we surely decided this") or an explicit `--deep` flag вҖ” and **NEVER by the assistant's internal pre-planning reflex**. Mechanism: the deep tier runs its **own** `gh search` for a **bounded candidate set** (вүӨ `RECALL_LIMIT`) that вҖ” unlike the light tier вҖ” **includes open issues** (a decision under active discussion is exactly the high-conviction case, e.g. an open issue's comment thread), then fetches those candidates' comments (`gh issue view <n> --json comments`) and matches them **locally with a token-aware FIXED-STRING predicate** (`grep -F` on the whole topic, else on any topic token вүҘ 3 chars вҖ” no regex/tokenizer), so dotted-version tokens like `3.12` that `gh search`'s server-side tokenizer drops are still found. The **candidate search itself is token-aware** (#526): it issues the whole-topic `gh search` first and, only if that returns **zero candidates** вҖ” GitHub free-text applies **AND** semantics, so a multi-token natural-language phrase whose tokens do not co-occur in any single issue's title/body finds nothing вҖ” **falls back** to re-querying per high-signal token (вүҘ 3 chars, the *same* tokenizer the local predicate uses), merging and deduping the hits under the same `RECALL_LIMIT` bound. This makes stage 1 (the candidate gate) **symmetric** with the OR-tolerant local predicate it feeds rather than strictly narrower: without it, the local predicate's token-tolerance is unreachable for exactly the discursive queries the deep tier exists to serve, since a candidate never fetched is never matched. The fallback fires only on the 0-candidate path and only under `--deep`, and each per-token query is fail-open (a `gh` error degrades to the light-tier result, never errors, never partial-dumps a body). It emits **only the pointers the light tier did not already print** (deduped against the light output), so a comment match on an already-surfaced closed issue never double-prints and the deep tier's contribution is the genuinely *new* pointers (chiefly open-issue comment decisions the closed-only light tier cannot reach). **Pointers-only is preserved structurally**: the local grep is a **predicate** (match / no-match) вҖ” the emitted output is only the `#<n> title` pointer, and the matched comment text is **never emitted**.

**Trigger asymmetry.** The light tier is **reflex-triggerable** by the assistant; the deep tier is **explicit-user-intent-only**. The routing contract itself is carried by the skill `description:` string on `.claude/commands/recall.md` (Claude Code matches natural-language intent against it вҖ” light-recall intent to the reflex path, comment-conviction intent to the deep path) plus the CLAUDE.md recall-routing norm. The rationale is the **cost-of-miss asymmetry** (В§6.0): the reflex is a **low-prior + cheap-miss** situation (light tier, fail-open, a wrong *allow* costs nothing вҖ” so it earns auto-trigger), whereas user conviction is a **high-prior + expensive-miss** situation (deep tier justified вҖ” but explicit-intent-only, so the comment fetch never spends context on the reflex hot path).

Out of scope / residual (Issues #422, #524):
- a vector/embedding store (the v0 substrate is `gh search` + `git grep` + the bounded comment fetch); changing В§6.5(b) injection; auto-running `/recall` without an explicit invocation (the `/work-on` pre-planning step is a deferred follow-up).
- **Deep tier is matched-issues-only.** It surfaces a comment-borne decision **when the topic reaches the candidate set** вҖ” i.e. the parent issue is found via the deep tier's own (open + closed) `gh search` hit (whole-topic first, else the per-token fallback above), then one of those candidates' comments carries the token-aware fixed-string match. Two cases must be distinguished:
  - **Multi-token natural-language phrase whose tokens *do* reach candidates individually** вҖ” e.g. `"мҡҙмҳҒ мқён„°н”„лҰ¬н„° 3.12 vs 3.14"`, where `мқён„°н”„лҰ¬н„°` / `3.14` each appear in some issue's title/body but the AND-joined whole phrase matches none. This was a **stage-1/stage-2 asymmetry bug** (the whole-topic candidate search returned 0 and the OR-tolerant local predicate never ran) and is **fixed** by the per-token candidate fallback (#526): each high-signal token re-queries the candidate set, so the parent issue is reached and its comment matched.
  - **No-shared-token residual (accepted, v0).** A decision recorded in a comment on an issue whose **title and body share no token with the query** вҖ” the token-tolerant candidate fallback still finds nothing, because *no* token reaches any candidate. Closing this fully requires the semantic / full-corpus search that is out of scope, and leaving it open is consistent with В§5.25's fail-open / bounded / best-effort ethos. A bare dotted query like `3.12` is the limiting sub-case: it is a single вүҘ3-char token, so the fallback *does* re-query it, but `gh search`'s server-side tokenizer drops the dotted form, so it still yields zero candidates unless a co-occurring token (e.g. `python`) brings the parent issue into the set.

**Routing disposition** (positive enforcement, В§6.0) вҖ” distinct from, and *not* a reversal of, the deferred forced auto-run just above. The agent **reaches for `/recall` at recall-shaped moments**: both **user-asked** ("have we addressed X before?", "what did we decide about Y?") and **self-identified** вҖ” an internal "have we decided this shape before?" beat before planning or a non-trivial decision. This is a **judgment-based** nudge laid generously, not a gate: a missed recall is recoverable (the wrong *allow* costs nothing), which is exactly why it earns the positive face вҖ” whereas a *forced* injection on every phase has the opposite cost-asymmetry (a wrong forced inject spends context that cannot be un-spent) and so **stays deferred**. The disposition above is the **light tier**; the **deep** comment sweep is deliberately outside it вҖ” reachable by explicit user intent only, never the pre-planning reflex вҖ” **with one bounded escalation** (#528): when a light `/recall` the assistant ran *for a user-asked substantive / answer-seeking question* returns **no matches (empty)**, the assistant **escalates once** to `--deep` as a single follow-up sweep, without the user having to type `--deep` or "search the comments". This is **not a reversal** of "explicit-user-intent-only" but a refinement that stays inside the cost-of-miss asymmetry (В§6.0; "Trigger asymmetry" above): deep fires **only after the cheap tier has already missed**, and **only on the high-conviction user-asked branch** вҖ” the **self-identified pre-planning** beat still **never auto-escalates** (that would be the forbidden deep-as-reflex, and the wrong-forced-inject cost that keeps it deferred). An empty light result on a substantive user ask is itself the high-prior signal the deep tier was built for, so paying its cost there is the *cheap-miss-already-realized* case, not a speculative spend. The lever is the trigger-oriented `description:` frontmatter of `.claude/commands/recall.md` (Claude Code matches natural-language recall intent to the skill on it) plus the CLAUDE.md recall-routing norm. The disposition never fetches a body вҖ” the pointers-only safeguard holds (both tiers) вҖ” and following a pointer is a separate targeted read, only if relevant.

### 5.26 `/replan-check` (Issue #427)

The **in-loop correction** of the selective-injection half вҖ” a checkpoint that keeps the Plan (a task-scoped injection manifest, MISSION "The mechanism") reflecting truth as execution proceeds. `planner` is one-shot (then `plan-reviewer`); without this, a Plan the actual diff has outgrown silently stops being a faithful manifest, eroding PR-as-living-doc (В§1.4). A thin command (`.claude/commands/replan-check.md`) delegating mechanical fact-gathering to `helpers/replan_check.sh`, with the divergence **judgment** kept in the skill (LLM) вҖ” the `/recall`вҶ’`recall.sh` split.

`replan_check.sh` surfaces only the mechanical facts, fail-open: the actually-touched files (`git diff --name-only <base>...HEAD`, `<base>` from `gh pr view --json baseRefName`, default `main`), the linked issue's AC checkboxes, and the PR-body `## Plan` / `## Checklist` / `## Key context` / `## Out of scope` (a touched file the Plan declared out-of-scope is a strong structural signal). The skill then applies the **structural-vs-cosmetic discriminator**:

- **Structural вҶ’ re-invoke `planner`** (mirroring `/work-on` step 6; in `unattended`, a clean `plan-reviewer` re-substitutes for approval): EITHER (a) the diff touches a **load-bearing** file/area the Plan/Checklist/Key-context never anticipated (a new module, a schema/contract surface, an un-named subsystem) вҖ” *not* a mechanical incidental; OR (b) an **AC is rendered unreachable** вҖ” the approach taken closes off a path a linked-issue acceptance criterion required.
- **Cosmetic вҶ’ no trigger** (a one-line advisory at most): files that are the **direct mechanical consequence** of a planned change (a regenerated TOC, a changelog fragment, the SSOT-coupling the Plan already implies вҖ” e.g. the В§8 tree bump for a planned helper), in-scope reordering/renaming, or any change leaving every AC reachable.

The threshold is **asymmetric by design** (В§6.0): re-invoking `planner` is expensive and the judgment is fallible, so it **fails toward not-triggering** вҖ” when in doubt, emit the advisory, do not re-plan. This is **positive enforcement** (a guiding checkpoint), not a hard gate; a missed nudge is recoverable, a wrong forced re-plan is not. `/sync-pr` (В§5.4) references it as a post-sync advisory step (the body was just curated вҖ” the natural cadence to compare it against the diff); `/ship` inherits the reference transitively (В§5.7 step 5). Trigger is explicit/invoked вҖ” the auto-on-every-phase-commit variant is deferred (parallel to В§5.25's auto-`/recall` deferral).

### 5.27 `/reconcile-spec` (Issue #464; Directive #455)

The **judgment + action** half of code-vs-SPEC drift reconciliation вҖ” the consumer of the measure-first detector `scripts/spec_drift_candidates.sh` (В§6.5(d), #462). The detector surfaces code-ahead drift *candidates*; `/reconcile-spec` reads the relevant SPEC section(s) and the drifted commits/code and classifies each candidate into **exactly one of three dispositions, before any SPEC edit**:

- **spec-ahead** вҖ” SPEC leads, the code is still being implemented вҶ’ **track, no edit**.
- **code-ahead-correct** вҖ” the code is right and SPEC is stale вҶ’ **propose a SPEC update to match the code**, applied **only after explicit user approval**.
- **code-wrong** вҖ” the code is a bug and SPEC is right вҶ’ **never edit SPEC**; route to a code fix / file a bug.

**The load-bearing invariant (Directive #455): the shell never silently rewrites SPEC to match possibly-buggy code.** Disposition `code-wrong` *never* edits SPEC, and `code-ahead-correct` edits it *only* after explicit user approval вҖ” the correction is human judgment, never the shell's autonomous act. **Operating mode**: in `attended` the command surfaces the classification + proposed edit and pauses for approval before applying; in `unattended` it **never auto-applies** a SPEC correction (a SPEC-to-match-code edit is a content/direction change, and the directing layer never autonomously sets direction вҖ” В§1.7) вҖ” it surfaces/parks the candidate instead. Classification *correctness* is agent judgment (mirroring `/onboard`'s SSOT-drafting half), not a mechanically-verified property.

Each handled candidate is audit-logged under the **`spec-reconcile`** category with its decision: `applied` (a `code-ahead-correct` SPEC edit, after approval), `tracked` (`spec-ahead`), `routed` (`code-wrong` вҶ’ code fix / bug), or `parked` (surfaced in `unattended`, not applied). Full procedure lives in `.claude/commands/reconcile-spec.md`. Escape: `SKIP_HOOKS=<cat> SKIP_REASON='<why>'` per В§7.

### 5.28 `/implement` (Issue #486; Directive #477)

The **default Code-phase author** вҖ” runs Phase C (Code) in the write-capable `implementer` subagent (В§4.12) instead of the main loop, so the within-Execution authoring churn (file reads, abandoned approaches, lint/smoke iterations) stays out of the main assistant's context. `/implement <issue#>` is the action-form of the В§1.2 / В§3.7 discard-boundary-at-Execution principle.

**Default-with-opt-out invariant (Directive #477 signal-4).** The Code phase routes here **by default** вҖ” `/work-on` step "Phase C" dispatches `/implement`. The **opt-out** is for trivial / one-line / glue edits and the orchestrator's own glue (Directive #477 Non-goal 2), which the main assistant authors directly. The default-flip descopes the original A/B measurement gate: the context-narrowing hypothesis is adopted as operating policy on circumstantial evidence (the convergent mainstream pattern + the native subagent context-discard), hedged by **fail-open reversibility** вҖ” a missing implementer path degrades to main-loop authoring and the documented opt-out makes the default revertible вҖ” rather than by a measured non-worse result. Auto-routing lives in the `/work-on` doc procedure only, **never** in a Stop / PostToolUse hook.

**Manifest contract (input the command assembles).** The subagent has no access to the conversation, so the command gathers the explicit manifest first: the **Plan** (PR-body `## Plan` / `## Checklist`, the planner output В§4.1), the **failing Phase-B test** + the exact command to run it, and the **named relevant file paths** (PR-body `## Key context`). A missing Plan or failing test means the manifest is incomplete вҖ” finish Phase A/B first. Before spawning, the command also **surfaces/warns on a dirty working tree** (`git status`): a clean tree is expected once the Phase-A Doc and Phase-B Test commits have landed, so a dirty tree signals uncommitted glue the implementer's path-scoped add (В§4.12) must not sweep in. This is a **surface/warn, not a hard block** вҖ” a legitimately dirty tree must not stall the flow, and the fail-open posture is unchanged.

**Structured-return contract (output the command absorbs).** Spawn `subagent_type: implementer` on the manifest; absorb **only** its structured return вҖ” (a) commit/diff ref(s), (b) plan-deviations, (c) discoveries вҖ” never the working churn. A **structural** plan-deviation (out-of-plan load-bearing file, an AC rendered unreachable) follows the `/replan-check` discriminator (В§5.26): re-invoke `planner`, then `/sync-pr`; a cosmetic deviation needs at most a one-line advisory.

**В§4.9.3 session-restart caveat.** A freshly-added `subagent_type: implementer` falls back to `general-purpose` until the next session restart; `implementer.md`'s self-describing prompt makes the fallback functionally complete (only the Type-aware tool restriction is lost), restart is canonical. The implementer authors its commit in the **work language** (В§5.7.2). Full procedure lives in `.claude/commands/implement.md`.

---

## 6. Hook enforcement

### 6.0 Enforcement style

The action-axis principle of MISSION "The mechanism" вҖ” enforcement has a *negative* face (block a wrong action) and a *positive* face (supply the right next one), and both are necessary вҖ” lands here as the design rule for every matcher, command, and reviewer the shell adds. The В§6.1 **Framing** paragraph below states the negative side's posture (a mistake-prevention guardrail, not a sandbox); this section is the cross-cutting rule that decides, for any given discipline, *which* face to give it and *where* to put it. Of the rules below, **P1, P3, and P4 derive from** that MISSION principle; **P2 is SPEC-local** вҖ” an engineering-physics rule about *where* a given enforcement runs (local hook vs remote backstop), with no MISSION parent.

**P1 вҖ” Cost-asymmetry selects the face (the criterion).** Choose negative vs positive by the cost of being *wrong*, not by how important the rule feels. Where a wrong *allow* is irreversible or corrupts shared history вҖ” a force-push onto a protected branch, a leaked secret, a destructive `rm` вҖ” the rule is a hard negative gate that **fails safe toward blocking**; the force-push matcher (В§6.1) reasons exactly this way (a wrong allow clobbers shared protected history вҖ” irreversible; a wrong block costs naming the branch вҖ” recoverable). Where a wrong *nudge* is simply ignored at no cost вҖ” a `next:` hint, a scaffolding command вҖ” the rule is positive and is laid generously. Corollary: **negative gates are narrow and precise, positive guidance is broad and abundant**, because the two failure costs are asymmetric (the type-aware carve-outs of В§6.1 are negative gates being made *more precise* to avoid false blocks, not weaker).

**P2 вҖ” Enforcement physics: pick the layer for the bypass model.** A local PreToolUse hook fires pre-action but is **bypassable** (eval, `bash -c`, dynamic construction вҖ” see В§6.1 Framing); a remote gate (CI, branch protection) fires later but is **unbypassable** and runs regardless of who acts. An irreversible rule therefore cannot rely on the local hook alone вҖ” it needs a remote backstop, with the local hook as its **pre-image** (the in-flow, fast-feedback copy of the remote check; e.g. the local changelog presence check is the pre-image of the `check-changelog` CI gate, В§18). Reversible / hygiene rules can live at the local layer only.

**P3 вҖ” The face is not fixed; it migrates with trust.** A rule is typically born **advisory** (a reviewer or skill recommendation), **hardened** into a hook once the pattern proves out (e.g. #199 promoted the advisory #197 labelвҶ”parent layer into the `label-parent-consistency` matcher вҖ” В§6.1), and **narrowed** again if it starts fighting the prescribed flow (the force-push matcher was relaxed from a blanket block to allow the named-branch force-push of the В§13 rebase-pull tail). This migration is the action-axis form of "the shell improves under use" (MISSION). The two directions were historically **not equally observable**: narrowing pressure shows in the audit log (escape clustering on one category/reason вҖ” В§7; the MISSION success signal "the escape hatch stays narrow"), surfaced by `scripts/narrowing_candidates.sh`. Promotion pressure once left no audit trace вҖ” an ignored advisory was invisible вҖ” but the reviewer-reject reason-class trail (#361) now records each non-pass reviewer verdict (issue-/plan-/activation-reviewer) with a categorized token, and `scripts/promotion_candidates.sh` aggregates those into advisoryвҶ’hook promotion candidates above a threshold. Both directions are thus observable; the narrow/promote decision still stays human / reviewer judgment (the consumers **surface** candidates, they do not act вҖ” tracking #41 principle #3). **The audit log is a *dual-positive* channel (Directive #356):** a block's in-band message is its immediate positive face (it names the alternative, P4), and the line it appends to `audit.jsonl` is a *deferred* positive face вҖ” but that line is only **latently** positive: it becomes an actionable positive channel solely once a consumer is wired to read the aggregate (the two scripts above). An unconsumed log is an inert record, not a positive channel; wiring the consumer is what completes the deferred positive face. **That consumer is now wired (#398, Directive #391):** the SessionStart В§6.5(d) friction advisory triggers the two readers (plus the `unattended-park` park-frequency signal bridged in by В§5.7.1) once per session, TTL-gated and fail-open, surfacing accumulated friction as a one-line pointer without a human remembering to run a script вҖ” so the deferred positive face is no longer latent. A third reader, `scripts/ceremony_candidates.sh` (#401), extends the same surface to **ceremony** mis-sizing вҖ” mined from commit history rather than `audit.jsonl` (the ceremony signal is not recorded there) вҖ” and is itself **born advisory**: it observes whether ceremony mis-sizing recurs *before* any В§1.2 weight model or relaxation gate is hardened against it, the P3 order applied to the device's own roadmap. The narrow/promote decision still stays human / reviewer judgment (the advisory **surfaces**, it does not act вҖ” tracking #41 principle #3).

**P4 вҖ” Pair the faces; never ship a bare gate.** A negative gate names its positive alternative in the block message (a `status:proposed` branch attempt is blocked with "run `/activate <N>`"; a bare force-push is blocked with "name the target branch") вҖ” a block that only says "no" is half a rule. Defaults reinforce the pairing: enforcement **fails open** (a missing helper warns and proceeds, never locks the developer out вҖ” see the В§6.1 fail-policy table) and the **escape hatch is always open but audited** (В§7). A reviewer is the paired form inside one agent вҖ” it produces an artifact (positive) and gates on a verdict (negative), a *generative gate* (В§1.5). Evaluate any enforcement proposal against this: a hard block with no named alternative, or guidance with no gate behind it, is the one-sided regression MISSION warns of.

### 6.1 PreToolUse вҖ” block

**Framing**: Hooks are a **mistake-prevention guardrail**, not a security boundary. An adversarial user can bypass them via shell features the matcher doesn't model (`eval`, `bash -c`, `python -c`, heredoc-spawned shells, dynamic command construction via parameter expansion). The hook's job is to stop honest mistakes вҖ” typos, autopilot moments, the wrong tab вҖ” not to be a sandbox. Patterns that suggest a bypass attempt are not blocked but are **audit-logged as warnings** so the trail is preserved for review.

Implementation note: command strings are **normalized** before matching вҖ” backslash-continued multiline (`\\\n`) collapses to single-space, internal newlines become spaces, multi-space whitespace collapses. So `git \\\n  push \\\n  --force-with-lease` matches the same blocked pattern as the single-line form. Normalization also **re-separates a glued unquoted command separator** (`&&`, `||`, `;`, `|`, and a lone background `&`) into a space-padded segment boundary, so an operator glued to an adjacent token вҖ” `git commit -m "x"&&git push --force origin main`, no space before `&&` вҖ” does not get folded into a single token by the `parse_env_prefix` shlex round-trip and dissolve the following `git push` verb (the entry-grep keys on `git push`, so a destroyed verb is a **false-negative** on the force-push/protected gate вҖ” В§6.0 P1, #446). Only separators **outside** quoted string values are split: a `&&`/`;`/`|`/`&` *inside* a quoted `-m`/`--message` value is data, not a boundary, and is never re-separated (no invented boundary вҖ” composes with the #440 message-value elision). A lone `&` that is part of a **redirect** (`>&`, `&>`, `N>&M`, `<&`, `&>>` вҖ” i.e. immediately adjacent to `>` or `<`) is a redirect operator, not a background separator, and is **never** re-separated, so a legitimate `git push --force origin feature 2>&1` is not over-blocked (#476). `push_segments` splits on the same set (incl. `&`), so a glued `&` cannot collapse a sibling clause's protected-looking token into the `git push` segment (#437 sibling-isolation parity). The glued and spaced forms of every separator are therefore treated identically by every downstream git matcher.

**Git option-prefix tolerance**: every `git <subcommand>` matcher accepts standard git-level options between `git` and the subcommand: `-c <key>=<value>`, `-C <path>`, `--git-dir=<path>`, `--work-tree=<path>`, `--no-pager`, `--literal-pathspecs`, `--exec-path[=<path>]`, `--namespace=<ref>`. So `git -c commit.gpgsign=false commit -m "вҖҰ"` and `git -C /some/repo push --force` both fire the same downstream checks as the bare `git commit` / `git push` forms вҖ” the option prefix can no longer be used (intentionally or not) to slip past the matcher.

**Type-awareness** (introduced alongside dir-mode, В§1.7; matchers wired by tracking #41 child #5, issue #46): the engineering-flow matchers below вҖ” branch-from-issue, AC-closeout, PR-link / `Closes #N` checks, default `gh issue list` wrappers вҖ” **do not apply their engineering-flow gate to a `Type=Directive` Issue**. Directive Issues are gated by `/complete-directive` + `activation-reviewer` (В§4.9), not by AC checkboxes or `Closes #N` semantics. (For **AC-closeout** specifically the carve-out is **all-or-nothing**, not per-item: the `gh pr merge` gate is skipped only when **every** closing Issue is a Directive вҖ” a mixed PR closing both a Directive and an Execution Issue still gates on the Execution Issue's unchecked AC; see the AC-closeout matcher row below.) The `proposed-protect` matcher in the table is the inverse: it actively blocks engineering-flow actions (most prominently `/work-on`) when the target Issue is **either** `status:proposed` (any type вҖ” not-yet-activated work, generalized by #171) **or** a Directive (any status вҖ” Directives never branch, В§10.5). The two conditions guard distinct invariants (lifecycle vs type) that share one branch-creation trigger; `proposed-protect` subsumes the former `directive-protect` rather than replacing it (a status-only check would let an Active Directive become branchable вҖ” a В§10.5 regression). The implementation predicates (`is_directive_issue <issue-#>`, cached; and `is_proposed_issue <issue-#>`, uncached because the `status:proposed` label is volatile under `/activate`) and the `safe_source` fail-policy entry live in `helpers/issue_type.sh` (#46, #171).

| Trigger | Check | Escape category |
|---------|-------|----------------|
| `git commit` pattern | If on a protected branch (`main`/`master`/`release/*`), block. Detached HEAD on the tip commit of any protected branch is treated the same вҖ” the matcher resolves `HEAD` against `refs/heads/{main,master}` and `refs/heads/release/*` and blocks when they share a SHA. **Case-insensitive name match (#555 A7):** the branch-*name* test (`is_protected_branch`) matches `main`/`master`/`release/*` case-insensitively, parity with the force-push arm's `grep -qiE` вҖ” so a `Main`/`MASTER` checkout on a case-insensitive filesystem (which resolves to the same ref) is recognized as protected rather than silently slipping past the commit/edit gates. | `branch` |
| `git commit -m "..."` | Conventional Commits format. Issue # required per type (В§6.1.1) | `commit-format` |
| `git commit` | Secret scan over staged diff. On hit, emits `<file>:<line>: <pattern-id>` per location (no body content) plus the legacy summary line. Honors `.shellsecretignore` at the target repo root: gitignore-narrow (glob, prefix-match for trailing `/`; no negation, no `**`).
