The default file at the shell-repo root lists component-aware test/example globs (`tests/`, `test/`, `*_test.*`, `*.test.*`, `*-test.*`, `*test_*.*`, `examples/`, `example/`, `*-example.*`, `*_example.*`, `*.example.*`), plus `docs/` and `*.md` вҖ” the file is the authoritative set. `.shellsecretignore` is the SPEC В§7 tuning mechanism for path-based false positives вҖ” repeated `SKIP_HOOKS=secret` escapes on fixture paths mean an allow-list entry is needed, not a normalized bypass. | `secret` |
| `git commit` | Quick lint/format check, bounded by `GHJIG_LINT_TIMEOUT` (default 30 s; "quick" enforced) | `format` |
| `git commit --allow-empty` | **No carve-out** вҖ” an empty commit goes through the same four gates as any commit (branch + commit-format + secret + lint). An empty commit is still a protected-branch write and still carries a subject; the secret and lint checks are harmless no-ops on an empty staged set. (Closed the `--allow-empty` matcher-entry bypass, #209.) | `branch`/`commit-format`/`secret`/`format` |
| `git commit --amend` | **Block only when the commit is already on upstream.** Local amend allowed | `amend` |
| `git commit --no-verify` | Block | `no-verify` |
| `git push` with a force variant (`--force`/`-f`/`--force-with-lease`) | **Allowed only to an explicitly-named non-protected branch** (`git push --force-with-lease origin <branch>`) вҖ” the normal tail of the rebase-pull motion when the base advances (В§13), so blanket-blocking it fought the prescribed flow. **Blocked** in two cases: (a) a **protected** branch (`main`/`master`/`release/*`) named in the force-bearing `git push` **segment** (block message names "protected"); (b) a **bare or remote-only** force-push with **no explicit target branch** вҖ” the block message instructs the user to name the target (`git push --force-with-lease origin <branch>`). **Segment isolation (#437):** like the protected-push (`branch`) arm (#366), the force-push arm now heredoc-strips the command and isolates the actual `git push` segment(s) via `push_segments`, then re-confirms the force flag, the protected token, the `--mirror/--all/--branches` refset, and the explicit-target positional count **per force-bearing push segment** вҖ” so a force flag, protected token, or target named in a **sibling non-push segment** (`git push --force-with-lease origin <feat> && gh pr create --base main`) or a **heredoc body** no longer false-trips the gate. If the force flag turns out to live only in a non-push sibling, the command is not a force-push and is allowed. **Multi-push-segment:** blocks if **any** force-bearing push segment is protected/refset/bare (fail-safe). **Heredoc-only strip** (not quote-stripping) preserves zero false-negatives on a genuine quoted protected force-push, and a strip failure / missing `python3` returns the command unstripped (segmentation only ever drops non-push segments) вҖ” so a real protected force-push always still matches. **Message-value strip (#440):** the arm uses `strip_command_data`'s `message` mode вҖ” it additionally elides the *argument values* of `-m`/`--message`/`-F`/`--file` (commit-message data, in `=`-glued/quoted/bareword form) before segmenting, so a force/protected literal documented inside a commit **message body** (`git commit -m "вҖҰ git push --force вҖҰ main вҖҰ"`) is treated as data, not a command, and no longer false-trips. The elision is anchored strictly to the message-flag token, so a quoted push **target** (`origin "main"` вҖ” no preceding message-flag) is never removed; an unclosed message quote fails closed to unstripped (today's recoverable false-trip, never an over-strip that drops a genuine target). **Why the bare form is blocked rather than HEAD-resolved (fail-safe on ambiguity):** a no-refspec push's real destination is config-dependent (`push.default`, the branch's configured upstream, `remote.*.push` refspecs), so the current branch *name* is not a reliable proxy for what gets written вҖ” a feature branch whose upstream is `origin/main` would otherwise let a bare force-push clobber `main`. The hook cannot verify a bare push's true target, so it fails safe to block and tells the user to make the target explicit. **"Verified target" definition:** a push with an explicit positional refspec вҖ” `origin <branch>`, `origin HEAD`, or `origin HEAD:<ref>` вҖ” counts as a named target (the positional-argument count sees it) and is allowed when non-protected; only a **no-positional** bare/remote-only form (`git push --force`, `git push --force origin`) is blocked. `HEAD` is accepted as explicit-named even though its *remote* destination is, like a bare push, config-dependent вҖ” the asymmetry is a deliberate choice: a user who typed `origin HEAD` has named the source ref explicitly (the common rebase-pull-tail form, В§13), whereas a no-positional push has named nothing, so only the latter is treated as unverifiable. Cost asymmetry justifies it: a wrong allow clobbers shared protected history (irreversible); a wrong block costs naming the branch or one audited `SKIP_HOOKS=force-push` escape (recoverable). **Bundled short-force detection (#555 A4):** the force-flag test (both the entry pre-filter and the per-segment re-confirm) recognizes a **bundled short cluster** вҖ” `git push -uf` / `-fu` вҖ” via a token-start-anchored `(^|space)-[A-Za-z]*f[A-Za-z]*` pattern, not only an isolated `-f`; pre-fix a bundled `-uf` carried no `-f\b` token so a **bare bundled force-push** slipped past the fail-safe entirely. The token-start anchor keeps a branch **name** containing `-f` (`my-feature`) from being misread as a force flag (no over-block). | `force-push` |
| `git push origin main`, etc. | Direct push to a protected branch blocked. **Push-target resolution (#366):** detection scans the **`git push` command segment(s)** for a protected token, not a resolved destination. The command is first **heredoc-stripped** вҖ” heredoc bodies removed via the shared `strip_command_data` helper (`heredoc` mode; factored from #340's `is_pr_merge_command`) вҖ” then **split on unquoted `&&`/`;`/`\|`/newline**, keeping only segments that contain a `git push` token; the protected-token grep runs per push segment. So a protected token that appears only inside a **heredoc body** (`cat <<EOF вҖҰ git push вҖҰ main вҖҰ EOF`) or in a **sibling non-push segment** (`git push origin <feat> && gh pr create --base main`) no longer false-trips the gate. **Quoted string literals are deliberately NOT stripped on the push arm** (unlike the `gh pr merge` arm): the push *target* is a positional that may legitimately be quoted, so quote-stripping could drop a genuine quoted protected target (`git push origin "main"`) and miss a real push вҖ” heredoc-only stripping preserves the zero-false-negative guarantee. **Fail-closed (zero false-negatives for genuine pushes):** a heredoc-strip failure or missing `python3` returns the command unstripped, and segmentation only ever *drops* non-push segments вҖ” so a real `git push origin main` (bare, `-u`, `HEAD:main` refspec, env-prefixed, in a non-first `&&` segment, or with a quoted target) always still matches. **Not caught here:** a bare push whose configured upstream is protected with no token in the command text вҖ” remote branch protection and the force-push arm are the backstops (out of scope, #366). **Accepted residual:** a protected token inside a *standalone* feature-branch slug (`git push origin release/x`) still trips вҖ” fail-safe-to-block, escapable via `SKIP_HOOKS=branch`. **Alias-rename residual (#503):** `git -c alias.<x>=push <x> origin main` invokes the gated verb under an alias *name*, so the `${GIT_PREFIX}push` verb grep never sees `push` вҖ” a contrived bypass of the same class as the `eval`/`bash -c` row below, left as a documented residual. (The *realistic* gap вҖ” an UNLISTED valid leading global flag such as `--no-lazy-fetch` dropping the whole verb match вҖ” IS closed: GIT_PREFIX carries a generic trailing `--long[=v]` / `-X` alternative, В§6.1 `git_matcher.sh`, so only the alias-rename and a space-separated value of an unlisted flag remain residual.) **Message-value strip (#440):** this arm also uses `message` mode, so a protected token documented inside a commit **message body** is elided as data (the strip is anchored to the `-m`/`-F` flag, so a quoted push target is preserved; unclosed message quote вҶ’ fail-closed unstripped). | `branch` |
| `/work-on <N>` (or equivalent branch-creation referencing Issue `<N>`) | Block when Issue `<N>` is `status:proposed` (any type) **or** `Type=Directive` (any status, В§1.7). `status:proposed` вҶ’ *"Issue is `status:proposed` вҖ” run `/activate <N>` (once available) to validate it before branching."* Active Directive вҶ’ *"Directive Issue вҖ” Directives do not branch directly into PRs; use `/file-issue --parent <N>`."* (#46 landed the Directive arm; #171 generalized to the `status:proposed` arm.) | `proposed-protect` |
| `rm`/`mv`/`cp` carrying a force **or** recursive flag with args pointing outside registry (e.g. `rm -rf ~/.claude`, `rm -rf /`, `rm -rf ${HOME}/x`) | Block. The entry pre-filter recognizes the flag in **any** surface form вҖ” clustered (`-rf`), separated (`-r -f`), long (`--force`, `--recursive`), non-first (`-i -rf`), **or placed after operands** (`rm <path> -rf`, valid GNU syntax вҖ” #277) вҖ” spanning operands between the verb and the flag but **stopping at a pipeline boundary** (`;` `|` `&`) so a flag belonging to another pipeline command does not trigger it (#212 cross-command anchoring preserved; the flag is matched as a whole token, so a `-rf` inside a filename is not a false trigger). Arg parsing is shell-aware (quotes preserved, no glob expansion via the hook); recognizes `~`, `$HOME`, and `${HOME}` forms; bare relative names are resolved against PWD and routed through `path_in_scope`. **Flagless `mv`/`cp` (#505):** a flagless `mv`/`cp` carrying an operand also enters `check_destructive_args` (every operand is scope-checked), so `mv in /out` clobbering an out-of-registry **dest** is now gated; `rm` is intentionally NOT broadened (an unforced single-file `rm` stays un-gated, #212). **Residual (#505):** `find вҖҰ -delete` / `find вҖҰ -exec rm`, `truncate`, and `>`/`>>` redirect clobbers to out-of-registry paths are NOT gated вҖ” shell-feature breadth of the same class as the `eval`/`bash -c` warn-only residual, left documented rather than modeled. **`--` end-of-options guard (#555 A3):** the flagless `mv`/`cp` entry arm skips an optional leading `--` before its operand test, so `mv -- <src> <out-of-registry>` still ENTERS `check_destructive_args` instead of evading both arms (the raw operand test saw the `--` and bailed); `--` is treated as a flag (skipped) by the operand scan, so an all-in-scope `mv -- a b` still passes. **Command-position skip (#555 A5):** `check_destructive_args` skips the verb/wrapper words (`rm`/`mv`/`cp`/`sudo`/`doas`/`time`/`env`) ONLY in the leading wrapperвҶ’verb prefix вҖ” pre-fix it skipped ANY token equal to those words regardless of position, so an OPERAND literally named `env`/`time`/etc. (`mv <in-scope> env`) skipped `path_in_scope` entirely; every operand after the verb is now scope-checked. | `out-of-scope` |
| `eval`, `bash -c`, `sh -c`, `python -c`, heredoc-spawned shells (`bash <<EOF`) | Don't block. Audit-log as `warn` with category `bypass-suspect` so the trail exists. Hooks are guardrails, not sandboxes. | (warn-only) |
| `git reset --hard` | Block. **Message-value strip (#555 A2):** like the push arms, the reset arm strips `-m`/`--message`/`-F`/`--file` values (`strip_command_data` `message` mode) before the `reset --hard` grep, so a `git reset --hard` mentioned only inside a commit **message** (`git commit -m "note git reset --hard"`) is data, not a command, and no longer false-blocks; a real invocation still blocks (the strip never removes a genuine command verb). | `destructive` |
| `git clean` with a force-flag cluster (`-f`, `-df`, `-xdf`, `-ff`, вҖҰ вҖ” the matcher is `clean\s+-[A-Za-z]*f`, so any short-flag cluster containing `f` blocks, not only the bare `-f`) | Block. Like the push arm (#366), the command is **heredoc-stripped** (`strip_command_data` `heredoc` mode) before the `clean -вҖҰf` grep, so the token appearing only inside a `cat <<EOF` body does not false-trip; a real `git clean -f`/`-fd` invocation still blocks. (Heredoc-only, not quote-stripping, by parity with the push arm вҖ” keeps a real `-f` flag undroppable.) **Message-value strip (#555 A2):** the clean arm's refinement now uses `message` mode (вҠҮ heredoc), additionally eliding a `-m`/`-F` commit-message value, so a `git clean -f` documented inside a commit message no longer false-blocks; a real `-f` flag is never a message value, so this cannot under-block. | `destructive` |
| `git merge <protected>` (e.g. `git merge main`, `git merge origin/main`, `git merge release/v1`) on a non-protected branch | Block as a **backmerge**. The recommended motion when the base advances is `git pull --rebase origin <base>` per В§13; merging the base into the feature branch makes a noisy bubble that muddies the per-PR commit graph. Allowed when currently on the protected branch itself (e.g. merging a PR locally on `main`). | `backmerge` |
| Edit/Write target path outside the registry (except `$GHJIG_ROOT/` prefix = shell self-modification; and `$HOME/.claude/` prefix = user-global auto-memory tier, issue #91) | Block. **Carve-out path normalization (#555 A1):** the two carve-out prefix matches run against a **lexically-normalized** `$target` (made absolute against cwd, then a pure-string collapse of `.`/`..` segments вҖ” **no** `pwd -P`/`realpath`/filesystem access), not the raw path вҖ” so a `..`-laden absolute path (`$GHJIG_ROOT/../../etc/passwd`) can no longer borrow a carve-out prefix to skip the out-of-scope gate; a traversal that escapes the root normalizes outside it and falls through to the block. Lexical (not physical) is required because an Edit/Write routinely targets a **not-yet-existing** path and a carve-out ancestor may be **absent** (e.g. `$HOME/.claude` on a fresh CI runner) вҖ” a physical resolve there falls back to the raw path and the bypass re-opens, so the normalization must hold regardless of what exists on disk. A genuine in-root edit still normalizes under the root and is carved out (no over-block); the sensitive-file check fires under both carve-outs regardless (#210). | `out-of-scope` |
| Edit/Write on `.env`, `*.pem`, `credentials*`, `id_rsa*`, `id_ed25519*` | Block (applies regardless of carve-outs вҖ” the sensitive-file check fires under **both** the `$GHJIG_ROOT/` and `$HOME/.claude/` carve-outs; #210). Matches the lexical basename **and**, when the final path component is a symlink, the `python3`-realpath-resolved basename вҖ” so a symlink with an innocuous name pointing at a sensitive target is blocked too (#234); `python3` absent/unresolvable вҶ’ lexical-only (fail-soft). TOCTOU and hardlinks are out of scope. | `sensitive` |
| Edit/Write on a protected branch (except when the file path is under `$GHJIG_ROOT/` = shell self-modification; or `$HOME/.claude/` = user-global auto-memory, issue #91 вҖ” those have no relationship to the repo's branch state) | Block | `branch` |
| `gh pr merge` when the PR's `closingIssuesReferences` includes any issue whose body has unchecked AC items (any task-list bullet family вҖ” `-`/`*`/`+` or an ordered `N.`, and indented forms вҖ” not only `- [ ]`; #500) and no **trusted-filer** comment (author association вҲҲ OWNER/MEMBER/MAINTAINER/COLLABORATOR вҖ” a drive-by non-trusted comment does **not** unlock the gate; #500) matching the **canonical marker** `^## AC closeout (resolved by PR #N)` (a comment that merely starts with `## AC closeout` no longer satisfies the gate; #500) has been posted yet. Closes the gap where `Closes #N` auto-closes an issue but leaves its AC list reading as "nothing was done." The helper `scripts/ac_closeout.sh <pr-num>` is idempotent and satisfies the gate by construction; `/ship` runs it as step 7.6. Fail-open with `audit_log warn` when `gh` calls time out or return malformed JSON (5-second per-call bound; SPEC В§6.1 framing вҖ” guardrails, not punishment for transient network issues). Also fail-open with `audit_log warn ac-closeout helper-missing` when `.claude/hooks/helpers/ac_closeout_gate.sh` is absent from the working tree at hook-fire time (e.g., a running session predates the helper's introduction вҖ” see the **session-restart caveat for hook-spec changes** below). The helper-source is presence-checked and a `gate_loaded` flag gates the downstream helper calls; an unloaded helper writes a warn and the merge proceeds вҖ” silent fail-through is treated as a regression. **Merge detection is on command words, not a raw substring** (#340): the shared `is_pr_merge_command` predicate strips heredoc bodies and quoted string literals before testing for the `gh вҖҰ pr вҖҰ merge` words, so `gh pr merge` appearing only as data (a heredoc body, a quoted `--body`/`-m` value, a commit message) no longer false-triggers the gate; it is fail-closed (any parse uncertainty / `python3` absence / helper miss вҶ’ treated as a merge), and a merge wrapped in an executed quoted string (`bash -c "gh pr merge вҖҰ"`) is a deliberate, documented non-detection. | `ac-closeout` |
| `gh pr merge` to the **default branch** without `--merge` вҖ” `--squash` / `--rebase` / a **bare** merge (no strategy flag, which the repo's `squashMergeAllowed` default resolves to a squash) вҶ’ block; `--merge` (including `--auto --merge`, the `/ship` form) вҶ’ allow. Enforces SPEC В§5.7.1's no-ff merge mandate: a squash collapses the DocвҶ’TestвҶ’Code arc (В§1.2's load-bearing artifact) into a single commit on the trunk, erasing on `main` the very evidence the flow produces. Keyed on the **live default branch** (`gh repo view --json defaultBranchRef`), NOT `PROTECTED_BRANCH_PATTERN` вҖ” so a squash into a **non-default** base (a topic branch consolidating sub-PRs, В§10.5) is **allowed** (the arc-preservation argument is about the trunk). Strategy and PR are parsed by a **gh-flag-aware token walk** (`parse_gh_merge_argv`, shell-aware via `shlex` with a `read -ra` fallback, #290): the strategy is the explicit strategy **flag token** вҖ” `--merge`/`-m` вҶ’ merge, `--squash`/`-s` вҶ’ squash, `--rebase`/`-r` вҶ’ rebase, none вҶ’ bare вҖ” **not a substring**, so a `--merge` appearing inside a `--body`/`--subject` *value* is not mistaken for the strategy (#290 A) and the short `-m` is correctly recognized as compliant (#290 C); the PR is the first **positional** token (or a `.../pull/N` URL's N), skipping value-taking flags' values (`--body`/`-b`, `--body-file`, `--subject`/`-t`, `--match-head-commit`, `--author-email`, `--repo`/`-R`) so a flag value is never read as the PR (#290 B). Strategy is evaluated **first**: an explicit `--merge` is allowed **silently** (`mark_allow`, no audit record) with no base resolution at all; only a non-`--merge` strategy triggers the base + default-branch lookup. Fail-open with `audit_log warn` if the PR base or the default branch can't be resolved (`gh` down / no auth; 5-second per-call bound), parity with `ac-closeout`. The PR falls back to the current branch's PR when the command names none. Independent of the `ac-closeout` arm (separate `should_skip` category; both fire on `gh pr merge` and each reaches its own decided state). The coarse entry grep is refined by the same `is_pr_merge_command` predicate as `ac-closeout` (#340), so `gh pr merge` text in a heredoc body / quoted argument / commit message does not engage this gate either (fail-closed on parse uncertainty). Escape: `SKIP_HOOKS=merge-strategy SKIP_REASON='<why>'`. (#288, #290, #340) | `merge-strategy` |
| `gh pr merge` when the **local branch is strictly ahead of its pushed remote head** вҖ” unpushed local commits exist that the merge would leave behind вҶ’ **block**. **git-only, no `gh`**: resolve the local HEAD and the branch's pushed remote-tracking head, then block **only** in the strictly-ahead state вҖ” local HEAD descends from the remote head **and** the two SHAs differ (`git merge-base --is-ancestor <remote> <local>` true **and** `<remote>` вү  `<local>`). Every other state вҶ’ **allow**: behind (remote ahead of local), diverged (neither is an ancestor of the other), an absent local or remote-tracking ref, a detached HEAD, or no configured upstream вҖ” the guard is a **positive** strictly-ahead detection, so any ambiguity falls to allow (a merge that races a re-push is caught instead by the `merge-attestation` staleness arm below and the В§5.7 merge-time re-pin). Prevents merging a **stale remote head that lacks unpushed work** (handol #244) вҖ” so the reviewed/attested local state actually reaches the trunk rather than a behind-remote head. Block message names the positive alternative: **"push your local commits first"**. Independent arm вҖ” its own `should_skip` category and `decided`/`mark_allow`/`block`/`pass_through_trace` terminal state, mirroring the `ac-closeout` and `merge-strategy` arms (both fire on `gh pr merge`, each reaches its own decided state). Escape: `SKIP_HOOKS=push-parity SKIP_REASON='<why>'`. (#544, #244) | `push-parity` |
| `gh pr merge` when the PR's review was **skipped or performed at the wrong head** вҶ’ **block**, in two independent sub-checks. The **attestation** is a local file `$(ghjig_state_dir)/attest/pr-<N>` holding the attested head SHA, written by `/ship` **strictly after** a review passes (В§5.7). **(a) Presence вҖ” a zero-network filesystem fact:** resolve the PR number from the merge argv (`extract_pr_from_merge_cmd`, **no `gh`**); if the PR# resolves and **no attestation file exists** for it вҶ’ **block with no `gh` call**. This is load-bearing: the never-ran-`/ship` fast-track (handol #246) is blocked **even when `gh` is down or the head is otherwise unresolvable** вҖ” presence is deliberately **not** coupled to a `gh` round-trip. **(b) Staleness вҖ” consults `gh`:** if the file exists, compare its attested head to the current PR head (`gh pr view <n> --json headRefOid`); a mismatch вҶ’ **block** (the review ran at a stale head, #543). **Head-equality only вҖ” no TTL**: a re-push advances the head and auto-invalidates the attestation. **Fail-open lines:** a `safe_source` helper-miss вҶ’ allow (shell safety, per the fail-policy table below); a PR-head-unresolvable failure (`gh` down вҖ” the **staleness sub-check only**, never presence) вҶ’ fail-open **allow** plus a **loud** `audit_log warn merge-attestation fail-open-skip` that the В§6.5(d) friction advisory can aggregate (В§6.0 P3 вҖ” an inert warn is not the fix; the root cause is unread warns). `ghjig_state_dir` empty/unset вҶ’ set-`u`-safe fallback, treated as attestation-absent, always reaching a terminal `decided` state (never crash-to-undecided). Block message names the positive alternative: **"run `/ship` to produce the attestation after the blind-compare"**. **CI-less-target framing (В§6.0 P2):** on a target with **no CI**, this local gate is the **sole merge-integrity backstop**, which is why **presence is fail-closed** (block) while only the network-dependent staleness sub-check fails open. **Threat model:** the attestation file is **forgeable** вҖ” deliberately **out of the В§6.1 threat model** (hooks are mistake-prevention, not a security boundary вҖ” same status as a `SKIP_HOOKS` escape); no security-boundary claim is made. Independent arm вҖ” its own `should_skip` category and terminal state, parity with `ac-closeout`/`merge-strategy`. **Out of scope here:** the deferred diffstat **`merge-completeness` warn** (advisory, warn-only) is tracked as **#548**; **base-aware fail-closed** (default-branch + head-unresolvable вҶ’ block-with-escape) is a measure-first follow-up, not built. Escape: `SKIP_HOOKS=merge-attestation SKIP_REASON='<why>'`. (#544, #246, #543) | `merge-attestation` |
| `gh issue close <N>` against a trusted-filer (OWNER / MEMBER / MAINTAINER / COLLABORATOR per `authorAssociation`) **non-discussion** Issue without `--reason completed` (i.e., the close is `not planned` or `duplicate`). Filer-aware invariant per В§1.5 вҖ” mode-independent, applies in both `attended` and `unattended`. **Discussion-tier is classified first and independent of trust** (#236): a `discussion`-labeled Issue follows the В§5.19 two-path rule (`--reason completed` / `"not planned"` allowed regardless of filer; bare/`duplicate` blocked) and never reaches this trusted-filer check. The issue selector is matched in all gh-accepted forms вҖ” bare number, quoted number, and `https://вҖҰ/issues/<N>` URL вҖ” and **normalized to the pure issue number** before the `is_trusted_filer` / discussion-label lookups and the block message (#223; `is_trusted_filer` requires a bare number, so an un-normalized URL/quoted selector would silently fail-open). When the selector is a **URL**, the lookups are **repo-aware** вҖ” filer-trust and the discussion label resolve against the URL's `owner/name` (via `--repo`), not the current directory's repo, so a foreign-repo close is evaluated against the foreign repo's issue rather than a same-numbered local one (#231). When the selector is a **bare number but an explicit `--repo owner/name` (or `[HOST/]owner/name`) flag вҖ” or `gh`'s `-R` short alias вҖ” is present**, that flag's repo is parsed and used for the same repo-aware lookups (#237 for `--repo`, #242 for `-R`, both completing #231) вҖ” `gh` accepts both `{<number>|<url>}` selectors and a `--repo`/`-R` flag, so the flag form is closed against the same cross-repo fail-open as the URL form. A bare-number selector with no `--repo`/`-R` flag keeps current-repo behavior; an unparseable URL or flag value fails soft to the current repo. **`owner/name` validation (#555 A6):** the resolved cross-repo target (URL- or flag-derived) is validated for a `.`/`..` path segment and the GitHub owner/repo charset вҖ” the prior parses checked segment *count* only, so a `.`/`..` segment (`../../evil`, `owner/..`) could redirect the trust/discussion `gh issue view --repo` lookup to an attacker-chosen repo; a rejected value falls back to the current repo (fail-soft), tightening the trust check. Fail-open if `is_trusted_filer` can't resolve. Escape: `SKIP_HOOKS=trusted-filer-mutate SKIP_REASON='<why>'`. | `trusted-filer-mutate` |
| `gh issue edit <N> --remove-label directive` against ANY filer (trusted or not). Removing the `directive` label declassifies a Directive and bypasses dir-mode review; human confirm required always. Matches **both** separator forms вҖ” `--remove-label directive` and `--remove-label=directive` (optionally quoted) вҖ” **and** a comma-joined value list where `directive` is any element (`--remove-label other,directive`; gh removes every listed label), with a word-boundary tail so a longer label like `directive-foo` does not over-match (#211). The issue selector is matched in all gh-accepted forms вҖ” bare number, quoted number, and `https://вҖҰ/issues/<N>` URL (#223). Same matcher and escape as the close-arm above. | `trusted-filer-mutate` |
| `gh issue edit <N> --add-label {execution\|task\|bug}` when the label contradicts the Issue body's line-1 `Parent Directive: #N` marker (the canonical resolver, В§5.2): `execution` with **no** marker (an `execution` Issue requires a parent, В§1.7), or `task`/`bug` **with** a marker present (standalone types must not be parented вҖ” the marker is a type smell). Blocks the contradictory relabel and names the fix (set/clear the line-1 marker first, then relabel). Converts the **advisory** #197 reviewer/skill layer into runtime enforcement вҖ” fires regardless of which agent or path applies the label, the "hooks-as-environment an agent cannot drift past" mechanism (MISSION). Scoped to the `--add-label` edit path only; the `gh issue create` path is already labelвҶ”marker-consistent via `/file-issue` (post-#197) and is **not** gated. The gated label is detected in both separator forms and **anywhere in a comma-joined value list** (`--add-label other,execution`; #212), terminated at a **true label boundary** вҖ” comma / whitespace / quote / end вҖ” so a hyphen- or underscore-suffixed custom label (`directive-foo`, `task_old`) that merely *starts with* a type token does **not** over-match it (#278 Theme C; a letter-suffixed `executionish` was already excluded). **Selector normalization (#276):** the issue selector is resolved via the shared `resolve_gh_issue_target` helper (`helpers/issue_type.sh`), tolerant of selector **form** (bare / quoted / URL вҖ” closing the A1 URL-form bypass) and flag **order** (the positional issue arg need not immediately follow `edit` вҖ” A2); a `-R`/`--repo owner/name` (or URL-embedded) target is threaded into the marker/label predicates so a **cross-repo** `--add-label` edit resolves against the command's target repo, not the cwd (A3 вҖ” the predicates' optional `repo` arg also keys the per-session cache by `owner/name`, so a foreign `#N` never poisons the current repo's same-numbered entry). The helper tokenizes **shell-aware** (`shlex`, mirroring `check_destructive_args`) so a quoted flag value's interior digits (`--body "fixes 99 things"`) are not mistaken for the positional issue, and normalizes a `[HOST/]owner/name` repo to `owner/name` (#283). **Also (#251):** blocks `--add-label initiative` on a `directive` Issue and `--add-label directive` on an `initiative` Issue (the two tier type-keys are mutually exclusive, keeping `is_directive_issue`/`is_initiative_issue` coherent); and blocks `--add-label directive` when the Directive body lacks **exactly one** parent kind вҖ” a `## MISSION fit` field (via `issue_has_mission_fit_field`) XOR a line-1 `Parent Initiative: #N` marker (via `issue_has_initiative_parent_marker`), i.e. both-present or neither-present (the parent-XOR, В§1.7). Fail-open if the Issue body can't be resolved (`gh` down / no auth / not found / predicate undefined) вҖ” the block fires only on a positively-resolved contradiction (parity with `proposed-protect` / `trusted-filer-mutate`). Escape: `SKIP_HOOKS=label-parent-consistency SKIP_REASON='<why>'`. | `label-parent-consistency` |
| Mutating `gh issue edit` / `close` / `reopen` (incl. `--add-label` / `--remove-label` / `--body` / `--title`) targeting an `initiative` Issue. An Initiative is **read-only to the shell except for appended comments** (В§1.7) вҖ” the shell *consumes* Initiatives and never edits, closes, relabels, or retires them; strategic decisions stay upstream. `gh issue comment` is not a mutating verb and is always allowed. The issue selector is resolved via the shared `resolve_gh_issue_target` helper (#276; bare / quoted / URL forms + flag-order tolerance), then `is_initiative_issue` resolves it against the **current** repo. This matcher deliberately **does not** honor a `-R`/`--repo` cross-repo target (unlike `label-parent-consistency`): **cross-repo Initiatives are out of scope** (В§1.7 вҖ” they would reintroduce the cross-repo-trust surface of the `trusted-filer-mutate` close arm), so the matcher governs only same-repo Initiatives; a foreign-targeted `gh issue edit` resolves against the cwd repo (and, if that is not an Initiative, `mark_allow`s). Fail-open if the predicate can't resolve. **Precedence over `trusted-filer-mutate`:** for `gh issue close <initiative>`, the two matchers give opposite verdicts вҖ” a trusted-filer close *with* `--reason completed` is *allowed* by `trusted-filer-mutate`, but *any* close on an `initiative` Issue is *blocked* here. `initiative-readonly` wins: an Initiative is **never** closed by the shell, even `--reason completed` by a trusted filer (the shell consumes Initiatives, never retires them вҖ” termination is an upstream decision surfaced via `/initiative-feedback`, В§5.22). The block holds by the **block-is-terminal** rule, not by matcher ordering: `trusted-filer-mutate` actually evaluates *first* in `pre_tool_use.sh` but only `mark_allow`s a `--reason completed` close (non-terminal вҖ” `decided=1; return 0`); `initiative-readonly` evaluates *later* and calls `block` (`exit 2`). Because any `block` terminates the hook while `mark_allow` never short-circuits a subsequent matcher, the block wins regardless of the two matchers' relative order. Escape: `SKIP_HOOKS=initiative-readonly SKIP_REASON='<why>'`. (#251) | `initiative-readonly` |
| A GitHub **close keyword** (`close`/`closes`/`closed`/`fix`/`fixes`/`fixed`/`resolve`/`resolves`/`resolved`, case-insensitive, optional `:`) followed by `#N` where Issue `#N` is a **Directive**, in either (a) the inline `--body`/`-b` value of `gh pr create` / `gh pr edit`, or (b) a commit message (`-m`/`--message` values + heredoc body, scanned inside the commit-format umbrella arm). | GitHub auto-closes a referenced Issue at merge when such a keyword + `#N` appears anywhere in a PR body **or** any commit message. For an **Execution** Issue this is correct (its merge resolves it); for a **Directive** it bypasses the `/complete-directive` signal-evidence gate (N=3 vote, В§5.13) вҖ” a Directive must close ONLY through that gate (live regression: PR #489's body `closes #477 signal 3` auto-closed Directive #477 while signal 4 was still pending). The shared detector `directive_close_violation` (`helpers/git_matcher.sh`) extracts ALL keyword + `#N` pairs and calls `is_directive_issue` **per `#N`**, blocking on the FIRST Directive; **Execution Issues are never blocked** (`Closes #<execution>` is the normal resolving trailer) and a non-close mention (`Refs #N`, `advances #N`, prose) never matches the close-keyword grammar, so it passes. **Per-`#N` fail-open**: an unresolved type (gh down / no auth / non-numeric) skips that `#N` (parity with `proposed-protect`/`initiative-readonly`). The PR vector reads the **inline** `--body`/`-b` value only вҖ” `--body-file`/`-F` (incl. the `-F -` stdin form `/ship`/`/sync-pr` use) is a **documented residual** (reading an arbitrary file path adds an IO/path-resolution/TOCTOU surface disproportionate to the vector); `owner/repo#N` and full-URL close-forms are likewise a residual (this shell authors bare `#N`). В§6.0: a wrong *allow* irreversibly evades the completion gate and corrupts governance history (high-cost вҖ” P1 hard negative gate failing safe toward block); a wrong *block* costs renaming to `Refs #N` (recoverable), and the block message names that positive alternative (P4). Escape: `SKIP_HOOKS=directive-close SKIP_REASON='<why>'`. (#490) | `directive-close` |

**Session-restart caveat for hook-spec changes.** Claude Code binds its hook routing from `.claude/settings.json` + the working tree at session start. Adding a *new* helper file under `.claude/hooks/helpers/` (or any path referenced by an existing hook via `.`/`source`) does not retroactively become reachable to a session that started before the file existed. Such a session continues to execute the *updated* `pre_tool_use.sh` (re-read per invocation), but a `. "$SHELL_ROOT/.claude/hooks/helpers/<new-helper>.sh"` line silently fails вҖ” and any function defined only in that helper is undefined, so downstream calls return rc=127 and matchers can fall through without ever reaching their block / warn arms. **The fix is to start a fresh `ghjig` session after pulling a hook-spec change that introduces a new helper file.** The hook-side mitigation is the **`safe_source`** utility (hosted in `.claude/hooks/hookrt.sh` вҖ” the "hook runtime" bootstrap that also hosts `audit_log`): every helper source line вҖ” both **hook-to-helper** (the 5 hook files under `.claude/hooks/` sourcing helpers) and **helper-to-helper** (a helper under `.claude/hooks/helpers/` sourcing another helper from the same directory, e.g. `branch_guard.sh` вҶ’ `git_matcher.sh`) вҖ” goes through `safe_source <helper-path> <audit-category>`, which presence-checks the file, sources it, and on miss emits `audit_log warn <category> helper-missing "<path>"` and returns 1. The one documented exception is the **bootstrap-to-runtime shim** at `helpers/log.sh:6` вҶ’ `hookrt.sh`: that source line can't go through `safe_source` because `safe_source` lives in the file being sourced (chicken-and-egg), so it falls back to a primitive `.` and is stderr-only on miss. The scope predicate for "in scope of the `safe_source` invariant" is: the source target is under `.claude/hooks/helpers/`, NOT directly under `.claude/hooks/` (i.e. `hookrt.sh` and the 5 hook entry-point files are exempt вҖ” they are the runtime, not helpers). The shape this closes вҖ” one site warning while a sibling source-site of the same helper fails silently, hiding the second consumer вҖ” was the regression #36 surfaced. The hook continues to **fail-open** (matcher arm short-circuits, command proceeds) so a missing helper is recoverable, not a developer-lockout вҖ” but the failure mode is visible in `audit.jsonl` instead of silent. Existing helpers that the running session already loaded (e.g. `helpers/coauthor.sh`) are unaffected вҖ” their function bindings persist across invocations of the parent hook. Cross-reference В§3.2.1 (hook command path resolution).

**`safe_source` fail-policy table** (per-helper audit category and on-miss behavior; **all entries fail-open** with a category-typed warn вҖ” future PRs may flip individual entries to fail-closed with their own SPEC В§1.4 justification):

| Helper | Audit category | On-miss notes |
|---|---|---|
| `hookrt.sh` (the runtime itself) | (n/a вҖ” primitive bootstrap) | Hook exits 0 with one-line stderr warn; cannot audit-log itself |
| `helpers/log.sh` (compatibility shim вҶ’ `hookrt.sh`) | `audit` | Stderr warn only; downstream `audit_log` unavailable |
| `helpers/escape.sh` | `escape` | `SKIP_HOOKS` machinery degrades to "always block"; documented |
| `helpers/cwd_guard.sh` | `out-of-scope` | `in_scope` undefined вҶ’ hook exits 0 anyway |
| `helpers/branch_guard.sh` | `branch` | **Security-relevant** вҖ” protected-branch enforcement off; warn carries a "not enforced" suffix |
| `helpers/secret_scan.sh` | `secret` | **Security-relevant** вҖ” secret enforcement off; warn carries a "not enforced" suffix |
| `helpers/conventional_commit.sh` | `commit-format` | Hygiene, not security |
| `helpers/detect_stack.sh` | `format` | Lint/format detection off |
| `helpers/git_matcher.sh` | `commit-format` | Constants source; downstream matchers degrade together |
| `helpers/ac_closeout_gate.sh` | `ac-closeout` | Already-shipped per #31/#32. **Also hosts (folded in, #544) the merge-parity gate functions** вҖ” `local_ahead_of_pr` (`push-parity` arm), and `write_review_attestation` + `attestation_matches` (`merge-attestation` arm; the write is an **inline function**, no new `scripts/review_attest.sh` and no new helper file). On-miss, the `push-parity` and `merge-attestation` arms **also fail-open** (allow) with a category-typed warn, same posture as the `ac-closeout` arm вҖ” the presence-check's *fail-closed* posture applies only when the helper is loaded and a PR# resolves; a `safe_source` miss of the file itself always fails open (shell safety). |
| `helpers/status.sh` | `status` | Informational only; no enforcement impact |
| `helpers/issue_type.sh` | `proposed-protect` | Type-awareness + lifecycle predicates (`is_directive_issue`, `is_initiative_issue`, `is_proposed_issue`, `issue_has_parent_marker`, `issue_has_initiative_parent_marker`, `issue_has_mission_fit_field`) (В§1.7); on miss the AC-closeout Type-aware skip, the `proposed-protect` matcher, the `label-parent-consistency` matcher (incl. its initiative/directive + parent-XOR arms), the `initiative-readonly` matcher, and the `directive-close` matcher (which calls `is_directive_issue` per `#N`) all fail-open (engineering hooks revert to non-Type-aware behavior; an undefined predicate is treated as "not blocked by that arm") |
| `helpers/issue_filer.sh` | `trusted-filer-mutate` | Filer-trust predicate (В§1.5 filer-aware invariants); on miss the `trusted-filer-mutate` matcher fails-open (the close / declassify proceeds under the regular attended/unattended rules вҖ” protection layer is best-effort, not blocking) |
| `helpers/reviewer_audit.sh` | `reviewer-reject` | `reviewer_reject_audit` emission for non-pass reviewer verdicts (#361, Directive #356 signal 3); on miss the skill's reject-audit record is skipped (fail-open вҖ” the reviewer verdict still gates the flow; only the observability trail is best-effort, never the gate) |
| `helpers/blast_radius.sh` | `reviewer-tier` | `is_high_asymmetry` high-asymmetry decision classifier (В§4.11); on miss the gated decision degrades to a **single reviewer** with an `audit_log warn reviewer-tier` record вҖ” never a lockout (a wrong degrade loses redundancy on one decision; a lockout would block all shipping вҖ” the asymmetry that picks fail-open) |

**`helpers/ship_mode.sh` is intentionally absent from this table** вҖ” it is *not* reached through `safe_source`, so the scope predicate above ("under `.claude/hooks/helpers/`, reached through `safe_source`") does not govern it. `ship_mode.sh` (`resolve_mode` + `ship_park_pr`) is loaded by the `/ship` and `/status` **command** surfaces via a direct `.`, and by `helpers/status.sh` via a manual `[ -f вҖҰ ] && . вҖҰ` guard (not `safe_source`) because `resolve_mode` there is **informational** (it populates the status projection's mode field, with no enforcement decision riding on it) вҖ” an absent helper already fails open to an empty mode string, and `/ship`'s own preflight handles a missing helper on the enforcement path. Its on-miss posture is therefore fail-open by construction, consistent with every table entry; no row is added because a row would assert a `safe_source` source-site that does not exist.

**`helper-missing` audit-event shape** вҖ” the on-miss line emitted by `safe_source` is:

```json
{"ts":"<RFC3339>","event":"warn","category":"<from-table>","decision":"helper-missing","reason":"<absolute-path-to-missing-helper>","cwd":"<pwd>","source":"<live|test>"}
```

`reason` and `cwd` are JSON-escaped per SPEC В§7. `decision` carries the constant token `helper-missing`. **`helper-missing` audit categories are a superset of `SKIP_HOOKS` categories** вҖ” for example, `status` is a valid audit category for an informational helper but is NOT a `SKIP_HOOKS` category. The escape-hatch list in В§7 stays unchanged; the audit categories enumerate what `safe_source` can emit, which is broader.

**Matcher pass-through audit contract.** PR #32 surfaced a class of bug where a matcher entered (its `grep -qE 'pattern'` matched) but no terminal arm fired вҖ” the matcher silently exited with no audit record. This made "matcher entered but produced no audit" indistinguishable from "matcher never matched the command" вҖ” a structural blind spot in the audit trail. The contract closes that gap:

> **For every matcher in `pre_tool_use.sh`, if the matcher entered (`grep` matched), `audit.jsonl` MUST gain exactly one record whose `category` field matches the matcher's category in this hook invocation.**

The terminal arm fires that record (or marks it as decided without emission):
- A `block` decision emits `audit_log block <cat> deny <reason>`.
- A `warn` decision emits `audit_log warn <cat> <decision-token> <reason>` (`decision-token` вҲҲ {`notice`, `helper-missing`, `pass-through`, ...}). Note `bypass-suspect` is a *category* (with decision-token `notice`), not a decision-token.
- A **high-frequency happy-path** arm (e.g., every clean `git commit`, every in-scope `rm -rf`, every local `--amend`) calls `mark_allow <cat>` (in `hookrt.sh`). This sets the caller's `decided` flag with NO audit emission вҖ” the matcher's contract is satisfied (it entered, evaluated cleanly, allowed) without per-action audit noise. Distinct from the explicit-`notice` warn path, which is used for low-frequency designed-allow cases where an audit record is desired.
- If no other arm fires by the matcher's tail, the helper `pass_through_trace <cat> "<cmd>"` (also in `hookrt.sh`) emits `audit_log warn <cat> pass-through "<truncated-cmd>"`. This is the anomalous case вҖ” the matcher decided to do nothing without naming why, which we treat as a soft regression worth flagging.

Implementation pattern (per Bash-branch matcher in `pre_tool_use.sh`):

```bash
if printf '%s' "$cmd" | grep -qE 'pattern'; then
  decided=
  # ... terminal arms set `decided=1` ...
  [ -z "$decided" ] && pass_through_trace <cat> "$cmd"
fi
```

The `decided=` flag is reset at the head of each matcher block so state cannot leak across matchers. Smoke (`scripts/test/smoke.sh` В§39) asserts the invariant:
- **В§39a**: for each matcher, a synthesized benign-but-entering command produces exactly one new audit record with the expected category.
- **В§39b**: structural awk-grep over `pre_tool_use.sh` вҖ” every `if printf '%s' "$cmd" | grep -qE ...; then` block ends with either an explicit `decided=1` audit-emitter or a `pass_through_trace` tail.
- **В§39c**: negative вҖ” a command that enters no matcher (e.g. `ls -la`) produces zero new audit records.

**Decision-token vocabulary** (`decision` field in `audit_log`):

| Token | Used by | Meaning |
|---|---|---|
| `deny` | `block` | Hook refused the command; `exit 2` follows. |
| `notice` | `audit_log warn` | Soft signal вҖ” degraded enforcement (gh timeout, indeterminate state, explicit allow with reason). |
| `helper-missing` | `safe_source` on miss | A hook helper was absent; matcher arm short-circuited. |
| `bypass-suspect` | bypass-suspect matcher | Command looks like an eval/heredoc bypass (warn-only, not a block). |
| `pass-through` | `pass_through_trace` | Matcher entered but no terminal arm fired вҖ” anomalous; treat as a soft regression. |
| `skip` | `audit_log escape` | `SKIP_HOOKS=` was honored; categorized as `escape`. |
| `reject` | reviewer-reject audit (#361) | A reviewer subagent returned a non-pass verdict; the `reason` carries `class=<reason-class> issue=#<N>`. |

The token list is intentionally short and stable; future arms add new tokens here, not new `event`-type kinds.

**Event-kind set.** The `event` field is one of `block` / `warn` / `escape` / `info`. `info` is an **informational** record вҖ” not a refusal вҖ” e.g. the AC-closeout Type=Directive skip (`pre_tool_use.sh`) and the dir-mode lifecycle notices (`audit_log info directive-*`, В§5.10+), typically carrying the `notice` decision token. This four-member set is the stable one the "not new `event`-type kinds" rule above refers to: arms add new `decision` tokens, not new event kinds.

**Audit `source` field** (live/test origin discriminator, #361 / Directive #356 signal 1). Every `audit_log` record carries an additive top-level `source` field вҖ” `live` for real sessions, `test` for test-harness fixture fires. It is the **last** field in the JSON object (after `cwd`), so it does not perturb the `reason`-anchored В§50a format scan or `_audit_validate_format` (which inspects only `category`/`decision`/`reason`, never the record shape). The value resolves from a single harness-owned environment marker: `source=test` **iff** `GHJIG_AUDIT_SOURCE` is exactly the token `test`; **any** other value вҖ” unset, empty, `smoke`, `live`, or arbitrary вҖ” resolves to `live` (fail-safe-to-`live`). The field is additive and append-only-safe: historical lines written before #361 have no `source` key (`.source == null` under `jq`); consumers treat an absent value as legacy/unknown (fail-open on absence).

**Anti-reclassification invariant** (Directive #356 Constraint вҖ” a `live` action must never be silently reclassifiable to `test`/`smoke` to dodge a friction signal). The marker is read from the **hook subprocess environment**. Per В§7, the live Claude Code Bash tool consumes a leading `VAR=val` as the *spawned command's* own environment вҖ” it never lands in `tool_input.command`, and the hook subprocess does not inherit it вҖ” and shell state does not persist between Bash-tool calls. So a real action cannot inject `GHJIG_AUDIT_SOURCE=test` into the hook subprocess that writes its audit record; only the process that **launches the session** (e.g. `scripts/test/smoke.sh`, which `export`s the marker before driving the hooks directly вҖ” mirroring the `GHJIG_STATE_DIR_OVERRIDE` test seam, В§3.2.2) can set it. Smoke pins the invariant: a fixture fire with the marker unset records `source=live`, and one with a *forged* `GHJIG_AUDIT_SOURCE=smoke` (a non-`test` value) still records `live`. A query can therefore partition the log by origin (`jq 'select(.source=="live")'` vs the all-records count) to exclude test-fixture noise from the existing backlog вҖ” the observability surface Directive #356 signal 1 requires (the forward noise source itself was already removed by #357's whole-run state isolation).

**Reviewer-reject reason-class vocabulary** (#361 / Directive #356 signal 3). When the three reviewer subagents (`issue-reviewer`, `plan-reviewer`, `activation-reviewer`) return a non-pass verdict (`refine`/`revise`/`reject`/`block`), the invoking skill flow emits a categorized audit record via the `reviewer_reject_audit` helper (`helpers/reviewer_audit.sh`): `audit_log warn <category> reject "class=<reason-class> issue=#<N>"`. The `<category>` is the reviewer's audit category вҖ” `issue-review` (`/file-issue` вҶ’ issue-reviewer), `plan-review` (`/work-on` вҶ’ plan-reviewer), or `activation` (`/activate` and `/complete-directive`, which both drive activation-reviewer). These are **audit-emission** categories, **not** `SKIP_HOOKS` escape categories вҖ” they are not reachable via `should_skip` and so are deliberately absent from the В§7 escape list (the `helper-missing`/audit-category set is a superset of the escape set). The `<reason-class>` is one of a small controlled vocabulary the skill maps the reviewer's free-text reason onto (nearest token): `schema-incomplete`, `unverifiable-ac`, `scope-bleed`, `mission-misfit`, `conflict`, `evidence-insufficient`. This produces the per-reviewer Г— reason-class trail that a promotion-candidate report (Directive #356 signal 4, a sibling Execution Issue) aggregates. The mapping is a skill-side judgment (the same free-textвҶ’token summarization `/activate` already performs); the helper only formats and emits.

Tests are run by `/ship` (В§5.7). During the draft PR's commit/push, only quick lint/format runs. A commit-time test gate would force WIP/share commits to escape every time, polluting the audit log вҖ” so we don't add one.

**Lint timeout**: the commit-time lint invocation is bounded by `GHJIG_LINT_TIMEOUT` (seconds, default 30) so a misconfigured or slow linter cannot hang the commit. Timeout fires as a `block format` decision, escapable via `SKIP_HOOKS=format`. If neither `timeout(1)` (coreutils) nor `gtimeout(1)` is on `PATH`, the lint runs unbounded with an `audit_log warn lint-timeout-absent` entry (decision token `notice`) recording the missing dependency вҖ” the hook neither hangs the user nor silently downgrades enforcement. `lint-timeout-absent` is an **audit-emission** category (like the reviewer-reject categories above), not a `SKIP_HOOKS` escape category, so it is deliberately absent from the В§7 escape list.

#### 6.1.1 Conditional issue # enforcement

| commit type | issue # required | Rationale |
|-------------|------------------|-----------|
| `feat`, `fix`, `docs`, `refactor`, `perf` | Required | External surface / behavior change |
| `test`, `style`, `build`, `ci`, `chore`, `revert` | Optional (passes without it) | Internal change |

Structural regex:
```
# required group
^(feat|fix|docs|refactor|perf)(\(#[0-9]+\))!?: .+$
# optional group (issue # optional)
^(test|style|build|ci|chore|revert)(\(#[0-9]+\))?!?: .+$
```

Subject length is measured in **codepoints (1..72)**. Byte-based measurement (`wc -c`, `${#var}`) is forbidden вҖ” under multibyte locales it mis-truncates Korean/CJK. The choice of tool is an implementation detail.

**Subject extraction across `-m` forms**: the hook accepts both the plain quoted form and the command-substitution + heredoc form that the harness uses for multi-line bodies (`Co-Authored-By`, etc.).

| `-m` form | Subject |
|-----------|---------|
| `-m "feat(#1): subject"` / `-m 'feat(#1): subject'` | The quoted text (its first line) |
| `-m "feat(#1): subjectвҸҺвҸҺbody"` (embedded newlines, single `-m`) | The **first line** of the value only вҖ” extracted from the **raw** command (whitespace normalization flattens the newlines, so a normalized-command parse would capture subject+body as one over-length blob) |
| `-m "subject" -m "body"` (multiple `-m`, git's multi-paragraph form) | The value of the **first** `-m` (not the last) |
| `-m "$(cat <<'TAG'` вҖҰ `TAG)"` (heredoc body inside the `-m` value) | The first non-blank, non-tag line of the heredoc body вҖ” **but only when the value's own first non-blank line is not already a valid Conventional-Commit subject** (line-1 precedence, below) |
| `-m "feat(#1): subjectвҸҺвҸҺвҖҰbody mentioning `<<EOF`вҖҰ"` (normal body that merely contains a `<<TAG` token) | The **line-1 subject** вҖ” a `<<TAG` appearing as prose in the body does **not** make it a heredoc message |
| `-F <file>` / `--file <file>` (no inline `-m`/heredoc message) | **Empty** вҖ” the message lives in a file the hook cannot read; the format check is **skipped** (fail-open) |

The heredoc tag may be single-quoted (`<<'EOF'`), unquoted (`<<EOF`), or indent-stripping (`<<-EOF`); the extractor returns the first body line that is not blank and not the closing tag, leading whitespace stripped, before the Conventional-Commits regex runs.

**Line-1 precedence** (#383): the heredoc walk is entered **only when the `-m` value's first non-blank line is not itself a valid Conventional-Commit subject**. The genuine substitution form's first line is the `$(cat <<TAG` opener вҖ” never a valid subject вҖ” so it falls through to the heredoc body as before. But a plain single `-m` whose first line *is* a valid subject and whose body merely mentions a `<<TAG` token (common when the change is *about* shell/heredocs) returns line-1 directly, rather than mis-reading a body line as the subject. This is fail-safe: line-1 is returned only when it passes the Conventional-Commits regex, so a malformed line-1 always falls through to the existing over-extracting (block-leaning) behavior.

**Extraction is bounded to the `git commit` command and operates on the raw command** (before whitespace normalization): it scans from the `commit` token onward, so a heredoc or `-m` belonging to a **sibling** command in a compound invocation вҖ” e.g. a `cat > file <<EOF вҖҰ EOF` redirect or another tool's `-m` chained before the commit вҖ” is never mistaken for the subject. A heredoc is treated as the subject **only** when it is the commit's own `-m "$(cat <<TAG)"` message value, not any heredoc elsewhere in the command line. python3 drives the primary parse; the legacy heredoc-walk + single-line `sed` is the fallback when python3 is absent (degrading toward the prior, over-extracting behavior вҖ” which fails toward *blocking*, never toward letting a malformed subject through).

Implementations expose a single helper (`extract_commit_subject`) consumed by `pre_tool_use.sh`'s commit gate. An empty return (no `-m`/heredoc message in the commit segment) makes the gate skip the format check (fail-open); the gate only ever blocks a subject it positively extracted and found malformed.

### 6.2 PostToolUse вҖ” supplementary

| Trigger | Action |
|---------|--------|
| After `Edit/Write/MultiEdit` | Auto-format the changed file with the detected formatter (failures don't block) |
| `Bash` matches `git commit` | Print a "remember to update the matching PR body checklist item" reminder (warn-only) |
| `Bash` matches `git push` | If a PR exists, check `gh pr checks` and notify the user |
| `Read` of a whole file (neither `offset` nor `limit`) above the line threshold (`GHJIG_READ_NUDGE_THRESHOLD`, default 200) | Nudge toward a targeted `Read --offset/--limit` or `explorer` delegation (warn-only, always `exit 0`). The positive narrowing affordance of В§1.8 вҖ” a missed nudge is ignorable at no cost (В§6.0 P1), so it guides, never blocks. Fires only inside a registered scope (the hook's `in_scope` gate) and only when `jq` is available. |

### 6.3 Stop вҖ” recommendation after each response

Claude Code's `Stop` hook fires **after every model response**, not at session end. To avoid noise, suggest only once every N responses:

- uncommitted changes + no recent review вҶ’ suggest `/review`
- recent commit + PR body checklist out of sync вҶ’ suggest `/sync-pr`

Suggestions print one line to stderr (no blocking). Throttling is a simple modulo of N (default 5, overridable via `$GHJIG_STOP_THROTTLE`) вҖ” no per-category state file.

Session-level cleanup (branch tidy, temp files) is a **deferred capability** (В§0.4) вҖ” neither a `SessionEnd` hook nor a `/wrap` command is specified or built today.

### 6.4 UserPromptSubmit вҖ” context injection

Before each user message, inject the **compact status** as system context вҖ” `status_compact` (`helpers/status.sh`, the same projection В§5.5 describes): current branch, the issue / PR one-liners, phase, `next:` hint, mode, shell-root, state, and work-lang. This is a small per-turn refresh, not a full context reload.

The heavier one-time injection вҖ” the full current-PR body, the referenced-issue body, and the MISSION summary вҖ” is **SessionStart's** job (В§6.5(b) Session restore), loaded once when a session resumes in-scope, not re-injected every turn (CLAUDE.md is loaded whole natively by Claude Code, not part of this injection). Keeping the per-turn surface to `status_compact` is the narrowing half of the MISSION mechanism (В§1, "as small and relevant as possible"); SessionStart selective-injection is the dual.

### 6.5 SessionStart вҖ” shell sync check + session restore + SessionStart banner + friction advisory + SSOT-presence health

At session start, do five things:

**(a) Shell sync check**
- Is the shell repo behind origin/main? If so, warn (no auto-pull; sudden behavior changes are risky).
- The `git fetch` is gated by a stamp file at `.claude/state/last-shell-fetched`. The fetch runs only when the stamp is older than `SESSION_START_FETCH_TTL` seconds (default 21600 = 6 h) or absent. Most sessions therefore skip the network call вҖ” the `git rev-list --count HEAD..@{u}` still runs against locally-known refs, so the "behind" warning is correct relative to whatever was last fetched (up to 6 h stale, which matches the warning's polite-not-critical role).
- The fetch is wrapped in `timeout $SESSION_START_FETCH_TIMEOUT` (default 5 s) so a hung network does not stall session startup. If `timeout(1)` / `gtimeout(1)` is unavailable the fetch runs unbounded, matching SPEC В§6.1 / `GHJIG_LINT_TIMEOUT`'s fallback pattern.

**(b) Session restore** вҖ” to seamlessly resume the previous session, inject once:
- The current branch's full PR body (if any)
- Full referenced issue body (if any)
- Target `MISSION.md` head (`head -n 20 MISSION.md`)
- One `/status` snapshot

`.claude/CLAUDE.md` is **not** hook-injected here вҖ” Claude Code natively loads it whole every session. Because it is an always-on injected surface it is held to the В§9 thin-pointer discipline + 12000-byte budget (smoke В§104).

Subsequent turns only refresh the short status summary from В§6.4.

**(c) SessionStart banner**

One silent-no-op state evaporates the В§0.1 enforcement guarantee with no operator signal: the runtime that hosts enforcement is missing. SessionStart surfaces it via a primitive inline `printf` stderr banner, debounced to one fire per session and independent of `hookrt.sh` / `audit_log` / `safe_source` (the runtime that is itself the missing piece).

**Inject-consistency banner вҖ” removed (#318, Directive #311).** This banner is **gone**, not re-conditioned. Its premise died with the #312 binding: it fired when the shell-root env var (then `$GHJIG_SHELL_ROOT`; retired as an input by #537) was unset and `settings.local.json` was an injected symlink, warning "every hook will no-op". Post-#312 that is the **normal working state** вҖ” a plain `claude` in an injected target resolves hooks via the per-project binding symlink `${CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR}/.claude/ghjig-root/...` and `session_start.sh` self-locates + exports `$GHJIG_ROOT` (В§3.2.1), so enforcement is fully on. The banner only false-fired. And the *genuine* residual no-op (the binding symlink missing/broken вҖ” and post-#537 no ambient env can substitute for it, В§3.2.1) is **structurally undetectable from SessionStart**: the SessionStart hook command itself traverses that binding (`settings.injected.json`), so a broken binding means `session_start.sh` never runs and the banner inside it can never fire вҖ” the banner would sit behind the very link it claims to check. No condition can both detect the failure and execute in it; the honest fix is removal. The forward-looking detector lives at **launch** time instead: `bin/ghjig <dir>` warns (non-blocking) when an injected target's `.claude/ghjig-root` binding is missing/dangling, before `exec claude` вҖ” it runs *before* the session and resolves the dir directly, so it is the one place that can surface the broken-binding no-op (#334, В§3.5).

**Registry-zeroed detector** (#502, Directive #498) вҖ” the per-project scope-guard registry (`ghjig-state/registry.txt`, В§3.2.2) going **empty** silently turns ALL enforcement off, because the global `in_scope` gate fails open on an empty/absent registry (by design, В§3.2.2 / В§773). An audit found this *zeroing* is reachable by an innocuous single command вҖ” `: > registry.txt`, `truncate`, or a flagless delete-then-touch вҖ” and was previously **traceless**. `session_start.sh` now detects a **present-but-EMPTY** registry (the distinguishable "armed-then-disarmed" signal; an *absent* registry is the normal pre-registration / unregistered-cwd transparent case and does **not** fire) and emits the same once-per-session banner + an `audit_log warn registry-zeroed` record. The detector **mirrors the reader's back-compat resolution order** (В§767, `cwd_guard.in_scope`/`path_in_scope`): when the per-project `ghjig-state/registry.txt` is **absent**, it stats the legacy shared `$GHJIG_ROOT/.claude/state/registry.txt` instead вҖ” otherwise an empty *legacy-shared* file (the fallback the reader still consults) would silently disable enforcement while the banner stayed mute, the exact blind spot the detector exists to close (#554). **This is a В§1.4 decision, NOT a fail-openвҶ’fail-closed flip:** the empty-registry transparency is the deliberate guardrail-not-sandbox posture (В§6.1 Framing) and is unchanged вҖ” the detector only makes the disarmed state **observable**, satisfying the "no enforcement-disable that is both innocuous-command-reachable AND traceless" bar. **Documented residuals (accepted, not closed):** (a) the redirect/`truncate` *write itself* is still un-gated at fire time (the В§6.1 destructive `find -delete`/`truncate`/`>` residual, #505) вҖ” detection is at the *next* SessionStart, not real-time block; (b) the **binding-symlink repoint** вҖ” repointing `.claude/ghjig-root` at an attacker-controlled tree with a neutered `hookrt.sh` disables the session and is **structurally undetectable from within** (this detector, like the whole SessionStart hook, is reached *through* the binding), extending the missing/dangling-binding residual above; the launch-time `bin/ghjig` check (В§3.5) catches a missing/dangling binding but not a repoint-to-a-valid-but-neutered tree. Both residuals are the documented "anyone who can write `ghjig-state` / repoint the binding can bash around the hook" posture (В§6.1 / В§7), not a new exposure.

**Hookrt-missing banner** (#37) вҖ” the shell root resolved (self-location, В§3.2.1), but `.claude/hooks/hookrt.sh` is absent (corrupt checkout, conflict-stashed file, manual `rm`). Each of the 5 hooks has a primitive check for the runtime and emits a per-invocation WARN to stderr before silently exiting 0; that per-invocation line trains operators to ignore "WARN hookrt-missing" as background noise, exactly when they shouldn't. The banner is the once-per-session actionable signal layered on top of that per-invocation diagnostic floor.

- **Trigger**: the resolved `$GHJIG_ROOT` is non-empty **AND** `$GHJIG_ROOT/.claude/hooks/hookrt.sh` is absent.
- **Action**: emit one stderr line naming the failure mode (`hook enforcement OFF until restored`) and the concrete fix вҖ” inspect tree state via `git -C $GHJIG_ROOT status`, then restore via `git -C $GHJIG_ROOT checkout -- .claude/hooks/hookrt.sh`. Non-blocking; SessionStart still exits 0 immediately after (no helpers can load without the runtime).
- **Idempotency**: a stamp file under `$TMPDIR/ghjig-banner-hookrt.${CLAUDE_SESSION_ID:-$PPID}` debounces to one banner per session. The `-hookrt` suffix is retained for stamp-name stability across sessions (it predates the #318 removal of the sibling inject-consistency banner).
- **Diagnostic floor**: the existing per-invocation WARN at `session_start.sh:23` (and equivalent at the other 4 hooks' bootstrap blocks) stays вҖ” it is the script-grep-friendly log-scraper-stable diagnostic that survives the banner's stamp-creation failure modes (hostile `$TMPDIR`, low-disk). The banner adds operator-facing actionability without removing the diagnostic floor.
- **Position**: runs **after** the shell-root self-location (the trigger needs the resolved root, В§3.2.1) and **before** the `. "$hookrt"` source line at `session_start.sh:37` вҖ” co-located inside the existing `if [ ! -f "$hookrt" ]` block, since it shares the trigger condition and immediate `exit 0` tail.

**Shell-root env banners** (#537) вҖ” two arms in the same once-per-session, mkdir-stamp-debounced family, the observability half of the В§3.2.1 ambient-never-consulted contract (a clean cut with no deprecation shim needs a signal, not a shim):
- **Legacy/mismatched-ambient arm**: an ambient `GHJIG_SHELL_ROOT` is set, **or** an ambient `GHJIG_ROOT` differs from the self-located root вҶ’ one stderr line: `GHJIG_SHELL_ROOT retired (#537): the ambient shell-root env is IGNORED вҖ” hooks self-locate via BASH_SOURCE and export GHJIG_ROOT internally. Fix: unset the stale export (legacy var or mismatched GHJIG_ROOT) from your shell profile.` The stale export is functionally ignored on the hook path; this arm is what keeps that ignore from being silent.
- **Override-seam arm**: `GHJIG_ROOT_OVERRIDE` is set in a live session вҶ’ one stderr line naming the active test-only seam and the tree hooks are loading from: `test-only seam active; hooks loading from <path>`.

Both arms are non-blocking observability surfaces, not gates.

**(d) Friction-candidate advisory** (#398, Directive #391)

This is the **trigger** that completes the deferred-positive-face loop of В§6.0 P3: the friction-candidate readers (`scripts/narrowing_candidates.sh`, `scripts/promotion_candidates.sh`, and the git-history reader `scripts/ceremony_candidates.sh` вҖ” #401) plus the new `unattended-park` park-frequency signal (below) are aggregated into a **one-line, non-blocking advisory** so the shell surfaces its own accumulated friction without a human remembering to run a script. It is the always-on counterpart described in MISSION:16 ("the log becomes the channel through which the shell sees its own friction") вҖ” a consumer wired to read the aggregate.

- **Face**: **positive, never a block** (В§6.0 P1 вҖ” a missed friction nudge is ignorable at no cost). It is a single advisory line pointing to `/audit` and the three reader scripts; it **never dumps** their output into context (MISSION:14 narrowing constraint вҖ” the per-session surface stays a fixed-size pointer, not a variable-length report).
- **Trigger condition**: emitted only when the readers surface at least one above-threshold candidate cluster, **or** when the audit aggregate contains `unattended-park` records. When nothing clusters, **no line is emitted** (the advisory is falsifiable вҖ” smoke В§105 pins both the fires-when-candidates and suppressed-when-none arms).
- **Cost control**: gated by a stamp at the `ghjig_state_dir`-resolved `.../state/last-friction-surfaced` (with the `$GHJIG_ROOT/.claude/state/...` fallback, parity with the В§6.5(a) fetch stamp). The compute runs only when the stamp is older than `SESSION_START_FRICTION_TTL` seconds (default 21600 = 6 h, sharing the В§6.5(a) sync-check cadence) or absent, so most sessions skip it. The reader invocation is wrapped in `timeout $SESSION_START_FRICTION_TIMEOUT` (default 3 s; unbounded fallback when `timeout(1)`/`gtimeout(1)` is absent, matching В§6.5(a)). The stamp is touched only after a successful compute.
- **Fail-open**: any error (missing/empty audit log, reader non-zero, absent script, timeout) degrades to **silence** вҖ” the advisory never blocks, stalls, or fails session startup (SessionStart still reaches the prompt). It reads the per-project audit aggregate via `ghjig_state_dir` (keyed on `CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR`, not cwd), so it runs **before** the `in_scope || exit 0` gate like the В§6.5(a) sync check.
- **Park-frequency line**: the `unattended-park` records (emitted by `ship_park_pr`, В§5.7.1) are read **directly** by the advisory вҖ” neither candidate script matches a `warn`/`parked` record (`narrowing_candidates.sh` keys `event==escape`, `promotion_candidates.sh` keys `event==warn`+`decision==reject`), so park frequency is surfaced as its own grep, leaving both scripts untouched.
- **Ceremony-mismatch line** (#401, Directive #401): `scripts/ceremony_candidates.sh` is a **measure-first** reader (В§6.0 P3). Unlike the two audit-log readers it mines **commit history** вҖ” the ceremony signal (commit `type` + the DocвҶ’TestвҶ’Code phase arc + changed-file count) lives in `git log`, not `audit.jsonl`, and the Directive forbids adding an author-facing field to record it there. It groups commits by `#<issue>` and surfaces **both directions**: *under-ceremony* (a `feat` group spanning >1 file with no `test`/`docs` phase commit) and *over-ceremony* (a вүҘ3-commit phase arc over a single file). It emits the same indented `вҖҰ | вҖҰ =N` cluster shape the advisory greps, so it adds **no new surface**, and it runs `git -C` against the project repo through the advisory's `timeout вҖҰ || true` envelope so a non-repo cwd / missing base degrades to silence. **Honest limits** (surfaced, not corrected): a batched single-commit PR collapses the phase arc and can false-positive as under-ceremony; over-classification is only weakly detectable. **Measure-first**: it observes whether ceremony mis-sizing is real and recurring; hardening into a В§1.2 weight model or a relaxation gate is a deferred follow-up Directive **gated on this consumer's evidence** (the P3 born-advisory-then-harden order applied to the device's own roadmap).
- **Spec-drift line** (#462, Directive #455): `scripts/spec_drift_candidates.sh` is a fourth **measure-first** reader (В§6.0 P3) joining the family. Like the ceremony reader it mines `git log` (not `audit.jsonl`): it greps `SPEC.md` for the repo paths it references, then flags **code-ahead drift** вҖ” a commit that touched a referenced path **without** co-touching `SPEC.md` ("code moved, SPEC didn't"). It emits the same indented `вҖҰ | вҖҰ =N` cluster shape (`  <path> | drift-commits=N`), so it adds **no new surface**, and fails open (non-repo cwd / absent or empty `SPEC.md` / no candidates вҶ’ a sentinel line, exit 0). **Detection only**: the three-way classification (spec-ahead / code-ahead-correct / code-wrong) and the user-gated SPEC correction are the sibling `/reconcile-spec` flow (В§5.27). The reader **is wired into the advisory above** (#466): it joins the `_session_friction_advisory` reader set under the same `timeout` envelope + once-per-session `last-friction-surfaced` stamp, and when candidates exist the advisory line reports the outstanding **drift-candidate count** (`N spec-drift candidate(s)`) вҖ” the once-per-session surface that makes the drift signal consumed without a human running the script. **Honest limits** (surfaced, not corrected): a batched commit touching both code and `SPEC.md` for unrelated reasons masks a real drift, and the path-token grep is coarse вҖ” it over-surfaces by design, to **measure** the real signal before any reconciliation machinery is hardened.

**(e) SSOT-presence health line** (#460, Directive #454)

A once-per-session, zero-network glance at the target's SSOT presence вҖ” the recurring counterpart to the one-time `/onboard` SSOT check, so a repo that drifts into (or was never given) a `SPEC.md` is re-surfaced each session rather than flagged only at adoption. `SPEC.md` is the **required behavioural SSOT** for any code-carrying repo (В§1.3); this line keeps that expectation visible.

- **Single source**: the presence facts come from `scripts/lib/onboard_checks.sh --dry-run` (filtered to its `ssot:MISSION.md` / `ssot:SPEC.md` lines) вҖ” **not** a reimplemented `[ -f SPEC.md ]` (В§9 single-source; the same script `/onboard` and `setup.sh` consume).
- **No per-session `gh` call**: `--dry-run` short-circuits `onboard_checks.sh`'s `gh_usable()` **before** any `command -v gh`, so the path is purely filesystem (`ssot:*` are two `[ -f ]` facts). The gh-dependent checks (fork / permission / branch-protection) stay one-time in `/onboard` вҖ” this surface is the cheap glance, not the full report.
- **Render**: both present вҶ’ one unobtrusive line `SSOT: MISSION.md вң“ SPEC.md вң“`; `SPEC.md` absent вҶ’ a prominent **SPEC-first nudge** pointing the user to author it before other work (the shell scaffolds the slot from `.claude/templates/spec.md`, never authors the contract content вҖ” the MISSION boundary).
- **Cadence вҖ” every session, not TTL-debounced**: unlike the В§6.5(d) friction advisory (whose 6 h TTL debounces an *expensive* compute), the SSOT check is two stats, so it fires **every** session start to satisfy the "once per session" contract вҖ” a nudge suppressed for 6 h would under-deliver it. It therefore lives in the in-scope section (alongside the В§6.5(b) branch banner, **after** `in_scope`), so it reports only for a registered target's cwd (no false "SPEC.md absent" in an arbitrary directory) and needs no second stamp.
- **Fail-open**: any error (script absent, unreadable output, indeterminate status) degrades to **silence** вҖ” never blocks or stalls session startup.

### 6.6 Stack-aware behavior

`helpers/detect_stack.sh` picks an active stack for `/ship`'s test runner, the commit-time lint gate, and the PostToolUse formatter. Detection is by sentinel file at PWD:

| Stack | Sentinel | Test (used by `/ship`) | Lint (commit gate) | Format (PostToolUse) |
|-------|----------|------------------------|--------------------|----------------------|
| node | `package.json` | `npm test` (if `test` script) | `npm run lint` (if `lint` script) | `prettier --write` |
| python | `pyproject.toml` / `setup.py` / `requirements.txt` | `pytest` | `ruff check .` | `ruff format` or `black` |
| go | `go.mod` | `go test ./...` | `go vet ./...` | `gofmt -w` |
| rust | `Cargo.toml` | `cargo test` | `cargo check` | `rustfmt` |
| ruby | `Gemfile` | `bundle exec rspec` | вҖ” | вҖ” |
| godot | `project.godot` | `godot --headless вҖҰ` (GUT if present, otherwise parse-only) | `gdlint .` (if installed) | `gdformat` (.gd) |

Notes for godot:
- Test: when `addons/gut/gut_cmdln.gd` is present, `/ship` invokes GUT via `godot --headless --path . -s res://addons/gut/gut_cmdln.gd -gexit`. Otherwise a parse-only check runs (`godot --headless --path . --quit-after 1`) вҖ” confirms the project loads.
- Lint / format: `gdlint` and `gdformat` ship in the `gdtoolkit` PyPI package. Helpers only invoke them when on PATH; absence is silent (no false-positive block).
- Scene and resource files (`.tscn`, `.tres`, `.import`) are not auto-formatted вҖ” they are editor-managed and any rewrite risks corrupting binary subresources.
- The C# variant of Godot (`project.godot` + `*.csproj`) still resolves to `godot` (script-level tooling). Mixed-language CI is the project's call, not the shell's.

**Formatter invocation safety**: `detect_format_cmd` shell-quotes the file path via `printf '%q'` before interpolating it into the returned command string. The PostToolUse hook can therefore safely `eval` the result вҖ” filenames containing spaces, `;`, `$(...)`, backticks, or other shell metacharacters do not change the executed command. (PostToolUse is best-effort and silent on failure; SPEC В§6.2.)

A target with no recognized sentinel resolves to `unknown`; `/ship` reports "no test runner detected" but does not block. Adding a stack means extending `detect_stack` plus the corresponding `detect_test_cmd` / `detect_lint_cmd` / `detect_format_cmd` branches.

**Version-field location** (the В§18.2 release manifest-match preflight, #469, Directive #468): `detect_version` (in `helpers/detect_stack.sh`) is the **single-source** per-stack locator that reads the project's native version field, for a verification-only `/release` preflight вҖ” the field is read, **never written** (write-back stays the shell's own `VERSION`, В§18.2):

| Stack | Version field |
|-------|---------------|
| node | `package.json` вҶ’ `.version` |
| python | `pyproject.toml` вҶ’ `[project] version` |
| rust | `Cargo.toml` вҶ’ `[package] version` |
| go / ruby / godot | вҖ” (no universal manifest version field вҶ’ skip) |

An unrecognized stack, an absent manifest, or an unparseable field returns empty вҶ’ the preflight **degrades to a graceful skip** (never a false block), mirroring `detect_stack`'s `unknown` fail-open. The locator lives only here; `/release` does not duplicate per-stack version knowledge (В§9).

---

## 7. Escape hatch

Three forms, chosen by where the escape needs to be read. The **file-token channel** (below) is the **primary in-agent recourse**; the two in-command forms are verbatim-delivery forms (a real shell, the smoke harness) вҖ” they do **not** land in-harness.

> **Observed caveat (this harness, 2026-06; the harness is a moving floor вҖ” re-verify, В§1.9):** in the live Claude Code Bash tool **both** in-command forms are **stripped before the hook reads `tool_input.command`** вҖ” the leading env-prefix is consumed as the spawned subprocess's environment, and the trailing sentinel comment is stripped too. The parsers are correct (they set the tokens when fed the literal string in isolation, e.g. the smoke harness), but the harness does not deliver either to the hook, so **neither in-command form takes effect in-harness** (#478). The working in-agent channel is the **file-based skip token** below (#479): it is written to per-project state and read by the hook *at fire time*, so the harness has nothing to strip. The **fallback** for a sanctioned in-agent guarded op remains a **real terminal** (no PreToolUse hook fires there) or doing the work on a non-protected branch and renaming.

**File-based skip token (primary in-agent channel, #479)** вҖ” a one-shot, category-scoped token the hook reads at fire time from per-project state, so it survives the harness (unlike the two in-command forms above):

- **Location**: one file per category at `$(ghjig_state_dir)/escape/<category>.token` (per-project state dir, В§3.2.2; gitignored under `ghjig-state/`). Per-category isolation makes category-scoping **structural** вҖ” a `branch.token` can only ever disarm `branch`.
- **Format**: `KEY=VALUE`, one per line, exactly these four keys вҖ” `category`, `reason`, `cmd_fingerprint`, `created` (epoch seconds). **Strict allow-list parse**: an unknown key or a missing key вҮ’ malformed вҮ’ **not honored**.
