- **Reader**: pure bash вҖ” **no `python3`/`jq`** вҖ” so there is no interpreter-absent failure mode; the reader is strictly fail-safe. It is integrated into `should_skip <cat>`: after the existing `$SKIP_HOOKS` check, `should_skip` consults `<cat>.token`. The hook exports `ESCAPE_BIND_CMD=$raw_cmd` (the current command) for the fingerprint check.
- **Honored only if ALL hold**: the file exists and is readable; all four keys present with no unknown keys; the `category` field equals the requested category equals the filename; `cmd_fingerprint` is non-empty **and a substring of the current command** (`ESCAPE_BIND_CMD`); `created` is numeric **and** `now вҲ’ created вүӨ 60` (the **TTL**, 60 seconds); the bind-cmd is non-empty.
- **On honor**: `audit_log escape <category> skip "<reason>"` (parity with the `SKIP_HOOKS` escape audit) вҶ’ **consume (delete) the token** вҶ’ skip that one category.
- **One-shot / consume-on-read**: the token is deleted on honor **and** deleted on a stale/malformed reject (poison cleanup) вҖ” a token never survives a `should_skip` call that examined it.
- **Fail-safe-to-block**: **any** doubt вҖ” absent, unreadable, malformed, category-mismatch, fingerprint-not-a-substring, stale, future-or-non-numeric `created`, empty bind-cmd вҖ” leaves enforcement **armed** (the matcher blocks). Never a spurious skip.
- **Binding weight (read this correctly).** The real AC-5 guards are **consume-once + the 60s TTL**: a token is single-use and self-expires. The `cmd_fingerprint` substring binding and the writer's min-length refusal are **footgun-reducers** вҖ” they stop a *stale or pre-written* token from disarming an *unintended* command вҖ” **not a security mechanism**. The threat model (В§6.1) is unchanged: hooks are mistake-prevention, not a security boundary; anyone who can write `ghjig-state/` can `bash -c` around the hook, so **no crypto/signature is used or needed**. Choose a **high-entropy distinguishing** fingerprint вҖ” the commit subject / version / branch name вҖ” **not** a bare verb like `git commit`.
- **Writer affordance**: `scripts/ghjig_skip.sh <category> <cmd_fingerprint> [reason]` вҖ” the fingerprint is **required** (it refuses to write without one, and refuses a fingerprint shorter than 8 chars as a footgun-reducer); the **category** is interpolated into the token path, so it is constrained to `^[A-Za-z0-9,_-]+$` вҖ” a value outside that charset (e.g. a `../`-traversal attempt) is refused with no token written (#551); the write is atomic, per-category, under `ghjig_state_dir` (the writer resolves the same project dir the hook reads вҖ” deriving it from the git top-level when `CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR` is unset for a Bash-tool subprocess вҖ” so writer and reader always agree, #483). The Write tool to `$(ghjig_state_dir)/escape/<cat>.token` (e.g. `.claude/ghjig-state/escape/<cat>.token`) is a documented **fallback** writer (the `.claude/` Edit/Write carve-out, В§6.1).
- **Bash-only boundary (R1, by design вҖ” not an oversight).** The channel works only on the **Bash** tool path, where `ESCAPE_BIND_CMD=$raw_cmd` is set. The **Edit/Write** protected-branch arm has **no command string**, so it cannot carry a token and the in-agent escape does **not** cover Edit/Write вҖ” consistent with В§5.0 step 2, which already routes the bootstrap MISSION/README authoring through a Bash `cp` precisely because "there is no command string to carry [a sentinel]."

The two in-command forms below remain defined (they land verbatim in a real shell and the smoke harness); they are no longer the in-agent recourse.

**Trailing sentinel** вҖ” read from the trailing edge of the raw command:
```bash
<command>  # ghjig:skip=<category>[,<category>...] reason=<reason>
```

**Leading env-prefix** вҖ” read from the leading edge of `tool_input.command`; works only where the prefix arrives *inside* the command string (a real shell that passes it verbatim, and the smoke harness):
```bash
SKIP_HOOKS=<category>[,<category>...] SKIP_REASON='<reason>' <command>
```

The PreToolUse hook parses the leading `SKIP_HOOKS=вҖҰ`/`SKIP_REASON=вҖҰ` tokens from the leading edge of `tool_input.command`, **and** a `# ghjig:skip=вҖҰ reason=вҖҰ` sentinel from the trailing edge of the raw command. Two forms exist as defense in depth across execution environments where one or the other arrives verbatim (a real shell, the smoke harness). **In the live Claude Code Bash tool, however, neither lands in `tool_input.command`:** the leading `VAR=val` is consumed as the spawned subprocess's own environment (the hook subprocess does not inherit it either вҖ” В§6.1), and the trailing `#`-comment is **stripped before the hook reads the command** too вҖ” so in-harness the recourse above (real terminal / non-protected branch + rename) applies, not these in-command forms. Both forms export the recognized tokens into the hook before downstream matchers run, then strip them from the command for the matcher pass (so a `reason=` containing a blockable substring cannot bleed into another matcher); **if both are present, the leading form wins.** Recognized tokens: `SKIP_HOOKS`/`SKIP_REASON` (leading) and `ghjig:skip=`/`reason=` (trailing) only вҖ” any other ALLCAPS `K=V` leading token (`PATH=`, `LD_PRELOAD=`, вҖҰ) halts the leading scan and is left as an ordinary argument. The sentinel is parsed from the **raw** command before whitespace-normalization (the normalization + `shlex` pass would otherwise mangle the `#`), is namespaced (`ghjig:skip=`) so an ordinary trailing comment is never mistaken for an escape, and is **one-shot** вҖ” it travels with the single command, so there is no persistent bypass state. The sentinel is honored **only when its `#` is a genuine unquoted shell comment token** вҖ” a `#` that the executed shell itself treats as the start of a comment. A `#` sitting inside a quoted argument (e.g. `gh pr comment 5 --body "see note # ghjig:skip=all reason=x"`) is argument text, not a comment: the shell runs the whole command intact, so the hook must **not** read it as an escape (doing so would let ordinary quoted text вҖ” a commit message, a PR-body paste, audit output quoting the sentinel вҖ” silently disarm every matcher with a falsified audit reason). The comment-token boundary is resolved with the same `python3`/`shlex` machinery the leading env-prefix uses; if `python3` is absent the trailing sentinel is **not** honored вҖ” a fail-safe no-op (enforcement stays armed), never a spurious skip. The sentinel must sit on the command's **final line** (the match is confined to a single line via `[[:blank:]]`/non-control-char classes plus a newline guard) so a line-1 sentinel can never strip or disarm a dangerous *later* line вҖ” such a command falls through to the matchers and blocks. **Scope:** like the leading env-prefix, the trailing sentinel is **command-scoped** вҖ” it disarms its named category (or `all`) across **every** line/clause of the command, not only the line it sits on. It remains **category-scoped**: a tail sentinel naming category X does not disarm a category-Y matcher (that command still blocks). So an `escape` audit record proves *which* category was skipped with a stated reason вҖ” read it as "category X was skipped for this command," not "this exact line was approved"; the reason text need not describe the specific operation disarmed. When run in a real terminal where neither form reaches a hook (there is no PreToolUse hook outside the harness), the command simply runs; the escape only matters when a hook is in the path.

Categories:
- `all`
- **eng-flow hook matchers:** `secret`, `branch`, `commit-format`, `format`, `force-push`, `amend`, `no-verify`, `destructive`, `sensitive`, `out-of-scope`, `backmerge`, `ac-closeout`, `merge-strategy`, `push-parity`, `merge-attestation`
- **type-aware / dir-mode hook matchers (В§6.1):** `proposed-protect`, `trusted-filer-mutate`, `label-parent-consistency`, `initiative-readonly`, `directive-close`
- **command-level reviewer-gate escapes:** `directive-review` (the `activation-reviewer` gate on `/file-directive` / `/activate` / `/revise-directive` / `/complete-directive` / `/consume-initiative`, В§4.9/В§5.10вҖ“В§5.22), `release-review` (the `code-reviewer` gate on `/release`, В§5.20)

This list is the complete set of `SKIP_HOOKS` categories the runtime honors (the hook matchers via `should_skip <cat>` in `pre_tool_use.sh`; the reviewer-gate escapes via the command/skill prose). It is kept in sync with the matchers/commands by the doc-consistency smoke check (В§17 / #267) вҖ” a new `should_skip <cat>` or reviewer-gate escape that is not listed here fails smoke.

(`issue-ref` is folded into `commit-format` вҖ” not a separate category. `format` is the commit-time lint/format gate. `out-of-scope` covers paths outside the registry (В§6.1). `backmerge` covers `git merge <protected-base>` on a feature branch (В§6.1). `ac-closeout` covers `gh pr merge` when a linked issue has unchecked AC and no `^## AC closeout` comment вҖ” see SPEC В§6.1 row + В§5.7.1 step 7.6 for the rule (step 7.5 is the unrelated checklist audit); `scripts/ac_closeout.sh <pr-num>` is the canonical fixer. `merge-strategy` covers `gh pr merge` to the default branch without `--merge` вҖ” see SPEC В§6.1 row + В§5.7.1 (squash erases the DocвҶ’TestвҶ’Code arc on the trunk); squash is allowed on a non-default base. `push-parity` covers `gh pr merge` while the local branch is strictly ahead of its pushed remote head (unpushed commits, git-only, #244) and `merge-attestation` covers `gh pr merge` whose review was skipped (no attestation file, zero-network) or done at a stale head (#543) вҖ” both un-skippable pre-merge arms, see SPEC В§6.1 rows + В§5.7. Tests are run by `/ship`, not a hook, so there's no `tests` category.)

Every skip is recorded in `.claude/audit/audit.jsonl`:
```json
{"ts":"2026-05-19T...","event":"escape","decision":"skip","category":"format","reason":"flaky lint JIRA-1234","cwd":"...","source":"live"}
```

The `reason` and `cwd` fields are JSON-encoded via `jq -Rs .` (or an inline `\n`/`\r`/`\t`/`\\`/`\"` escape when jq is absent). Newlines and control characters in `SKIP_REASON`, and shell metacharacters in PWD (legal in POSIX paths), therefore do not break the "one JSON object per line" invariant вҖ” every `audit.jsonl` is parseable by `jq -c '.'` regardless of input contents. Other fields (`event`, `category`, `decision`, `ts`, `source`) are internal-constant or RFC 3339-shaped and need no encoding (`source` is the `live`/`test` enum, В§6.1).

Policy:
- Skips should be temporary.
- A skip with no `SKIP_REASON` is logged as `unspecified` вҖ” review target.
- `all` is for emergencies.
- A category that gets skipped repeatedly means the hook is misconfigured вҖ” open a fix PR.

Audit logs rotate as appropriate (exact threshold is an implementation choice), but the diff body is never written вҖ” only path, line, category metadata.

---

## 8. Directory structure (final)

This tree is **authoritative and drift-guarded by smoke В§103**: the flat leaf-list directories (`agents/`, `commands/`, `helpers/`, `docs/`) are count-checked against disk, so a PR that adds or removes one of those files must update this block in the same PR. `templates/` and `scripts/` carry summarized subtree nodes (their leaves churn independently); the guard asserts those subtree nodes are present rather than counting their leaves. Regenerate this block when the flat-dir contents change.

```
GHJig-Claude/
в”ңв”Җв”Җ README.md
в”ңв”Җв”Җ README.ko.md
в”ңв”Җв”Җ SPEC.md                           вҶҗ this document
в”ңв”Җв”Җ MISSION.md                        вҶҗ canonical long-term direction
в”ңв”Җв”Җ CHANGELOG.md
в”ңв”Җв”Җ VERSION                           вҶҗ version of record (В§18.2)
в”ңв”Җв”Җ .gitignore                        вҶҗ workspace/* (with .gitkeep and README.md whitelisted), .claude/{audit,state,ghjig-state}/
в”Ӯ
в”ңв”Җв”Җ changelog_unreleased/             вҶҗ per-PR changelog fragments (В§18.1), consolidated by /release
в”Ӯ
в”ңв”Җв”Җ .claude/
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ settings.json                 вҶҗ hook / permission definitions (shell's own session)
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ settings.injected.json        вҶҗ injected-target hook config (symlink target; В§3.2.1)
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ CLAUDE.md                     вҶҗ shell norms
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ agents/                       вҶҗ 11 subagents (В§4); count-guarded (smoke В§103)
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ activation-reviewer.md
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ code-reviewer.md

в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ escape.sh
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ gh_state.sh           вҶҗ PR/issue lookup helpers
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ git_matcher.sh        вҶҗ protected-branch + git-subcommand patterns (SSOT; must precede branch_guard)
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ issue_filer.sh        вҶҗ is_trusted_filer (authorAssociation; В§6.1)
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ issue_type.sh         вҶҗ is_directive_issue / is_proposed_issue / parent-marker predicates (В§1.7, В§6.1)
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ log.sh                вҶҗ bootstrap shim вҶ’ hookrt.sh
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ pr_cache.sh           вҶҗ PR body cache (В§5.4)
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ recall.sh             вҶҗ recall_pointers decision-record retrieval (В§5.25)
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ replan_check.sh       вҶҗ replan_check_facts plan-divergence facts (В§5.26)
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ reviewer_audit.sh     вҶҗ reviewer_reject_audit categorized reject record (В§6.1)
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ secret_scan.sh
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ ship_mode.sh          вҶҗ resolve_mode operating-mode resolution + post-ready dispatch (В§5.7.1)
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ status.sh             вҶҗ status_compact projection (В§5.5, В§6.4)
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ tests.sh
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ       в””в”Җв”Җ work_lang.sh          вҶҗ resolve_work_lang (В§5.7.2)
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ templates/                    вҶҗ 9 top-level templates (В§9) + target-substrate subtree
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ adr.md
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ directive.md
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ issue.md
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ issue_template_for_target.md
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ mission.md
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ pr_body.md
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ pr_template_for_target.md
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ readme_for_target.md
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ spec.md
в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ target-substrate/         вҶҗ installed into targets by /onboard-dir-mode: workflows/, ISSUE_TEMPLATE/, changelog_unreleased/
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ audit/                        вҶҗ .gitignored (legacy shared audit.jsonl вҖ” block / escape / warn events)
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ state/                        вҶҗ .gitignored (legacy shared caches + back-compat registry floor)
в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ ghjig-state/                    вҶҗ .gitignored (per-project audit/caches/registry вҖ” В§3.2.2, #314/#316)
в”Ӯ
в”ңв”Җв”Җ bin/
в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ ghjig                    вҶҗ env setup + binding check + exec claude (В§3.5)
в”Ӯ
в”ңв”Җв”Җ scripts/                          вҶҗ 19 top-level scripts + lib/ + test/
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ ac_closeout.sh                вҶҗ posts '## AC closeout' on PR-linked issues (idempotent; satisfies В§6.1 gate)
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ bootstrap.sh
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ build_toc.sh                  вҶҗ regenerates the SPEC TOC (В§0 reading note; smoke В§28 --check)
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ ceremony_candidates.sh        вҶҗ clusters commit-history ceremony mis-sizing вҶ’ measure-first candidates (В§6.0 P3, В§6.5(d))
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ clone-into.sh
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ dir_mode_project.sh
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ ghjig_skip.sh                   вҶҗ writes a one-shot file-based skip token (В§7 file-token escape channel)
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ ensure_v3_labels.sh           вҶҗ installs directive / status / P0-P3 labels (В§0.4)
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ lint.sh                       вҶҗ pinned+SHA256-verified shellcheck; per-file lint + Linux peak-RSS flag (В§11, #545)
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ migrate_v3.sh
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ narrowing_candidates.sh       вҶҗ clusters escape records вҶ’ narrowing candidates (В§6.0 P3)
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ onboard_target.sh
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ promotion_candidates.sh       вҶҗ aggregates reviewer-reject classes вҶ’ advisoryвҶ’hook promotion candidates (В§6.0 P3)
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ spec_drift_candidates.sh      вҶҗ clusters code-ahead code-vs-SPEC drift вҶ’ measure-first candidates (В§6.0 P3, В§6.5(d))

в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ setup.sh                      вҶҗ single host-side entry: deps вҶ’ register/clone вҶ’ onboard pre-flight вҶ’ dir-mode gate (В§3.5)
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ setup_project.sh
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ lib/                          вҶҗ shared script libs: audit_log_path, detect_bare_refs_directive, dir_mode_project_resolve, inject, resolve_parent_directive, self_register
в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ test/
в”Ӯ       в””в”Җв”Җ smoke.sh                  вҶҗ smoke suite (В§16 verification; numbered В§-sections)
в”Ӯ
в”ңв”Җв”Җ workspace/                        вҶҗ .gitignored body
в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ .gitkeep
в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ README.md
в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җ docs/                             вҶҗ 7 thin-pointer digests (В§9); count-guarded (smoke В§103)
    в”ңв”Җв”Җ CONFIG.md
    в”ңв”Җв”Җ DIR_MODE_FLOW.md              вҶҗ dir-mode flow digest
    в”ңв”Җв”Җ ENGINEERING_FLOW.md           вҶҗ flow diagram + step details
    в”ңв”Җв”Җ ESCAPE_HATCH.md
    в”ңв”Җв”Җ HARNESS_OVERLAP.md            вҶҗ harness-overlap classification pointer (В§1.9)
    в”ңв”Җв”Җ SUBAGENTS.md                  вҶҗ eleven-agent usage guide
    в””в”Җв”Җ TROUBLESHOOTING.md            вҶҗ common blocks + fixes
```

---

## 9. Template specifications

Each `.claude/templates/` file is read by a command and variable-substituted at use time. Single source of truth.

**`docs/*.md` and `.claude/CLAUDE.md` are thin pointers, not parallel content.** The human-facing `docs/*.md` digests (e.g. `ENGINEERING_FLOW.md`, `DIR_MODE_FLOW.md`, `SUBAGENTS.md`) exist as a readable on-ramp to a SPEC section вҖ” they must **lead with a "Full details/spec in SPEC В§X" reference and carry no parallel or detailed contract content** that could silently drift from the SPEC. SPEC is the single source; a digest that restates a contract becomes a second copy to keep in sync by hand (the divergence hazard В§1.3's single-file principle exists to prevent). Smoke enforces the lead-with-a-SPEC-reference rule (В§91). When a digest would need detail to be useful, link to the SPEC section instead of duplicating it.

The same discipline binds `.claude/CLAUDE.md`. Unlike the `docs/*.md` digests, `.claude/CLAUDE.md` is an **always-on injected surface** вҖ” Claude Code natively loads it whole every session вҖ” so it must point to SPEC for contract detail and carry no detailed contract content that could drift. It is held to a size budget: `wc -c .claude/CLAUDE.md` must stay **вүӨ 12000 bytes** (drift-guarded by smoke В§104). The always-on injected floor is task-independent context loaded before any task is known, so an unbounded always-on surface is "bloat past the task" (MISSION:20); keeping `CLAUDE.md` a thin pointer-index is the always-on counterpart to В§6.4's per-turn `status_compact` narrowing.

### 9.1 `mission.md` (draft for target's `MISSION.md`)

Draft body for a target's `MISSION.md`, offered by `/onboard` (В§5.1) and `/bootstrap-repo` (В§5.0) when absent; authoritative body in `.claude/templates/mission.md` (substitutes `{{ today }}`). Fixed sections: `## What this exists for` (one paragraph вҖ” what breaks without this project), `## Success looks like` (3вҖ“5 observable metrics/scenarios), `## Explicitly NOT goals`, `## Stakeholders`, `## Last reviewed:`. The shell scaffolds the slot; it never authors the contract content (В§5.1).

### 9.2 `issue.md`

Draft body for `gh issue create`, enforced by `/file-issue` (В§5.2); authoritative body in `.claude/templates/issue.md` (no substitution vars). Fixed sections: `## What`, `## Why` (names the `MISSION.md` item/metric served), `## Acceptance criteria` (вүҘ1 verifiable `- [ ]` condition), `## Out of scope`, `## Notes`. The MISSION reference, acceptance criteria, and a priority are the В§5.2 rationale-triad `issue-reviewer` gates on.

### 9.3 `pr_body.md`

Draft body for `gh pr create --body-file`, authored by `/work-on` (В§5.3) and curated as the PR-as-living-doc (В§1.4); authoritative body in `.claude/templates/pr_body.md` (substitutes `{{ closes_or_refs }}`, `{{ issue }}`). `{{ closes_or_refs }}` becomes `Closes` (single or final PR) or `Refs` (intermediate PR) per В§10.3 вҖ” `/work-on` defaults to `Closes`, the user adjusts on split. Sections вҖ” Goal, How this serves the mission, Plan, Alternatives considered, Key context, Checklist, Out of scope, Risks, Open questions, Decisions, Test plan, Docs touched, Ship gate вҖ” and who fills each are the В§9.3.1 contract below.

#### 9.3.1 Section owners

| Section | Filled by | When |
|---------|-----------|------|
| `{{ closes_or_refs }} #<N>` | `/work-on` (default `Closes`), user adjusts on split | PR create / split decision |
| Goal | `/work-on` (one-line summary of issue title, user confirms) | PR create |
| How this serves the mission | planner | PR create |
| Plan | planner | PR create |
| Alternatives considered | planner (mandatory; forced-choice acceptable) | PR create |
| Key context | planner + (if needed) explorer enrichment | PR create / during work |
| Checklist | planner (Doc/Test/Code order) | PR create / ticked during work |
| Out of scope | planner | PR create |
| Risks | planner | PR create |
| Open questions | planner | PR create / all resolved before merge |
| Decisions | main assistant (`/adr` auto-links ADRs) | during work |
| Test plan | test-writer | Phase B |
| Docs touched | doc-writer | Phase A |
| Ship gate | fixed (template); `/ship` verifies and ticks | PR create / `/ship` |

### 9.4 `adr.md`

Draft body for an Architecture Decision Record, authored by `/adr` for irreversible decisions; authoritative body in `.claude/templates/adr.md` (substitutes `{{ number }}`, `{{ title }}`, `{{ today }}`, `{{ pr }}`). Fixed sections: a header (`# ADR {{ number }}: {{ title }}` + Date / `Status` / Context PR lines), `## Context`, `## Decision`, `## Alternatives considered` (each with why-rejected), `## Consequences`, `## Notes`. `Status` follows the lifecycle `Proposed` вҶ’ `Accepted` вҶ’ `Superseded by ADR-<M>` (the file seeds `Proposed`). Linked from the PR body `## Decisions` section (В§9.3).

### 9.5 `pr_template_for_target.md`, `issue_template_for_target.md`

Standard templates the target repo can install into `.github/`. `/onboard` suggests these when absent.

The shell repo **dogfoods its own scaffold** (#320, SPEC В§17): `.github/PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE.md` is `pr_template_for_target.md` with the leading install-hint HTML comment stripped вҖ” so a human/web-UI PR against the shell opens with the same Doc/Test/Code + Ship-gate checklist the shell mandates everywhere else. Smoke asserts the two stay in sync (the PR template equals the target template minus its comment line), so an edit to one without the other fails CI. (The `/ship` skill path is unaffected вҖ” it authors PR bodies from `pr_body.md` via `gh pr create --body-file`; the GitHub template only scaffolds manual PRs.)

### 9.6 `directive.md`

Read by `/file-directive` (В§5.10) and variable-substituted into a Directive Issue body; the body is then reviewer-gated by `activation-reviewer` (В§4.9.1). Fixed section set (every section required): `## Objective` (must name a concrete artifact-level boundary вҖ” file paths / issue counts / AC ticks / merge events, not "improve" without a target), `## Success signals` (2вҖ“5 objectively-testable conditions), `## Non-goals` (вүҘ2 explicit exclusions), `## Constraints` (вүҘ1 invariant to preserve), `## MISSION fit` (names the `MISSION.md` section/criterion served), `## Priority` (`P0`/`P1`/`P2`/`P3`, default `P2`), `## Confidence` (0вҖ“100). The `priority=P<N>` value feeds the `directive-file/created` audit record validated by `_audit_validate_format` (`hookrt.sh`).

### 9.7 `spec.md`

Draft for a target's `SPEC.md`, copied by `/bootstrap-repo` (В§5.0) and suggested by `/onboard` (В§5.1) when absent. Substitutes `{{ project }}`. Ships a machine-generated **Table of contents** block (the START/END markers `build_toc.sh` regenerates) followed by a broad section skeleton вҖ” `## 1. Overview`, `## 2. Contracts`, `## 3. Non-goals` вҖ” that the target grows section-by-section. Carries the single-file-SSOT guidance in its header blockquote (consult the ToC, `Read --offset` the section; split into a per-subsystem directory only when the file grows too large to read whole).

### 9.8 `readme_for_target.md`

Draft for a target's `README.md`, copied by `/bootstrap-repo` step 2 (В§5.0). Substitutes `{{ repo_name }}`. Sections: a one-paragraph description, `## Status` (records the stage-0 bootstrap + the `/onboard` next step), `## Getting started` (build/run/test, filled as the project takes shape), `## Documentation` (links to `MISSION.md` and the rest of the SSOT set).

---

## 10. Convention summary

### 10.1 Branch naming

```
<gh-username>/<type>/[<issue#>-]<slug>

# required-issue-# group (feat/fix/docs/refactor/perf) вҖ” always includes <issue#>-
ilgyu/feat/42-oidc-login
ilgyu/fix/57-null-pointer
ilgyu/docs/89-update-architecture

# optional group (chore/style/build/ci/test/revert) вҖ” issue # may be omitted
ilgyu/chore/typo-readme
ilgyu/chore/89-update-deps    вҶҗ if an issue exists, you can include it
```

Types: `feat | fix | docs | style | refactor | perf | test | build | ci | chore | revert`

`/work-on <issue#>` always has an issue, so it always includes `<issue#>-` regardless of group. Issueless ad-hoc branches in the optional group are created by the user with plain `git checkout -b`.

### 10.2 Commit messages

```
<type>(#<issue>)[!]: <subject вүӨ 72 chars>

<body вҖ” one blank line>

Closes #<N>     вҶҗ last commit, or single-PR consolidator
Refs #<N>       вҶҗ intermediate commit
Co-Authored-By: Claude <noreply@anthropic.com>   вҶҗ optional trailer; toggleable
```

Phase prefixes:
- `docs(#42): describe OIDC callback flow`
- `test(#42): add failing tests for /auth/oidc/callback`
- `feat(#42): implement OIDC callback handler`

**Co-Authored-By trailer toggle**: the `Co-Authored-By: Claude вҖҰ` line is a convention, not a contract. It is included by default but can be disabled per-target. Resolution priority (high вҶ’ low, mirroring SPEC В§5.7.1's mode pattern):

1. `$GHJIG_COAUTHOR` env var (`on` / `off`).
2. `.claude/state/coauthor` per-target file (one of `on` / `off`, no other content).
3. Default `on`.

Unknown values fail-safe to `on` and emit a stderr warning naming the offending source. The helper `.claude/hooks/helpers/coauthor.sh` exposes `coauthor_trailer` (prints the line when enabled, empty when disabled); `/work-on`'s commit template sources it. The line is **version-agnostic** вҖ” `Co-Authored-By: Claude <noreply@anthropic.com>`, with no model version (#294) вҖ” so it never re-drifts at a model bump (it was previously pinned to `Opus 4.7` and went stale once the model advanced to 4.8). The toggle covers the default behavior of `/work-on` flows only вҖ” the trailer remains free to be added or omitted manually in any specific commit.

**`ghjig_commit` slot-assembly helper** (Issue #436; ADR-0002 GO target): the positive-enforcement face (В§6.0) of the commit-subject contract вҖ” the agent *fills slots* instead of hand-rolling `git commit -m "<type>(#N): вҖҰ"`. `.claude/hooks/helpers/ghjig_commit.sh` exposes `ghjig_commit <type> <issue> <subject> [body-paragraphвҖҰ]`: it assembles `<type>(#<issue>): <subject>`, validates it via `check_commit_subject` (format + 1..72 codepoints) **before** committing вҖ” on rejection it errors `ghjig_commit: вҖҰ` with a nonzero rc and **does not commit** (the failure surfaces with full context, not as an opaque post-hoc hook block). It then commits via a **bash argv array** `git commit -m "<subject>" -m "<body-para>"вҖҰ ` (one `-m` per body paragraph, `coauthor_trailer` appended as a final `-m` when enabled):

- The **first `-m` carries only the assembled subject**, so the `commit-format` matcher *sees and accepts* it on the happy path вҖ” `ghjig_commit` does **not** rely on the `-F` fail-open bypass (git's `-m`/`-F` are mutually exclusive anyway, and an `-F`-only commit makes the matcher extract an empty subject and skip the check вҖ” a bypass, not a guarantee).
- The **array argv** (no `eval`, no string re-quoting) makes multibyte and multi-paragraph bodies round-trip losslessly вҖ” the inline-`-m` quoting pitfall is a string-construction hazard, absent when argv is assembled programmatically.

**Offered, not forced**: `ghjig_commit` is positive guidance with the `commit-format` hook retained as the mandatory net (В§6.0 P4); skills *offer* it (e.g. `/work-on`'s commit step) but the hand-roll path remains valid. The caller passes the `Closes #N` / `Refs #N` trailer as a body paragraph (the trailer choice is base-dependent, В§10.3/В§10.5 вҖ” the caller's decision, not the helper's).

**Relationship with Conventional Commits (conscious choice)**: we reuse the standard CC `scope` slot for the issue # marker. Consequences:

- Passes default `commitlint` rules (with `(#42)` allowed in scope).
- Tools like `conventional-changelog` / `semantic-release` parse `(#42)` as scope, so changelog scope columns will show `#42`. We don't carry both a domain scope (e.g. `auth`) and issue # вҖ” issue # wins.
- If a domain scope is essential, put it in the commit body via a `Scope: auth` trailer.

### 10.3 PRs

- Always start as draft.
- `Closes #N` or `Refs #N` is required. If a single issue spans multiple PRs, intermediates use `Refs #N` and the final uses `Closes #N`. Checklist distribution is planner/user's call.
- **Base**: PRs default to `main`. For experimental or long-lived feature work, `/work-on --base <branch>` opens the PR against an alternate base вҖ” see В§10.5. Non-`main`-base PRs default to `Refs` (the issue closes only when the work reaches `main`).
- Body follows `.claude/templates/pr_body.md`.
- Curate the body right after each commit.
- `/ship` transitions to ready after ship-gate verification.

### 10.4 PR вҶ” checklist sync

Order: **commit вҶ’ PR body update**. Commit is the fact; PR body reflects it. Reverse order creates "checklist ticked but commit absent" states. Refetch the remote body right before updating вҖ” abort the auto-update if external edits (reviewer, GitHub UI, parallel session) are detected.

### 10.5 Topic-branch workflow

The default flow (`/work-on <#>`) targets `main`. For two scenarios the user can opt into an alternate base via `/work-on <#> --base <branch>`:

1. **Experimental work** вҖ” risk too high for `main`. The user creates `experiment/foo` from `main`, iterates with a few PRs whose base is `experiment/foo`, and only consolidates to `main` via one final PR when the experiment stabilizes (or abandons the branch).
2. **Big features** вҖ” a multi-PR refactor where the integration point is a long-lived feature branch. Sub-task PRs target the feature branch; the feature branch itself is eventually merged to `main`.

**Conventions:**
- Sub-task PRs use `Refs #N` (not `Closes #N`) so the issue stays open until work reaches `main`. `/work-on` enforces this default for non-`main` bases.
- The alternate base must already exist locally + remotely. `/work-on --base <branch>` does NOT auto-create it; the user creates the base deliberately (e.g. `git checkout main && git pull && git checkout -b experiment/foo && git push -u origin experiment/foo`).
- The alternate base's remote branch-protection settings are the user's responsibility. For sub-task PRs to auto-merge into `experiment/foo`, the GitHub branch-protection rules on `experiment/foo` must permit the same flow as `main` (or be more permissive). `/work-on` does not inspect or modify remote settings.
- The alternate base is NOT in SPEC В§6.1's protected list (`main`/`master`/`release/*`). The user is free to commit directly to `experiment/foo` between sub-task PRs вҖ” it's an integration point, not the canonical product line.
- The work-branch name (`<gh-user>/<type>/<#>-<slug>`) is unchanged. Stacking multiple work-PRs on the same issue+base is not supported by `/work-on` alone вҖ” manual branch creation (`git checkout -b ...`) is the escape hatch for that rare case.

**Use with Directives (dir-mode integration):** scenario 2 ("Big features") is the canonical pattern for Directive-scoped multi-PR work (В§1.7, В§2.1). The user creates a topic branch from `main` (e.g., `feature/directive-92`); each Execution Issue parented under the Directive (via `/file-issue --parent <directive-#>`, В§5.2) runs `/work-on <execution-#> --base feature/directive-92`, producing sub-task PRs with `Refs #N`. The Directive Issue itself is **not** branched вҖ” the `proposed-protect` matcher in В§6.1 blocks `git checkout -b` against a Directive Issue (any status), by design; the Directive scopes the work, the Execution Issues do the work. Consolidation follows the standard pattern (one final PR head=topic-branch, base=`main`, body `Closes` each Execution Issue), and `/ship`'s Directive-aware audit (В§5.7) fires once per parented Execution Issue at consolidation. `/complete-directive <directive-#>` (В§5.13) must run **after** consolidation вҖ” `activation-reviewer` (В§4.9) evaluates closed-Execution-Issue evidence, so running completion while the topic branch is still unconsolidated yields insufficient-evidence and blocks.

**Consolidation back to `main`:** when the topic branch is ready, open ONE PR with head=`experiment/foo` and base=`main`, body `Closes #<#>`. This is a regular `gh pr create` invocation вҖ” `/work-on` is not designed for the consolidator step (the branch already exists; there's no planner phase to repeat).

**Enforcement вҖ” the bare-`Refs`-to-default anti-pattern (#337):** the convention above requires that directive-scoped work reach the default branch via a PR that `Closes` an Execution Issue; a PR that merges to the default branch carrying only bare `Refs #N` (empty closing set) leaks the work вҖ” no Execution Issue closes, so the dir-mode post-merge reflection chain never fires and the parent Directive gets no progress record (the historical #92 failure: PRs #100вҖ“105 merged to `main` with bare `Refs`, no `Closes`). The **post-merge workflow** (`.github/workflows/dir-mode-post-merge.yml`, В§5.15) enforces this: on a merged PR whose base is the **live default branch** AND whose `closingIssuesReferences` is **empty** AND whose body carries вүҘ1 `Refs #N` resolving (via the same depth-2 label-aware climb as the reflection resolver, #335) to a **directive-scoped** issue (a Directive, or an Execution Issue parented under one), it posts a single idempotent **warning comment on the merged PR** (marker `<!-- bare-refs-warning pr=#N -->`) naming the violation and the recovery (re-open + `Closes` an Execution Issue, or run `/reflect <pr>`). It is **warn-only** вҖ” the merge already happened, so there is no block point вҖ” and **fail-soft** (any `gh` resolution failure вҶ’ no warning, never aborts the workflow). The check lives in the post-merge **workflow**, not a PreToolUse hook, deliberately: the #92 violations were predominantly human GitHub-UI merges, which a `gh pr merge` hook structurally never observes; the merge-triggered workflow fires regardless of who merged. The detection logic is a sourced, smoke-tested helper (`scripts/lib/detect_bare_refs_directive.sh`) with the same three-copy cmp-locked discipline as the resolver.

---

## 11. CI awareness

- **Right before** ready transition: `gh pr checks --json state` for a one-time check. **Block only on `failure` or `cancelled`**. `pending` / `in_progress` / `queued` pass вҖ” the background watch picks up monitoring after ready transition. (В§5.7 step 7)
- **Right after** ready transition: `gh pr checks --watch` runs in **background**, returning immediately.
- The background watch's failure detection routes to a PostToolUse hook (В§6.2) notification.
- The post-push PostToolUse hook (`Bash` matching `git push`) also warns about PR-less push patterns (detached HEAD, missing draft PR).

This shell repo ships its own CI workflow at `.github/workflows/ci.yml` running on `pull_request` and `push: main`. The `syntax` and `smoke` jobs run on an OS matrix of `ubuntu-latest` and `macos-latest` (the BSD branch is the production path for the primary user; Linux-only CI would leave it unverified); the `mutation` job (В§11.1) runs on `ubuntu-latest` only (its logic is platform-independent; the matchers themselves are covered per-OS by `smoke`):
- **syntax** вҖ” `bash -n` AND `shellcheck --severity=warning --shell=bash` over `bin/ghjig`, `scripts/*.sh`, `scripts/lib/*.sh`, `.claude/hooks/*.sh`, `.claude/hooks/helpers/*.sh`. Repo-wide silences (e.g. SC1090 for dynamic sourcing via `BASH_SOURCE`-relative paths and per-test fixture variables) live in `.shellcheckrc`; documented-deliberate patterns (`eval` on jq-emitted `@sh` scripts in `helpers/status.sh`, `printf -v` to dynamic varname in `helpers/escape.sh`) carry inline `# shellcheck disable=SCвҖҰ` with one-line justification. Both the enumeration and the invocation live in **`scripts/lint.sh`** вҖ” the CI `syntax` job runs `./scripts/lint.sh`, and a developer runs the **same** script locally, so "clean locally" and "clean in CI" are one predicate by construction (the local-pre-image-of-remote-gate discipline, В§7.4/В§18.6). shellcheck is **version-pinned** (`GHJIG_SHELLCHECK_VERSION`, currently `0.11.0`) and resolved reproducibly: `scripts/lint.sh` downloads the pinned `koalaman/shellcheck` release tarball for the host OS/arch (`curl --retry 3 --retry-all-errors`) and **SHA256-verifies it fail-closed** (hard error on mismatch/absence вҖ” never runs an unverified binary) against a per-platform checksum table (linux.x86_64, linux.aarch64, darwin.x86_64, darwin.aarch64 вҖ” the CI matrix legs plus the common local-dev platforms). The pin is **end-to-end**: both the release tarball *and* the extracted binary (the artifact actually executed) carry pinned hashes, and the binary hash is re-checked on **every cache hit** вҖ” so a tampered, pre-seeded, or truncated cached binary is discarded and re-fetched rather than run (the "never runs an unverified binary" invariant holds on the warm path, not just the cold download; #549 review). The cache lives under a per-user root (`$RUNNER_TEMP` in CI, else `$XDG_CACHE_HOME`/`$HOME/.cache`) вҖ” never a predictable world-writable `/tmp` path a co-tenant could pre-seed. The floor is `вүҘ0.10.0` (first release shipping a `darwin.aarch64` asset вҖ” `macos-latest` runners are arm64). In CI the download is wrapped in `actions/cache` keyed on version+os+arch so a green run does not re-fetch from the release CDN on every run (CDN flake would otherwise be red-CI-that-is-not-a-code-defect вҖ” the non-reproducible signal this section exists to kill). **Memory guard** (the pre-#539 combined `shellcheck "${files[@]}"` run peaked ~18 GB RSS on the 13.7k-line `scripts/test/smoke.sh` and OOM-killed the ubuntu runner as an illegible "runner received a shutdown signal"): shellcheck is invoked **per file** (bounds peak RSS at the single largest file вҖ” `external-sources=false` in `.shellcheckrc` means no cross-file analysis is lost), and on Linux the per-file pass is measured under `/usr/bin/time -v` and peak RSS is checked against a documented fraction of runner memory вҖ” a **non-fatal flag** that surfaces an approaching-limit regression legibly (a single file creeping toward the cliff) *without ever failing CI*: the legitimate per-file baseline (~12 GB, dominated by `scripts/test/smoke.sh`) sits close to any runner-safe budget, so a hard exit would risk the exact false-red this section exists to kill. The combined-pass regression is instead gated by the smoke structural lock (В§11.1-adjacent, `scripts/test/smoke.sh` В§138) вҖ” and would OOM the runner before `/usr/bin/time` could report anyway. A hard `ulimit -v` address-space cap is likewise *not* used вҖ” it caps virtual address space, not RSS, so it false-reds legitimate runs.
- **smoke** вҖ” installs `jq` (apt-get on Linux; pre-installed on macOS) and runs `./scripts/test/smoke.sh`.
- **mutation** вҖ” runs `./scripts/test/mutation.sh`, the enforcement-matcher kill-rate guard (В§11.1).

`fail-fast: false` on the matrix so per-platform failures surface independently.

### 11.1 Enforcement-matcher mutation harness

The smoke suite asserts that the enforcement matchers *behave* correctly; it does not, on its own, prove those assertions actually **kill** a regression вҖ” a silently-weakened matcher could still pass a smoke assertion that no longer exercises the weakened path. `scripts/test/mutation.sh` closes that gap by measuring the smoke suite's **kill-rate** on the critical matchers (#423): it is the systematic, generalized form of the ad-hoc falsifiability premise-locks the suite already carries (the В§357 live-sink lock; the В§65i release-subject lock).

For each critical matcher the harness applies one **mutation** вҖ” a weakened redefinition *appended* to a throwaway **git-worktree copy** of the tree (append-override: bash takes the last definition, so no fragile in-body edit) вҖ” then runs the full smoke suite in that worktree (the worktree's smoke copy **self-locates** to it вҖ” В§3.2.1; the harness sets no shell-root env), and asserts smoke **fails** (exit вү  0 вҖ” the mutant is *killed*). A **surviving** mutant (smoke still green under a weakened guard) is reported as a harness failure: it means the matcher is no longer pinned by any assertion. The git worktree isolates the mutation from the parent working tree and is removed after each case, so the harness never mutates the live tree.

The seeded mutations (extensible) target the matchers whose wrong-*allow* cost is highest (В§6.0): `check_commit_subject` вҶ’ always-accept (commit-format), `scan_staged_secrets` вҶ’ always-clean (secret), `PROTECTED_BRANCH_PATTERN` вҶ’ never-match (protected-branch). Per В§6.0 this is the cost-asymmetry rationale made testable вҖ” the same matchers whose negative gate fails safe toward blocking are the ones whose test coverage most needs a kill-rate proof.

So `/ship`'s `gh pr checks` step has something concrete to watch for on PRs against this repo. Other repos that adopt the shell can copy the workflow as a starting point.

---

## 12. Operational decisions (locked)

| Item | Decision |
|------|----------|
| Workspace structure | Inside the shell repo's `workspace/` by default; external paths registerable via `scripts/register.sh` |
| Scope of application | Only inside `workspace/` (cwd guard). External paths via registered symlinks count the same. |
| User-global impact | None (`~/.claude` left alone) |
| Enforcement level | "Strong enforcement; escapable on conscious choice." No policy is set in stone. |
| Hosting | GitHub (gh CLI) |
| Fork usage | None (upstream-only) |
| Quickfix path | Partially absorbed via issue-#-optional types (`chore`/`style`/`build`/`ci`/`test`/`revert`). External surface changes still need an issue. |
| Phase order | Strict for `feat`/`docs`/contract changes. `fix`/`refactor`/`perf`/spike use the В§1.2 relaxations. |
| Test gate | `/ship` runs tests right before ready transition. Draft commit stage is fast lint/format only. |
| Amend policy | Local amend allowed; amend after push blocked. |
| CI watch | `/ship` runs background watch. |
| Subagent calls | `planner` + `code-reviewer` default; others trigger- or explicit-call. |
| Operating mode | Default `attended` (stop at PR-ready). `unattended` is opt-in via В§5.7.1's resolution priority and continues `/ship` to merge or park. |
| Merge strategy | `gh pr merge --merge --delete-branch` (no-ff merge commit). Preserves the Doc вҶ’ Test вҶ’ Code commit graph on `main` and anchors each PR with a merge commit. See В§5.7.1 "Merge mechanism". |

---

## 13. Failure modes and recovery

| Situation | Handling |
|-----------|----------|
| Issue body is ambiguous | `/work-on` refuses to start; asks the user to clarify the issue |
| Phase A reveals the spec was wrong | Strike through the checklist with reason, re-invoke planner |
| Phase B test passes accidentally | Two branches: (a) Phase A spec is weak or test inputs insufficient вҶ’ strengthen doc/test. (b) Adding a regression test for already-implemented behavior is legitimate вҶ’ note in one line in PR body and proceed. Don't always restart from doc. |
| Base (main or `--base` target) advances during work | `git pull --rebase origin <base>` вҶ’ resolve conflicts вҶ’ re-push PR. The base is whatever the PR's `baseRefName` is вҖ” read via `gh pr view --json baseRefName` if uncertain. Do NOT `git merge <base>` into the feature branch вҖ” the В§6.1 `backmerge` matcher blocks that motion specifically to keep feature branches rebase-clean (escape `SKIP_HOOKS=backmerge` exists for exceptional cases but should be rare). |
| Another contributor touches the same branch | `--ff-only pull`, escalate to user on conflict |
| Can't finish in one PR | Intermediate PRs use `Refs #N`, the final uses `Closes #N` |
| Issue acceptance criteria change mid-work | Update the issue body + comment with the change log; mirror in the PR body |
| CI fails while local passes | `/ship` blocks. CI logs first, then hotfix commit + re-push |
| Hook misfires | Use escape hatch + audit it + file a fix PR for the hook |
| Same escape category repeats in audit | Sign the hook is wrong вҖ” fix PR takes priority |

---

## 14. Security / sensitive items

- Direct editing of `.env`, `credentials.*`, `*.pem`, `id_rsa*`, etc. is blocked by hook.
- Pattern detection over staged diff for known secret formats (AWS, GitHub tokens, GitLab tokens, OpenAI/Anthropic keys, Slack tokens, password literals, etc.).
- Shell repo audit logs never contain secrets вҖ” the diff body is not written to the log.
- bootstrap checks `gh auth status`. Claude creates issues/PRs under the human's name, so commits include a `Co-Authored-By` trailer.

---

## 15. (removed)

Operating decisions are documented in their respective sections in the body. No duplicate index here.

---

## 16. Build order (recommended)

When starting from an empty directory:

1. Directory skeleton + `.gitignore`. The shell repo's `.gitignore`:
   ```gitignore
   workspace/*
   !workspace/.gitkeep
   !workspace/README.md
   .claude/audit/
   .claude/state/
   ```
   The `workspace/` directory itself is tracked via `.gitkeep`; clones and symlinks inside are ignored, except for the explanatory `workspace/README.md`. `.claude/audit/` is the legacy shared audit log; `.claude/state/` holds legacy shared caches + the back-compat registry floor. Post-#314/#316 the per-project audit, caches, and registry live under `ghjig-state/` (В§3.2.2), resolved via `ghjig_state_dir()` / `ghjig_registry_file`. `.claude/settings.local.json` exists only on the target side (as a symlink slot), so it's not in the shell repo's `.gitignore`.
2. `.claude/audit/` and `.claude/state/` empty dirs with `.gitkeep` вҖ” at runtime the legacy shared `audit.jsonl` (audit/) and registry floor (state/) land here; the per-project equivalents land under `ghjig-state/` (В§3.2.2).
3. `.claude/templates/*` first вҖ” every command and agent consumes these.
4. `.claude/CLAUDE.md` вҖ” shell norms (a summary of В§1, В§2 of this document).
5. `.claude/agents/*` (eleven of them).
6. `.claude/hooks/helpers/*` вҖ” the full set is enumerated canonically in В§8 (the count is drift-guarded by smoke В§103; do not re-list here). `git_matcher` must precede `branch_guard` вҖ” branch_guard sources it for the `PROTECTED_BRANCH_PATTERN` SSOT.
7. `.claude/hooks/{pre_tool_use, post_tool_use, stop, user_prompt_submit, session_start}.sh`.
8. `.claude/settings.json` вҖ” registers the hooks above.
9. `.claude/commands/*` вҖ” the full set is enumerated canonically in В§8 (count drift-guarded by smoke В§103; do not re-list here). The original core (onboard, file-issue, work-on, sync-pr, status, review, ship, adr, audit) came first; dir-mode / initiative / discussion / changelog / flush / bootstrap commands were layered on later.
10. `bin/ghjig` wrapper вҖ” including the auto-register prompt for unregistered external paths.
11. `scripts/bootstrap.sh`, `scripts/clone-into.sh`, `scripts/register.sh` (sharing inject logic via a helper).
12. `scripts/test/smoke.sh` вҖ” single-entry-point reproduction of the clone-into вҶ’ /onboard вҶ’ /file-issue вҶ’ /work-on вҶ’ D-T-C cycle вҶ’ /ship simulation (В§17's primary verification).
13. `docs/*`, `README.md`.
14. Run the smoke test once to confirm passing.
15. First-commit the shell repo on itself (bootstrap exception). All subsequent commits self-enforce the flow. **The same first-commit exception applies to target repos** via `/bootstrap-repo` (В§5.0): a brand-new target with no default branch (empty repo / unborn HEAD reporting `main`) cannot make its seed commit ride a flow that presupposes a prior commit, so stage-0 makes the seed commit through the scoped, audit-logged `branch` escape. Both cases are the same chicken-and-egg, and both keep the bypass visible in `audit.jsonl`.

---

## 17. Verification checklist (does it meet the spec?)

All of the following must be yes before operating.

- [ ] `ghjig` works inside `workspace/`; hooks pass transparently outside it.
- [ ] Direct commits/pushes to protected branches are blocked by hooks.
- [ ] Force push is blocked by hooks.
- [ ] Commits without Conventional Commits + issue # are blocked.
- [ ] Secret patterns in staged diffs are detected and blocked.
- [ ] `--amend` (after push) and `--no-verify` are blocked.
- [ ] Dangerous commands (`rm -rf` with out-of-registry args, `git reset --hard`, `git clean -f`) are blocked.
- [ ] Edit/Write whose target path is outside any registry entry is blocked.
- [ ] Edits to `.env`, `*.pem`, `credentials*` are blocked.
- [ ] Shell installation and operation leave no changes in user-global state like `~/.zshrc` (В§3.4).
- [ ] PostToolUse auto-formats changed files with the detected formatter.
- [ ] UserPromptSubmit injects a PR body + issue body + status summary into context.
- [ ] SessionStart warns when the shell repo is behind origin/main.
- [ ] `/onboard` checks fork status, push permission, MISSION presence, `.github/`, branch protection.
- [ ] `/file-issue`, `/work-on`, `/sync-pr`, `/status`, `/review`, `/ship`, `/adr`, `/audit` all behave as intended.
- [ ] The eleven subagents are defined; planner produces a Doc вҶ’ Test вҶ’ Code checklist.
- [ ] `.claude/templates/*` is the single source of truth for every command.
- [ ] The escape hatch works for every block category and is recorded in the audit log.
- [ ] The shell repo can develop itself on this same flow (dogfooding).
- [ ] `bootstrap.sh` self-registers the shell repo in its own per-project `.claude/ghjig-state/registry.txt` via `ghjig_registry_file "$SHELL_ROOT"` (idempotent вҖ” В§3.6, #316).
- [ ] `register.sh "$SHELL_ROOT"` skips the `workspace/` symlink-loop and skips `inject_into` while still registering the path and ensuring the committed `.claude/ghjig-root -> ..` self-symlink (idempotent вҖ” В§3.6, #539).
- [ ] The smoke scenario (clone-into вҶ’ /onboard вҶ’ /file-issue вҶ’ /work-on вҶ’ D-T-C cycle вҶ’ /ship simulation) is reproducible via a single call to `scripts/test/smoke.sh`.
- [ ] Shell assets that conflict by name with the target's existing `.claude/agents/<name>.md` or `.claude/commands/<name>.md` are not injected; only a warning is printed.
- [ ] Local amend passes; amend after push is blocked.
- [ ] `feat`/`docs` commits require issue #; `chore`/`style` etc. pass without it.
- [ ] Draft PR commit/push runs only fast lint/format; tests run when `/ship` runs them right before ready transition.
- [ ] Right before a PR body update, the remote body is refetched; conflicts with external edits abort the auto-update.
- [ ] Commit subjects pass the codepoint 1..72 range. A 72-codepoint Korean subject is not falsely truncated.
- [ ] `ghjig <path>` triggers the auto-register prompt when called with an unregistered external path.
- [ ] A monorepo subproject's own `.claude/` is left untouched by the shell.
- [ ] `shellcheck --severity=warning --shell=bash` is clean across all shell sources on both CI matrix legs (`ubuntu-latest`, `macos-latest`); `.shellcheckrc` records intentional silences and inline `# shellcheck disable=` carry per-line justifications (В§11).
- [ ] `gh pr merge` is blocked when a linked issue (`closingIssuesReferences`) has unchecked AC items and no `^## AC closeout` comment; `scripts/ac_closeout.sh <pr-num>` satisfies the gate idempotently and is invoked by `/ship` step 7.6 (В§6.1).

---

## 18. Release backbone

Locks the shape of how releases happen: per-PR fragment files, one consolidator skill (`/release`), and a templated CI gate. Adopters consume the substrate via `/onboard-dir-mode` (В§18.6). Established by Directive #128; depends on the VERSION + tag surface from Directive #122 (В§3.5).

### 18.1 Fragment contract

The release line consumes per-PR **changelog fragments** under `changelog_unreleased/<category>/<N>.md`:

- `<category>` вҲҲ {`added`, `changed`, `deprecated`, `removed`, `fixed`, `security`} вҖ” the six [Keep a Changelog](https://keepachangelog.com/en/1.1.0/) categories. Each is a subdirectory under `changelog_unreleased/`.
- `<N>` is the issue or PR number that introduces the fragment (positive integer; filename stem).
- The fragment body is a **single-line markdown bullet** (one line starting with `- `).
- The bullet **must contain `(#<N>)`** where `<N>` matches the filename stem. CI rejects mismatches (В§18.6).
- **No YAML frontmatter, no multi-paragraph prose, no nested headers inside the fragment.** The contract is intentionally minimal вҖ” the directory is the category, the filename is the PR/issue link, the bullet is the user-facing line.

`changelog_unreleased/TEMPLATE.md` documents the contract for fragment-authors in project-neutral language. The template ships in the shell and `/onboard-dir-mode` installs it (along with the six empty category subdirectories) into adopting repos.

`/release X.Y.Z` (В§5.20) consolidates all present fragments into a new `## [X.Y.Z] вҖ” YYYY-MM-DD` section in `CHANGELOG.md` at repo root, grouped under Keep-a-Changelog category subheadings, and deletes the consumed fragments in the same commit.

### 18.2 Version of record

The canonical version-of-record is the top-level `VERSION` file (locked by Directive #122 / В§3.5). `/release X.Y.Z`:

- Validates `X.Y.Z` is semver 0.x (`MAJOR=0`).
- Strips any `-dev` suffix from `VERSION`.
- Writes `X.Y.Z` to `VERSION`.
- Falls back to `git describe --tags` for **resolution-time queries only** вҖ” never for write-back. The file is authoritative on `main`.

Multi-file version-of-record (`package.json`, `Cargo.toml`, `pyproject.toml`) is deferred. A documented extension point вҖ” `.claude/release-config.json` вҖ” is **reserved** at this location for projects whose VoR lives elsewhere; the file is currently unimplemented and the reservation prevents the name from being claimed by something else.

**Manifest-match preflight** (verify, not write-back; #469, Directive #468): while multi-file VoR *write-back* is deferred, `/release` runs a **verification-only** preflight вҖ” it resolves the detected stack's version field via `detect_version` (В§6.6) and **refuses** (non-zero, naming both the manifest version and the `X.Y.Z` being cut, with the fix: bump the manifest) when they contradict, so a release cannot tag a version the project's own manifest does not reflect. This is the **confident-mismatch** arm only; an unknown stack / absent or unparseable field is the **uncertain** arm and degrades to a graceful skip with a note (never a false block вҖ” the diverse-project posture, В§6.0 cost-asymmetry). The manifest is **read, never written** вҖ” write-back remains `VERSION`-only. Stack-aware bump *automation* is an explicit deferred non-goal (Directive #468).

### 18.3 Trunk branch model

Default development line is `main`. `/release` operates on `main` unless `--base <branch>` targets a maintenance branch (e.g., `0.3-maintenance`). Maintenance branches are **not auto-created by the shell** вҖ” adopters who need LTS lines create them manually. See В§10.5 for the topic-branch / alternate-base flow.

The CI fragment-gate (В§18.6) targets `main` and `*-maintenance` by default; configurable per project at workflow-install time.

### 18.4 Tag format

Tags follow `v` + semver 0.x вҖ” `v0.1.0`, `v0.2.0`, etc. Locked by Directive #122 (CLOSED); preserved verbatim here so downstream tooling reads one canonical clause. Tag-freshness is **not** enforced as a merge gate per #122's non-goal вҖ” tag-state drift is drift, not breakage. `/release` creates the tag (`gh release create vX.Y.Z --target <merge-sha>`) at the release-PR merge boundary; pre-merge release-PRs are tagless.

### 18.5 Non-goals

Locked by Directive #128 (closed):

- **No `/prepare-release` skill.** VERSION's `-dev` suffix replaces the scope-locking ceremony of a prepare PR.
- **No `/changelog-check` *lint* skill.** CI workflow + optional local hook arm cover the *validation* surface; a manual re-validation skill is a third redundant surface. This forbids a skill that **re-checks** an existing fragment's shape вҖ” it does **not** forbid an **authoring** affordance: `/changelog` (В§5.23) *writes* a fragment or applies the `skip-changelog` label and delegates all validation to the CI gate (В§18.6), and the `/ship` pre-ready arm (В§5.7, step 7.7) is exactly the "optional local hook arm" sanctioned in this clause. Authoring the artifact plus one in-flow presence check of the single contract is permitted; re-validating that contract a second time is not.
- **No tag-push merge gate, no tag-freshness enforcement** (preserves Directive #122's explicit non-goal).
- **No automated maintenance-branch creation, no backport / port-PR flow.** Deferred to a successor Directive when at least one adopter requests LTS.
- **No release-please / external-service integration.** The shell ships a ~30-line CI script under shell control. Adopters who already use release-please keep it; the shell does not displace it but also does not configure it.
- **No automated distribution** (npm, PyPI, Docker, Homebrew, binary upload). Per-project extension surface.
- **No release cadence enforcement.** When to cut a release is a human / per-project call.
- **No breaking-change policy enforcement.** Shell stays at `0.x` per #122 (`MAJOR=0` invariant); downstream projects at `1.x+` define their own compat policy.
- **No multi-file version-of-record bump.** `VERSION` is canonical; `.claude/release-config.json` is reserved but currently unimplemented.
- **No fragment frontmatter or template enforcement beyond filename/PR-number consistency.**
- **No major-rollover archive logic.** Shell stays at `0.x` per #122; revisit when `1.0.0` is on the table.
- **No retroactive per-milestone CHANGELOG entries** for pre-`v0.1.0` history. The inaugural section covers `init..v0.1.0` as one block, not split per historical sub-milestone.

### 18.6 Cross-project surface

`/onboard-dir-mode` installs the release-backbone substrate into adopting target repos as part of its tier-3 PR:

- `.github/workflows/check-changelog.yml` вҖ” the per-PR fragment-gate workflow.
- `changelog_unreleased/TEMPLATE.md` + the six empty category subdirectories with `.gitkeep` placeholders.

The workflow validates the following rules on every PR targeting a protected branch (`main` and `*-maintenance` by default). Rule 1 is a presence check; rules 2вҖ“4 are applied to **every** added fragment, and if **any** added fragment fails the gate fails вҖ” a single valid fragment does **not** mask a malformed sibling (the all-valid contract, matching `scripts/release_consolidate.sh`):

1. The PR diff adds at least one file under `changelog_unreleased/<category>/<N>.md` where `<category>` is one of the six Keep-a-Changelog subdirectories.
2. The filename stem `<N>` is a positive integer.
3. The file contains `(#<N>)` where `<N>` matches the filename stem.
4. The bullet begins with `- ` (the single-line markdown bullet form, per `changelog_unreleased/TEMPLATE.md`).

Failure (no fragment, malformed filename, mismatched PR ref, or a non-bullet line) blocks the PR with an error referencing this section. Rules 2вҖ“4 mirror `release_consolidate.sh`'s fragment validation so the per-PR gate and the release-time validator enforce one contract rather than diverging.

**`skip-changelog` opt-out**: a PR labeled `skip-changelog` bypasses the fragment check. The label is auditable on the PR; the workflow logs its application. Intended for PRs with no observable end-user behavior change вҖ” pure docs-fix typos, dependency-only chores, internal refactors. **PRs carrying the label produce no fragment and are not represented in the eventual CHANGELOG section** вҖ” by design, since there is nothing for a user to read about. Workflow trigger events include `labeled` and `unlabeled` so the opt-out re-runs the check.

Adopters consume the backbone with zero in-repo configuration beyond the substrate install plus their own `VERSION` file and a `CHANGELOG.md` at repo root. `/release X.Y.Z` runs against any repo where these three artifacts are present.

**Workflow does not self-trigger on its own landing PR**: per [GitHub's `pull_request` security policy](https://docs.github.com/en/actions/using-workflows/triggering-a-workflow#using-event-types), workflows modified inside a PR do **not** run on that PR (otherwise a fork could exfiltrate secrets via a self-modified workflow). The first PR after `check-changelog.yml` lands on `main` is the first empirical observation of the fragment-gate; the landing PR itself only validates the workflow's structure via smoke В§66c-e + the `code-reviewer` walk-through. Adopters running `/onboard-dir-mode` see the same: the substrate-install PR opens the workflow but the workflow fires from the next PR onward.

### 18.7 Skip criterion (the `skip-changelog` decision)

Every PR satisfies the fragment gate (В§18.6) one of two ways: it **adds a fragment**, or it carries the **`skip-changelog`** label. Which one applies is a content judgment, and this clause is its SSOT вҖ” `changelog_unreleased/TEMPLATE.md`, the `/changelog` skill (В§5.23), and the `/ship` pre-ready arm (В§5.7) reference this criterion rather than restate it:

- **Fragment required** when the PR changes user- or adopter-observable surface: a behaviour/contract change, a CLI/API/schema/protocol change, a SPEC contract change, or anything that alters how someone uses or integrates the project.
- **`skip-changelog` eligible** when the PR has no such surface: an internal `refactor` with unchanged external behaviour, `test`-only, `chore`/`build`/`ci`, `style`, or a docs-internal edit that changes no contract.

When in doubt, write the fragment вҖ” a redundant one-line entry is cheaper than a silently missing one. This criterion governs the *decision* only; the *shape* of any fragment written is validated solely by В§18.6, and neither the skill nor the `/ship` arm re-validates shape (В§18.5).

## 19. Closing
